Hila for Fidyat al-Salat for the Deceased
Complete hila for paying fidya for missed prayers on behalf of a deceased person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi legal device (hila) for fulfilling fidya for missed prayers of a deceased person, including the process of gathering poor recipients and the gift-back mechanism.

Core Idea
Fidya for missed prayers via hila: give to ten poor, gift back, repeat.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a complete hila shar'iyya for fulfilling a bequest of fidyat al-salat for a deceased person who had missed prayers. The hila ensures that the compensation is validly completed by a process of giving to ten poor individuals, having them gift the money back, and repeating until all missed prayers are covered. This lesson walks through the steps and conditions of this hila.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basis: the bequest for fidya from one-third of wealth
The fidya is to be paid from one-third of the deceased's estate if he bequeathed it. If no wealth, the heirs may borrow.
The bequest is executed only if the deceased made a wasiyyah.
2
Understand the fidya amount: half sa' per prayer/fast
Each missed fard prayer, witr, and day of fast requires half a sa' of wheat (approx. 2.5 kg or specific measure).
The sa' is 8 ratls; mann is 2 ratls.
3
Grasp the number of poor persons required: ten per round
The heir gathers ten poor persons who are not rich, not slaves, not minors, and not insane. Each round covers ten years of missed prayers (or one year per poor person? Actually each poor covers one year).
The ten are required to avoid giving to a single poor repeatedly?
4
Follow the transfer mechanism: give, accept, gift back
The heir gives the fidya amount to a poor person as ownership, the poor person accepts, then gifts it back to the heir. This is repeated for each of the ten poor.
This ensures the poor actually own the money before it returns.
5
Apply the calculation: age of deceased minus puberty years
The total missed prayers are calculated from the age of puberty (12 for males, 9 for females) to death. Multiply by 5 daily prayers + witr + any missed fasts.
The fidya amount is 4072 dirhams per year? The text mentions 4000+ dirhams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا مات الرجل وعليه صلوات فائتة وأوصى بأن يعطى كفارة صلاته يعطى لكل صلاة نصف صاع من بر، وللوتر نصف صاع، ولصوم يوم. نصف صاع وإنما يعطى من ثلث ماله، وإن لم يترك مالاً تستقرض ورثته نصف صاع ويدفع إلى المسكين ثم يتصدق المسكين على بعض ورثته ثم يتصدق ثم وثم حتى يتم لكل صلاة ما ذكرنا ولو قضاها ورثته بأمره لا يجوز وفي الحج يجوز اهـ. وفي الظهيرية اتفق المشايخ على تنفيذ هذه الوصية من ثلث ماله واختلفوا هل يقوم الإطعام مقام الصلاة ؛ قال محمد بن مقاتل ومحمد بن سملة : يقوم. وقال البلخي لا يقوم. ولا رواية في سجدة التلاوة أنه يجب أولاً . ولو أعطى فقيراً واحداً جملة جاز بخلاف كفارة اليمين، ولو أعطى عن صبي هبتهم وعشرين وأربعة وخمسون يوماً وثلث يوم وثلث عشر يوم، فبقي أن تحسب فدية الصلاة بالنسبة الشمسية أخذاً بالاحتياط من غير اعتبار ربع اليوم ومعلوم أن فدية كل فرض من الحنطة خمسمائة درهم وعشرون درهماً وللوتر كذلك، فتكون فدية صلاة كل يوم وليلة من الحنطة ثلاثة آلاف . ومائة درهم درهماً، وفدية كل سنة شمسية مائة واثنان وأربعون كيلاً بكيل قسطنطينية وسبع أوقية، فحينئذ يجمع الوارث عشرة رجال ليس فيهم غني لقوله تعالى إنما الصدقات للفقراء والمساكين﴾ [التوبة : ٦٠] الآية ولا عبد ولا ولا مجنون لأن لا تصح ، ثم يحسب سن الميت فيطرح . منه اثنتا عشرة سنة لمدة بلوغه إن كان الميت ذكراً، وتسع سنين إن كانت أنثى، لأن أقل مدة بلوغ الرجل اثنتا عشرة سنة، ومدة بلوغ المرأة تسع سنين . ثم يأخذ الوارث من مال اليتيم وجوباً إن أوصى واستحباباً إن لم ، أربعة آلاف درهم واثنين وسبعين درهماً أو شيئاً قيمته ذلك، أو يأخذ الأجنبي من مال نفسه تبرعاً مقدار ما ذكر . فيدور المسقط بنفسه - وارثاً كان أو غير وارث - أو يوكل غيره فيقول المسقط أو وكيله الواحد من الفقراء هكذا فلان بن فلان ويذكر اسمه واسم أبيه فاتته صلوات سنة هذه فديتها ماله نملكك إياها ويعلم أن المال المدفوع إليه صار ملكاً له، ثم يقول الفقير هكذا وأنا قبلتها وتملكتها منك فيدفع المعطي ويسلم إليه فيقبض المعطي فحينئذ تصير فدية صلاة سنة كاملة مؤداة ثم يفعل مع فقير آخر هكذا إلى أن تتم العشرة فحينئذ تصير فدية عشر سنين مؤداة في دور واحد، ثم يفعل هكذا مرة أخرى ثم وثم إلى أن تتم فدية فوائته بحسب الحساب، فإذا تمت فدية فوائته من الصلاة يقول المعطي لفقير واحد من تلك العشرة هكذا فلان بن فلان ملكك سائر ما وجب عليه من ماله إن كان الميت ذكراً، وإن كان أنثى يقول فلانة ملكتك جميع ما وجب عليها في مالها. ويفعل مع كل فقير كذلك فيعترفون كلهم بالقبول ثم يهبونه المال فيأخذه صاحبه وارثاً كان أو غير وارث ثم يتصدق على الفقراء العشرة ما شاء من الدراهم، ولا يجب تقسيم المال المذكور جميعاً على الفقراء وهذه حيلة شرعية والله تعالى أعلم ا هـ . قوله : (تسعة أمناء جمع من وهو رطلان، والصاع ثمانية أرطال من فالمن ربع الصاع .
If a man dies and he has missed prayers and bequeathed that expiation be given for his prayers, he is given for each prayer half a sa' of wheat, and for witr half a sa', and for a day's fast half a sa'. It is given from one third of his wealth. If he leaves no wealth, his heirs borrow half a sa' and give it to a poor person, then the poor person gives charity to some of his heirs, then gives charity, and so on until for each prayer what we mentioned is completed. If his heirs make up the prayers by his order, it is not valid; but in Hajj it is valid. In Al-Zahiriyyah: the scholars agreed on executing this bequest from one third of his wealth, but differed whether feeding substitutes for prayer. Muhammad ibn Muqatil and Muhammad ibn Salama said it does substitute. Al-Balkhi said it does not. No narration regarding prostration of recitation that it is obligatory first. If he gives to one poor person in a lump sum, it is permissible, unlike the expiation of an oath. And if he gives on behalf of... [calculation details]. Then the heir gathers ten men among whom there is no rich person, because of the verse 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and needy' [9:60], nor a slave, nor a minor, nor a madman because it is not valid. Then he calculates the age of the deceased, subtracts twelve years for the duration of his adulthood if the deceased was male, and nine years if female, because the minimum age of adulthood for a man is twelve years, and for a woman nine years. Then the heir takes from the orphan's wealth necessarily if he bequeathed, and voluntarily if not, four thousand and seventy-two dirhams or something of that value, or the stranger takes from his own wealth voluntarily the aforementioned amount. Then the remover (musqit) does the process by himself — whether heir or not — or appoints an agent, he says to one of the poor: 'So-and-so son of so-and-so, missed prayers of this year, their fidya is this wealth, we make you its owner,' and he knows that the money given to him becomes his property. Then the poor person says: 'I accept it and own it from you.' Then the giver gives and hands it over, the receiver takes it. Then the fidya of one full year is rendered. Then he does the same with another poor person until ten are completed, then the fidya of ten years is rendered in one round. Then he does this again and again until the fidya of all his missed prayers is completed according to calculation. When the fidya of his prayers is complete, the giver says to one poor person from those ten: 'So-and-so, I give you ownership of the rest of what is obligatory upon him from his wealth' (if deceased male) or 'her wealth' (if female). He does likewise with each poor person, and they all acknowledge acceptance, then they donate the money to him, and he takes it, whether heir or not. Then he gives charity to the ten poor whatever he wishes of dirhams. Dividing all the mentioned money among the poor is not obligatory. This is a legal trick. And Allah knows best. And his saying: 'Nine amnad' (plural of mann) which is two ratls, and the sa' is eight ratls, so the mann is one quarter of a sa'.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a complete hila (legal trick) for paying fidya (compensation) for missed prayers of a deceased person using a mechanism involving multiple poor recipients and a gift-back process. The fidya is half a sa' of wheat per missed fard prayer, same for witr and per fast day. The money comes from one third of the estate if bequeathed, otherwise heirs may borrow. The scholars of Al-Zahiriyyah agree on executing this bequest but differ on whether feeding (fidya) actually substitutes for prayer — some say yes, others no. The trick then details a method using ten poor men (to avoid the prohibition of giving to a single poor multiple times? Actually to handle multiple years). The age of the deceased is calculated, subtracting the years before puberty (12 for males, 9 for females). The money (4072 dirhams) is calculated for the fidya of missed prayers over the adult years. The trick involves giving the money to a poor person as ownership, then the poor person gives it back as a gift, and then the heir can do as he wishes. The goal is to fulfill the bequest in a Sharia-compliant way by ensuring the poor person actually owns the money before returning it. The passage ends with a note on weights: one mann is two ratls, one sa' is eight ratls, so one mann is quarter of a sa'.

Key Terms
حيلة شرعية (hila shar'iyya): A legal device that achieves a permissible outcome while complying with Sharia rules.
فدية الصلاة (fidyat al-salat): Monetary compensation for missed prayers, typically half a sa' of grain per prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Fidya for missed prayers on behalf of a deceased is valid in the Hanafi school through a hila that involves multiple poor persons and a gift-back mechanism, fulfilling the bequest from one-third of the estate.

12 min
Fidyah for Missed Prayers and the Legal Trick (Hila)
Ruling on fidyah for missed prayers and a complex hila for payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for missed prayers after death and describe the legal trick (hila) used to fulfill it, including its conditions and the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Fidyah for missed prayers is a bequest from one-third; the legal trick (hila) using ten poor persons is a valid Hanafi device.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a practical problem: how to compensate for missed prayers after death. It presents a complex legal trick (hila) that allows the heir to fulfill the bequest while ensuring the wealth returns. Understanding this hila requires careful attention to its conditions and the underlying ikhtilaf among Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on fidyah
Determine the amount and source of fidyah for missed prayers: half a sa' of wheat per prayer or fast, given from one-third of the deceased's wealth if bequeathed.
If no bequest, it is not obligatory.
2
Understand the hila mechanics
Follow the cycle: the heir gives wealth to ten poor persons, who then gift it back, and the heir gives charity to them. This repeats until all fidyah is paid.
The hila ensures the fidyah is considered paid while the wealth stays with the family.
3
Note the conditions and participants
The poor must be free, sane, and not rich. The deceased's adult years are calculated (subtract 12 for males, 9 for females). The number of rounds depends on years missed.
The hila uses a known formula for calculating the total amount.
4
Recognize the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Scholars differed on whether feeding substitutes for the prayer itself (Muhammad ibn Muqatil vs. al-Balkhi) and whether the hila can cover all five daily prayers (Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf vs. Abu al-Qasim).
The preferred position is that the hila is valid, but the substitution debate remains.

Source Text

باب قضاء الفوائت . وهي واقعة محمد بن الحسن سألها أبا حنيفة فأجابه بما ذكرنا فأعاد العشاء. إذا فاتت صلاة عن وقتها ينبغي أن يقضيها في بيته ولا يقضيها في المسجد إذا مات الرجل وعليه صلوات فائتة وأوصى بأن يعطى كفارة صلاته يعطى لكل صلاة نصف صاع من بر، وللوتر نصف صاع، ولصوم يوم. نصف صاع وإنما يعطى من ثلث ماله، وإن لم يترك مالاً تستقرض ورثته نصف صاع ويدفع إلى المسكين ثم يتصدق المسكين على بعض ورثته ثم يتصدق ثم وثم حتى يتم لكل صلاة ما ذكرنا ولو قضاها ورثته بأمره لا يجوز وفي الحج يجوز اهـ. وفي الظهيرية اتفق المشايخ على تنفيذ هذه الوصية من ثلث ماله واختلفوا هل يقوم الإطعام مقام الصلاة ؛ قال محمد بن مقاتل ومحمد بن سملة : يقوم. وقال البلخي لا يقوم. ولا رواية في سجدة التلاوة أنه يجب أولاً . ولو أعطى فقيراً واحداً جملة جاز بخلاف كفارة اليمين، ولو أعطى عن يوص، صبي هبتهم وعشرين وأربعة وخمسون يوماً وثلث يوم وثلث عشر يوم، فبقي أن تحسب فدية الصلاة بالنسبة الشمسية أخذاً بالاحتياط من غير اعتبار ربع اليوم ومعلوم أن فدية كل فرض من الحنطة خمسمائة درهم وعشرون درهماً وللوتر كذلك، فتكون فدية صلاة كل يوم وليلة من الحنطة ثلاثة آلاف . ومائة درهم درهماً، وفدية كل سنة شمسية مائة واثنان وأربعون كيلاً بكيل قسطنطينية وسبع أوقية، فحينئذ يجمع الوارث عشرة رجال ليس فيهم غني لقوله تعالى إنما الصدقات للفقراء والمساكين﴾ [التوبة : ٦٠] الآية ولا عبد ولا ولا مجنون لأن لا تصح ، ثم يحسب سن الميت فيطرح . منه اثنتا عشرة سنة لمدة بلوغه إن كان الميت ذكراً، وتسع سنين إن كانت أنثى، لأن أقل مدة بلوغ الرجل اثنتا عشرة سنة، ومدة بلوغ المرأة تسع سنين . ثم يأخذ الوارث من مال اليتيم وجوباً إن أوصى واستحباباً إن لم ، أربعة آلاف درهم واثنين وسبعين درهماً أو شيئاً قيمته ذلك، أو يأخذ الأجنبي من مال نفسه تبرعاً مقدار ما ذكر . فيدور المسقط بنفسه - وارثاً كان أو غير وارث - أو يوكل غيره فيقول المسقط أو وكيله الواحد من الفقراء هكذا فلان بن فلان ويذكر اسمه واسم أبيه فاتته صلوات سنة هذه فديتها ماله نملكك إياها ويعلم أن المال المدفوع إليه صار ملكاً له، ثم يقول الفقير هكذا وأنا قبلتها وتملكتها منك فيدفع المعطي ويسلم إليه فيقبض المعطي فحينئذ تصير فدية صلاة سنة كاملة مؤداة ثم يفعل مع فقير آخر هكذا إلى أن تتم العشرة فحينئذ تصير فدية عشر سنين مؤداة في دور واحد، ثم يفعل هكذا مرة أخرى ثم وثم إلى أن تتم فدية فوائته بحسب الحساب، فإذا تمت فدية فوائته من الصلاة يقول المعطي لفقير واحد من تلك العشرة هكذا فلان بن فلان ملكك سائر ما وجب عليه من ماله إن كان الميت ذكراً، وإن كان أنثى يقول فلانة ملكتك جميع ما وجب عليها في مالها. ويفعل مع كل فقير كذلك فيعترفون كلهم بالقبول ثم يهبونه المال فيأخذه صاحبه وارثاً كان أو غير وارث ثم يتصدق على الفقراء العشرة ما شاء من الدراهم، ولا يجب تقسيم المال المذكور جميعاً على الفقراء وهذه حيلة شرعية والله تعالى أعلم ا هـ . قوله : (تسعة أمناء جمع من وهو رطلان، والصاع ثمانية أرطال من فالمن ربع الصاع .
خمس صلوات تسعة أمناء فقيراً ومناً فقيراً آخر قال أبو بكر الإسكاف : يجوز ذلك كله. وقال أبو القاسم : وهو اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث يجوز عن أربع صلوات دون الخامسة لأنه متفرق، ولا يجوز أن يعطى كل مسكين أقل من نصف صاع في كفارة اليمين فكذلك هذا. فالحاصل أن كفارة الصلاة تفارق كفارة اليمين في حق أنه لا يشترط فيها العدد وتوافقها من حيث إنه لو أدى أقل من نصف صاع إلى فقير واحد لا يجوز اهـ. والله أعلم.
Chapter of Making Up Missed Prayers. This is an incident of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan who asked Abu Hanifa and he answered as we mentioned, so he repeated Isha. When a prayer is missed after its time, one should make it up at home and not in the mosque. When a man dies and has missed prayers and bequeaths that expiation for his prayers be given, he is given for each prayer half a sa' of wheat, and for witr half a sa', and for a fast of a day half a sa'. And it is given from one-third of his wealth. If he left no wealth, his heirs borrow half a sa' and give to the poor person, then the poor person gives charity to some of his heirs, then gives charity again and again until for each prayer what we mentioned is completed. If his heirs made it up by his order, it is not permissible, but in Hajj it is permissible. End. In al-Zahiriyya, the scholars agreed on executing this bequest from one-third of his wealth, but they differed whether feeding stands in place of prayer: Muhammad ibn Muqatil and Muhammad ibn Samala said it stands; al-Balkhi said it does not stand. There is no narration about prostration of recitation that it is obligatory first. And if he gave to one poor person in bulk, it is permissible contrary to the expiation of an oath. And if he gave for...[unclear]. The fidyah of prayer is calculated according to the solar year, taking precaution without considering a quarter of a day. It is known that the fidyah of every obligatory prayer is five hundred and twenty dirhams of wheat, and for witr likewise. So the fidyah of prayer for every day and night is three thousand one hundred dirhams of wheat, and the fidyah of every solar year is one hundred and forty-two qeels by the qeel of Constantinople and seven uqiyas. Then the heir gathers ten men among whom there is no rich person, due to the verse 'Indeed the charities are for the poor and the needy' (9:60), and no slave nor... nor insane because it is not valid. Then he calculates the age of the deceased and subtracts twelve years for the duration of his majority if the deceased was male, and nine years if female, because the minimum age of majority for a man is twelve years and for a woman nine years. Then the heir takes from the orphan's wealth obligatorily if he bequeathed, and commendably if not, four thousand and seventy-two dirhams or something of that value, or a stranger takes from his own wealth voluntarily the mentioned amount. Then the person executing the transfer himself, whether heir or not, or his agent, says to one of the poor: 'O so-and-so son of so-and-so (mentioning his name and his father's name), missed prayers of a year, their fidyah is this wealth, we make you own it,' and he knows that the wealth paid to him becomes his property. Then the poor person says: 'I accept it and take ownership from you.' Then the giver hands over and gives to him, and the receiver receives. Then the fidyah of a full year's prayers becomes paid. Then he does similarly with another poor person until the ten are completed. Then the fidyah of ten years becomes paid in one round. Then he does similarly again and again until the fidyah of his missed prayers is completed according to calculation. When the fidyah of his missed prayers from prayer is completed, the giver says to one poor person from those ten: 'O so-and-so, I give you ownership of all that was due upon him from his wealth if the deceased was male,' and if female, he says: 'O so-and-so, I give you ownership of all that was due upon her from her wealth.' He does similarly with every poor person, and they all acknowledge acceptance. Then they gift the wealth to him, and the owner takes it, whether heir or not. Then he gives charity to the ten poor whatever he wishes of dirhams. It is not obligatory to distribute all the mentioned wealth to the poor. This is a legal trick. And Allah Almighty knows best. End. His statement: (nine mann: the mann is two ratls, and a sa' is eight ratls, so the mann is a quarter of a sa'.) Five prayers: nine mann for a poor person and a mann for another poor person. Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf said: all that is permissible. Abu al-Qasim said, and it is the choice of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth: it is permissible for four prayers but not for the fifth because it is disjoined. It is not permissible to give each poor person less than half a sa' in the expiation of an oath, and likewise this. The conclusion is that the expiation of prayer differs from the expiation of an oath in that the number of poor is not required in it, and it agrees in that if one pays less than half a sa' to one poor person, it is not permissible. End. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a ruling and a detailed legal trick (hila) for the expiation (fidyah) of missed prayers after a person's death. The passage begins by stating that if a person dies with a bequest to give expiation for his missed prayers, the expiation is given from one-third of his wealth: for each missed obligatory prayer or witr, half a sa' of wheat, and for each missed fast day, also half a sa'. If he left no wealth, the heirs borrow and arrange a cycle of charity and gift to fulfill the expiation. The author then notes that the scholars agreed on executing this bequest from the third, but differed on whether the feeding actually substitutes for the prayer itself (an issue of legal efficacy). The core of the passage is the elaborate hila: the heir gathers ten poor persons, calculates the number of missed prayers based on the deceased's adult years (subtracting 12 for males, 9 for females), and then through a series of gifts and returns (tamlik, then hiba, then sadaqa), the fidyah is considered paid. The hila ensures that the wealth effectively returns to the heir while the poor benefit from charity. The passage also clarifies differences between kaffara of prayer and kaffara of oath: in prayer kaffara, giving a lump sum to one poor person is permissible, but giving less than half a sa' per person is not. The text reflects later Hanafi fatwa literature (mutakhkhirin) and includes ikhtilaf among Hanafi authorities like Muhammad ibn Muqatil, al-Balkhi, Abu Bakr al-Iskaaf, and Abu al-Qasim (likely al-Hakim al-Shahid).

Key Terms
كفارة الصلاة (kaffarat al-salah): Expiation for missed prayers after death, consisting of giving half a sa' of wheat per prayer.
حيلة شرعية (hilah shar'iyyah): A permissible legal maneuver to achieve a desired outcome by using lawful means; here, a cycle of gift and return to fulfill fidyah.
فدية (fidyah): Compensation payment for missed religious obligations, here for missed prayers and fasts.
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume equal to 8 ratls (approx. 2.5-3 kg). Used for fidyah and kaffarah.
تمليك (tamlik): Giving ownership; the act of making the poor person owner of the fidyah amount.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hila described, how many poor persons must be gathered in one round to pay fidyah for ten years of missed prayers?
A) Five
B) Ten
C) Two
D) One per year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a legal trick (hila) to fulfill the bequest of fidyah for missed prayers, using ten poor persons and a cycle of gift and return, provided all conditions are met.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sajd al-Sahw: Compensator Only for Forgetful Omissions
Introduces sajd al-sahw and its limitation to forgetful omissions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of sajd al-sahw, distinguish between forgetful and intentional omissions, and apply the rule that intentional omissions require i'adah.

Core Idea
Sajd al-sahw compensates forgetful deficiencies but not intentional transgressions.

This passage opens the chapter on sajd al-sahw. It defines the act, clarifies its scope (all prayers), and establishes a crucial boundary: sajd al-sahw is a jābir (compensator) only for forgetful (sahw) mistakes, not for intentional omissions of a wajib. The reasoning is that intentional omission is a graver deficiency that cannot be remedied by a lesser act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its compensator function
The passage introduces sajd al-sahw as a jābir al-nuqṣān (compensator for deficiency). Understand that it applies to any prayer, not just obligatory ones.
The compensator is specifically for forgetful deficiencies, not all deficiencies.
2
Distinguish forgetful and intentional omissions
The passage contrasts forgetful (sahw) and intentional ('amd) omission of a wajib. Only forgetful omissions can be compensated by sujud.
The term 'sahw' is defined as absence of recollection at the time of need, while nisyan is departure after having known.
3
Understand the aqli proof
Intentional omission is a greater deficiency than forgetful omission. Since sajd al-sahw is legislated as an equivalent (mithl) for forgetful omission, it cannot compensate a greater deficiency—a thing cannot be compensated by something lower.
This reasoning is quoted from al-Walwalji's Fatawa and supported by the majority.
4
Apply the ruling
Conclude: if a wajib is left intentionally, i'adah (repetition) of the prayer is required, not sujud al-sahw. This applies uniformly to all wajibat in prayer.
No distinction is made between different wajibat; the rule is absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو . لما فرغ من ذكر الأداء والقضاء شرع في بيان ما يكون جابر النقصان يقع فيهما. كذا في العناية. والأولى أن يقال : لما فرغ من ذكر الصلاة نفلها وفرضها أداء وقضاء شرع فيما يكون جابراً لنقصان يقع فيها فإن سجود السهو في مطلق الصلاة ولا يختص بالفرائض . وهذه الإضافة من باب إضافة الحكم إلى السبب وهي الأصل في الإضافات لأن الإضافة للاختصاص وأقوى وجوه الاختصاص اختصاص المسبب بالسبب. وذكر في التحرير أنه لا اللغة فرق في بين النسيان والسهو وهو عدم الاستحضار في وقت الحاجة. وفرق بينهما في السراج الوهاج بأن النسيان عزوب الشيء عن النفس بعد حضوره، والسهو قد يكون عما كان الإنسان عالماً به وعما لا يكون عالماً به وظاهر كلام الجم الغفير أنه لا يجب السجود في العمد وإنما تجب الإعادة إذا ترك واجباً عمداً جبراً لنقصانه . وذكر الولوالجي في فتاواه أن الواجب إذا تركه عمداً لا ينجبر بسجدتي السهو لأنهما عرفتا جابرتين بالشرع والشرع ورد حالة السهو وجعلهما مثلاً لهذا الفائت لا ،فوقه لأن الشيء لا يجبر بما فوقه والنقصان المتمكن بترك الواجب عامداً فوق النقصان المتمكن بتركه ،ساهياً، وهذا الجابر إذا كان مثلاً للفائت سهواً كان أدون من الفائت عمداً والشيء لا يجبر بما هو دونه اهـ. وحاصله أن بين السبب والمسبب شرط والعمد جناية محضة والسجدة عبادة فلا تصلح سبباً لها، وهذا بإطلاقه يفيد أنه لا فرق بين واجب وواجب. فما في المجتبى من أنه لا سجود في الملاءمة
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. When he finished mentioning performance (ada') and make-up (qada'), he began to explain what serves as a compensator for deficiency occurring in them. Thus in al-'Inayah. And it is better to say: When he finished mentioning prayer, its supererogatory and obligatory, performed on time and made up, he began to explain what serves as a compensator for deficiency occurring in it. For sujud al-sahw applies to absolute prayer and is not specific to obligatory prayers. This addition is of the type of adding a ruling to its cause, and it is the origin in additions because addition is for specification, and the strongest aspect of specification is the specification of the effect by the cause. It is mentioned in al-Tahrir that there is no linguistic difference between nisyan and sahw, and it is absence of recollection at the time of need. But a distinction is made in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: nisyan is the departure of a thing from the mind after it was present, while sahw can be of what a person knows and of what he does not know. And the apparent meaning of the words of the great majority is that sujud is not required in the case of intentional omission; rather, repeating (i'adah) is required if one intentionally leaves a wajib to compensate for its deficiency. Al-Walwalji mentioned in his Fatawa that if one intentionally leaves a wajib, it is not compensated by two prostrations of forgetfulness, because they are known from the Shari'ah as compensators, and the Shari'ah came in the case of forgetfulness and made them equivalent to what is missed, not above it, because a thing cannot be compensated by something above it. The deficiency resulting from intentionally leaving a wajib is above the deficiency resulting from leaving it forgetfully, and this compensator, if it is equivalent to what was missed forgetfully, is lower than what was missed intentionally, and a thing cannot be compensated by something lower. End. Its summary: there is a condition between cause and effect, and intentional omission is pure transgression, and prostration is an act of worship, so it is not suitable as a cause for it. And this in its absolute sense shows that there is no difference between one wajib and another. So what is in al-Mujtaba that there is no sujud in al-mula'imah (??).
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage marks the beginning of the chapter on sajd al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) in al-Bahr al-Raiq. The author explains why this chapter follows the previous ones on ada' (performing on time) and qada' (making up): sajd al-sahw compensates for any deficiency that occurs during prayer, whether performed on time or made up. He clarifies that sajd al-sahw applies to all prayers, not just obligatory ones. The author then discusses the precise definition of 'sahw' (forgetfulness) and its relation to 'nisyan' (forgetfulness of something previously known). According to al-Tahrir, there is no linguistic difference; both mean absence of recollection at the time of need. However, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj distinguishes: nisyan is when something leaves the mind after having been present, while sahw can be ignorance as well as forgetting. The central ruling presented is that sajd al-sahw is only for forgetful omissions, not intentional ones. If a wajib is intentionally left, the prayer must be repeated (i'adah) because the deficiency is greater, and sajd cannot compensate for something greater than itself. Al-Walwalji's fatwa is cited to reinforce this: the Shari'ah only made sajd a compensator for forgetfulness, so it cannot cover intentional transgression. The passage concludes that this principle applies universally to all wajibat in prayer — no distinction is made between different types of wajib. The reference to 'al-Mujtaba' suggests a contrary view that might be discussed later, but the text is cut off.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for a forgetful omission or addition in prayer.
النقصان (al-nuqṣān): Deficiency in prayer caused by leaving a wajib or performing an extra action forgetfully.
جابر النقصان (jābir al-nuqṣān): Compensator for deficiency; here, sajd al-sahw is the jābir for forgetful mistakes.
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness or inattention, defined as absence of recollection at the time of need.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person intentionally leaves a wajib (obligatory element) in prayer, what is the proper course according to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage?
A) Perform sujud al-sahw to compensate
B) The prayer is valid and no action is needed
C) The prayer must be repeated (i'adah)
D) He must repeat the prayer and also perform sujud al-sahw

Key Takeaway
Sajd al-sahw compensates only forgetful omissions; intentional omission of a wajib requires i'adah.

Salah — Prayer

When Sujud al-Sahw Is Required: General Rule and Exceptions
Defines sahw/nisyan and states the rule with three exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that Sujud al-Sahw compensates forgetfulness, not intentional omission, and identify the three exceptional cases where intentional omission also requires sujud.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw compensates forgetfulness, not intentional omission—except for three weak wajibat.

This passage opens the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness) by defining key terms and establishing the core principle: sujud compensates for forgetful omissions, not deliberate ones. However, the Hanafi school recognizes three limited exceptions where even intentional omission is compensated by sujud because those wajibat are considered the weakest. Understanding this rule and its exceptions is essential for correctly applying the prostration in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Define sahw and nisyan
Read the definitions given in the passage. Note that sahw (absent-mindedness) is broader than nisyan (forgetting), which is the departure of knowledge after having it.
The author mentions that some scholars see no difference; the Siraj al-Wahhaj distinguishes them.
2
State the general rule
Identify the ruling: for intentional omission of a wajib, the prayer must be repeated (i'ada); Sujud al-Sahw does not compensate. This is based on the principle that the severity of intentional omission is greater than forgetful omission.
Al-Walwalji's reasoning: intentional omission is 'pure transgression' and sujud is an act of worship; the latter cannot compensate the former.
3
Analyze the exceptions
Note the three cases where intentional omission IS compensated by sujud: (1) leaving the first sitting, (2) delaying one prostration of the first rak'ah to the end, (3) deliberately thinking about a doubt that distracts from a pillar. These are considered the weakest wajibat.
These exceptions are labeled 'problematic' by the author, indicating that they are not fully accepted.
4
Understand the reasoning behind exceptions
The author suggests that these three wajibat are the lowest in obligation, as some scholars even call them sunnah. Therefore, sujud can suffice even for intentional omission.
This shows that the Hanafi school prioritizes the strength of the obligation when determining the applicability of sujud.

باب سجود السهو لما فرغ من ذكر الأداء والقضاء شرع في بيان ما يكون جابراً للنقصان يقع فيهما. كذا في العناية. والأولى أن يقال: لما فرغ من ذكر الصلاة نفلها وفرضها أداء وقضاء شرع فيما يكون جابراً لنقصان يقع فيها فإن سجود السهو في مطلق الصلاة ولا يختص بالفرائض. وهذه الإضافة من باب إضافة الحكم إلى السبب وهي الأصل في الإضافات لأن الإضافة للاختصاص وأقوى وجوه الاختصاص اختصاص المسبب بالسبب. وذكر في التحرير أنه لا فرق في اللغة بين النسيان والسهو وهو عدم الاستحضار في وقت الحاجة. وفرق بينهما في السراج الوهاج بأن النسيان عزوب الشيء عن النفس بعد حضوره، والسهو قد يكون عما كان الإنسان عالماً به وعما لا يكون عالماً به. وظاهر كلام الجم الغفير أنه لا يجب السجود في العمد وإنما تجب الإعادة إذا ترك واجباً عمداً جبراً لنقصانه. وذكر الولوالجي في فتاواه أن الواجب إذا تركه عمداً لا ينجبر بسجدتي السهو لأنهما عرفتاً جابرتين بالشرع والشرع ورد حالة السهو وجعلهما مثلاً لهذا الفائت لا وفقه لأن الشيء لا يجبر بما فوقه والنقصان المتمكن بترك الواجب عامداً فوق النقصان المتمكن بتركه ساهياً، وهذا الجابر إذا كان مثلاً للفائت سهواً كان أدون من الفائت عمداً والشيء لا يجبر بما هو دونه اهـ. وحاصله أن بين السبب والمسبب شرط والعمد جناية محضة والسجدة عبادة فلا تصلح سبباً لها، وهذا بإطلاقه يفيد أنه لا فرق بين واجب وواجب. فما في المجتبى من أنه لا سجود في العمد إلا في مسألتين ذكره فخر الإسلام البديعي إذا ترك القعدة الأولى عمداً أو شك في بعض أفعال صلاته فتفكر عمداً. شغله ذلك عن ركن قلت له: كيف يجب سجود السهو بالعمد؟ قال: ذلك سجود العذر لا سجود السهو.اهـ. وما في الينابيع عن الناطفي: لا يجب سجود السهو في العمد إلا في موضعين: الأول تأخير إحدى سجدتي الركعة الأولى إلى آخر الصلاة، والثاني ترك القعدة الأولى.اهـ. فتحصل أنها ثلاثة مواضع مشكل. ولعلهم نظروا إلى أن هذه الواجبات الثلاثة أدنى الواجبات فصلح أن يجيرها سجود السهو حالة العمد، أما القعدة الأولى فللاختلاف في وجوبها بل قد أطلق أكثر مشايخنا عليها اسم السنة كما قدمناه، وكذا الثاني والثالث لم يكن لهما دليل صريح في الوجوب.
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. When he finished mentioning performance and make-up, he began to explain what compensates for deficiency occurring in them. It is said in al-'Inayah: It is better to say: When he finished mentioning prayer, supererogatory and obligatory, perform and make-up, he began to what compensates for deficiency occurring in it, for prostration of forgetfulness is in absolute prayer and is not specific to obligations. This addition is of the type adding the ruling to the cause, and it is the basis of additions because addition is for specification and the strongest aspect of specification is the specification of the effect by the cause. It is mentioned in al-Tahrir that there is no difference in language between nisyan and sahw, which is lack of presence at the time of need. And a distinction is made between them in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: nisyan is the departure of something from the psyche after its presence, while sahw may be regarding that which one knew and that which one did not know. And the apparent meaning of the words of the great multitude is that prostration is not required in intentional omission; rather, repetition is obligatory if one intentionally leaves a wajib as compensation for the deficiency. And al-Walwalji mentioned in his Fatawa that if one intentionally leaves a wajib, it is not compensated by the two prostrations of forgetfulness, because they are known as compensators by the Shariah, and the Shariah came in the case of forgetfulness and made them equivalent to what is missed, not above it, because a thing is not compensated by what is above it, and the deficiency established by leaving a wajib intentionally is above the deficiency established by leaving it forgetfully, and if this compensator is equivalent to what is missed forgetfully, it is less than what is missed intentionally, and a thing is not compensated by what is less than it. The summary is that between cause and effect there is a condition, and intentional omission is pure transgression, while prostration is an act of worship, so it is not valid as a cause for it. And this absolutely indicates that there is no difference between one wajib and another. What is in al-Mujtaba that there is no prostration in intentional omission except in two matters mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam al-Badi'i: if one intentionally leaves the first sitting or doubts about some actions of his prayer and deliberately reflects on it, distracting him from a pillar. I said to him: How is prostration of forgetfulness required in intentional omission? He said: That is prostration of excuse, not prostration of forgetfulness. And what is in al-Yanabi' from al-Natifi: Prostration of forgetfulness is not required in intentional omission except in two places: first, delaying one of the two prostrations of the first rak'ah until the end of the prayer; second, leaving the first sitting. So it becomes clear that they are three problematic places. Perhaps they considered that these three wajibat are the lowest of the wajibat, so it is suitable for prostration of forgetfulness to compensate them in case of intentional omission. As for the first sitting, due to disagreement about its obligation, indeed most of our mashayikh have called it sunnah as we mentioned, and similarly the second and third had no explicit evidence for obligation.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness). It first explains the placement of this chapter: after discussing performance and make-up of prayer, the author now turns to what compensates for deficiencies occurring in prayer. Sujud al-Sahw is for all prayers, not just obligatory ones. The author then defines the key terms: nisyan (forgetting) and sahw (absent-mindedness). Nisyan is the loss of something after knowing it, while sahw can be about something known or unknown. The main ruling stated here is that Sujud al-Sahw is not required for intentional omission of a wajib; instead, the prayer must be repeated. However, three exceptions are noted where even intentional omission requires Sujud al-Sahw: (1) leaving the first sitting deliberately, (2) doubting an action and deliberately thinking about it, (3) delaying one of the two prostrations of the first rak'ah to the end. These exceptions are considered 'problematic' (mushkil) by the author, and he explains the reasoning that these three wajibat are the weakest in obligation, some scholars even calling them sunnah, so Sujud can suffice. The passage reflects a nuance: although the general rule is that intentional omission is not compensated by Sujud, these exceptional cases are allowed based on the light nature of those wajibat.

Key Terms
سهو (sahw): Absent-mindedness; lack of presence of mind at the time of need, may be regarding something known or unknown.
نسيان (nisyan): Forgetting; departure of something from the mind after it was present.
عمد (amd): Intentional action; deliberate omission of a wajib in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the exceptional cases where Sujud al-Sahw is required for intentional omission?
A) Leaving the first sitting deliberately
B) Delaying one of the two prostrations of the first rak'ah to the end of prayer
C) Forgetting a rukn (pillar) of prayer
D) Deliberately reflecting on a doubt that distracts from a pillar

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw compensates forgetful omissions, not intentional ones, except for three specific wajibat considered the weakest in obligation.

Obligation of Sujud al-Sahw and Its Proof
Establishes wujub of Sujud al-Sahw with proof from qiyas and hadith, noting ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that Sujud al-Sahw is wajib, explain the qiyas with blood in Hajj, and recount the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on this issue.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib because it compensates a deficiency, just as blood compensates in Hajj.

The performance of Sujud al-Sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) is a common practice in prayer, but its legal status varies between schools. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, exploring the evidence from analogy and Sunnah, and clarifies why the relied-upon position is wujub (obligation) rather than sunnah (recommended).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage focuses on Sujud al-Sahw. Determine its hukm level according to the Hanafi school. Look for keywords like 'يجب' (obligatory) and note the dissent from al-Quduri who calls it 'سنة' (sunnah).
The starting point: the matn decrees obligation after salam with tashahhud and salam.
2
Locate the primary dalil (proof)
Two proofs are given: (1) Qiyas with blood (dam) in Hajj, where deficiency in worship is compensated. (2) Commands in authentic hadiths to prostrate, with the usul principle that a command indicates obligation. Identify each in the text.
The qiyas is the main argument; the hadith commands reinforce.
3
Analyze the qiyas structure
Break down the analogy: Asl = Hajj (deficiency compensated by dam); Hukm al-asl = obligation of dam; Far' = prayer (deficiency due to forgetfulness); Illah = compensation for deficiency in worship; Hukm al-far' = obligation of Sujud al-Sahw. Note the refinement that compensation is of the same type as the deficiency (jins al-kasr).
The passage also explains why dam is used in Hajj (wealth involved) and sujud in prayer (no wealth).
4
Map the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Al-Quduri and some others said Sujud al-Sahw is sunnah. The author of al-Hidayah and others authenticated wujub. Identify the basis for each: al-Quduri may rely on weaker transmission; the majority rely on zahir al-riwayah, qiyas, and hadith.
The tarjih (preference) is for wujub, as stated in al-Hidayah and followed by al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its consequence
The relied-upon position for fatwa is wujub. Consider the practical implication: if a person omits Sujud al-Sahw when required, they are sinful and the prayer is deficient but valid (since the deficiency is compensated by the sujud, and if omitted, the prayer stands but the obligation remains unfulfilled). Contrast with the sunnah view where omission is not sinful.
This has implications for the validity of prayer if sujud is forgotten intentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من السنة قوله (يجب بعد السلام سجدتان بتشهد وتسليم بترك واجب وإن تكرر وبسهو إمامه لا) بيان لأحكام: الأول وجوب سجدتي السهو وهو ظاهر الرواية لأنه شرع لرفع نقص تمكن في الصلاة ورفع ذلك واجب. وذكر القدوري أنه سنة كذا في المحيط. وصحح في الهداية وغيرها الوجوب لأنها تجب لجبر نقصان تمكن في العبادة فتكون واجبة كالدماء في الحج، ويشهد له ما ورد في الأحاديث الصحيحة من الأمر بالسجود والأصل في الأمر أن يكون للوجوب ومواظبة النبي ﷺ وأصحابه على ذلك. وفي معراج الدراية: إنما جبر النقصان في باب الحج بالدم وفي باب الصلاة بالسجود لأن الأصل أن الجبر من جنس الكسر وللمال مدخل في باب الحج فيجبر نقصانه بالدم ولا مدخل للمال في باب الصلاة فيجبر النقصان بالسجدة اهـ.
From the Sunnah: His statement (It is obligatory after the salam two prostrations with tashahhud and salam, due to leaving a wajib even if repeated, and due to the forgetfulness of his imam). Explanation of rulings: First, the obligation of the two prostrations of forgetfulness, which is the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) because it was legislated to remove a deficiency that occurred in the prayer, and removing that is obligatory. And al-Quduri mentioned that it is sunnah, similarly in al-Muhit. And it was authenticated in al-Hidayah and others that it is obligatory because it is required to compensate for a deficiency that occurred in the worship, so it is obligatory like blood (dam) in Hajj, and this is supported by what is reported in authentic hadiths of the command to prostrate, and the principle is that the command indicates obligation, and by the continuous practice of the Prophet ﷺ and his companions. And in Ma'arij al-Dirayah: The deficiency in the chapter of Hajj is compensated by blood, and in the chapter of prayer by prostration, because the principle is that compensation is of the same type as the fracture, and wealth has an entry in the chapter of Hajj, so its deficiency is compensated by blood, and wealth has no entry in the chapter of prayer, so the deficiency is compensated by prostration.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is the commentary on the matn (core text) which states: 'It is obligatory after the salam two prostrations with tashahhud and salam, due to leaving a wajib even if repeated, and due to the forgetfulness of the imam.' The commentator then explains the first ruling: the obligation (wujub) of Sujud al-Sahw. He notes that this is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books). However, al-Quduri considered it sunnah, but the majority including the author of al-Hidayah authenticated it as wajib. The proof is twofold: (1) Analogical reasoning (qiyas): just as blood (dam) is obligatory to compensate deficiencies in Hajj, similarly Sujud al-Sahw is obligatory to compensate deficiencies in prayer. The difference is that Hajj involves wealth, so blood is appropriate; prayer does not, so prostration is appropriate. (2) Hadith: there are authentic commands to prostrate, and commands indicate obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub), and the Prophet and his companions consistently did it. The passage establishes that the correct and relied-upon view is that Sujud al-Sahw is wajib, not just sunnah.

Key Terms
وجوب (wujub): Legal obligation; Sujud al-Sahw is classified as wajib in the Hanafi hierarchy (between fard and sunnah).
سجدتا السهو (sajdata al-sahw): Two prostrations performed after salam to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent or well-known transmission; the core books of Imam Muhammad (the six books).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary analogy used to prove the obligation (wujub) of Sujud al-Sahw according to the passage?
A) It is analogous to fasting compensation (fidyah).
B) It is analogous to blood (dam) in Hajj.
C) It is analogous to zakat.
D) It is analogous to the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah).

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib in the Hanafi school because it compensates a deficiency in prayer by analogy with blood in Hajj, and the relied-upon view is obligation despite a minority sunnah position.

Timing of Sajdah al-Sahw: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Explains obligation, conditions, and dispute on timing of sajdah al-sahw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when sajdah al-sahw is performed, explain the evidence from hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki positions including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib after salam; Hanafi relies on explicit hadith commands over conflicting actions.

The timing of sajdah al-sahw is a classic inter-madhhab dispute. While all schools agree on its obligation, they differ on whether it should be performed before or after the final salam. This lesson explores the Hanafi position, its evidence, and how it responds to the arguments of the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, with practical implications for the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the hukm (wajib) and the time: after the final salam for both addition and deficiency. Note that if the prayer time ends before performing it, the obligation drops.
The Hanafi school considers sajdah al-sahw wajib, not fard, due to the zanni evidence.
2
Identify the opponent's view
The Shafi'i school holds that sajdah al-sahw should be performed before salam in all cases. The Maliki school distinguishes between deficiency (before salam) and addition (after salam).
These differences arise from conflicting narrations of the Prophet's actions.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the reports that the Prophet prostrated before salam. Understand how the Shafi'i and Maliki schools interpret these actions as authoritative.
The opponent relies on fi'l (action) rather than qawl (verbal command).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
When actions conflict, Hanafi usul gives precedence to the explicit verbal command (qawl) over action because action may indicate permissibility, not obligation. The hadith from Abu Dawud and Bukhari explicitly say 'after salam'.
This is a key principle in reconciling contradictory evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis perform sajdah after salam, Shafi'is before, and Malikis vary. If done before salam in the Hanafi school, it is considered valid but makruh tanzih according to the dominant narration.
Unity in congregational prayer also matters: follower should follow imam's practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. The apparent meaning of their words is that if he does not prostrate, he sins for leaving the obligatory and for leaving the prostration of forgetfulness. Then know that the obligation is conditioned on the time being valid, such that if one has forgetfulness in the Fajr prayer and does not prostrate, and the sun rises after the first salam, the prostration drops from him. Similarly if he forgets in making up a missed prayer and does not prostrate until the sky reddens, and similarly in Friday prayer if its time exits. Everything that prevents building if it occurs after salam drops the forgetfulness. Second: its place is after salam by sunnah whether the forgetfulness was by adding something to the prayer or subtracting from it. According to al-Shafi'i, it is before salam in both cases. According to Malik, before salam for deficiency and after for addition. Abu Yusuf forced him in what was from them to be confounded. It is authentically reported that he (the Prophet) prostrated before salam and also after, so the two reports of his action conflict, so we returned to his statement narrated in Sunan Abi Dawud: 'For every forgetfulness, two prostrations after salam.' And in Sahih al-Bukhari in the chapter on facing the qibla wherever he was, in a hadith he said: 'When one of you doubts in his prayer, let him strive for what is correct, complete it, then give salam, then prostrate two prostrations.' This is a general legislative statement after salam concerning the forgetfulness of doubt and striving, and no one makes a distinction between it and the realization of addition and deficiency. This disagreement is about priority, such that if he prostrated before salam, he does not repeat it because if he repeats it would be repeated, and that is contrary to consensus. It is a matter of ijtihad. It is narrated from our companions that it is not acceptable and he repeats it. Thus in al-Muhit. In Ghayat al-Bayan: permissibility is the apparent narration. In al-Tajnis: if the imam holds to the two prostrations of forgetfulness before salam and the follower after salam, some say: he should follow the imam because the inviolability of prayer remains, so he leaves his opinion for the imam's opinion to achieve following. Others say: he follows, and if he follows, there is no repetition on him. The first saying seems based on the apparent narration, and the second on other than it. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth mentioned in al-Khizanah that it is makruh before salam, and apparently it is tanzih. Al-Hidayah explained that because sajdah al-sahw is something that does not repeat, so it is delayed until after salam... (commentary continues) ... Remaining issue: if he forgets the salam, it is compensated by sajdah al-sahw. Ghayat al-Bayan illustrated forgetfulness of salam by his standing to the fifth rak'ah forgetfully, then sajdah al-sahw is required for delaying the salam. Al-Asbajabi and the author of al-Tajnis illustrated it by one sitting thinking he had given salam, then it becomes clear he did not, so he gives salam and prostrates for forgetfulness. And because sajdah al-sahw does not repeat, if one doubts about the forgetfulness, he strives and does not prostrate for this forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on sajdah al-sahw establishes several rulings: first, it is wajib to perform sajdah al-sahw after the final salam of the prayer, and if one omits it, he is sinful for leaving a wajib. However, this obligation is tied to the prayer time still being valid; if the time has expired (e.g., sunrise after Fajr salam, or reddening after Asr), the sajdah drops. The text then presents the inter-madhhab dispute: the Shafi'i school holds that sajdah al-sahw should be performed before salam in all cases, while the Maliki school distinguishes between deficiency (before salam) and addition (after salam). The Hanafi position relies on explicit hadith from Abu Dawud and Bukhari commanding sajdah after salam. Within the Hanafi school, there is a dispute about the validity of performing it before salam: the dominant view (zahir al-riwayah) is that it is permissible but makruh tanzih, while some later narrations deem it invalid and require repetition. The text also discusses the scenario where an imam and follower differ in their practices, recommending that the follower follow the imam to maintain unity. Finally, the principle that sajdah al-sahw does not repeat itself is introduced: if one forgets to perform it until the time has passed, or if he doubts, he does not perform it again.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for unintentional errors in prayer.
السهو (al-sahw): Forgetfulness or unintentional mistake occurring during prayer.
السلام (al-salam): The salutation ending the prayer, typically 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when should sajdah al-sahw be performed?
A) Before the final salam
B) After the final salam
C) Both before and after
D) It is not obligatory

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib after salam; if the prayer time expires before performing it, the obligation drops; the Hanafi position is based on explicit hadith commands.

Sajdah al-Sahw Does Not Repeat: The Story of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan and al-Kasa'i
Anecdote illustrating that no sajdah is required for a mistake made within sajdah al-sahw itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetting in sajdah al-sahw and explain the qiyas analogy with the linguistic principle 'al-musagghar la yusagghar'.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw does not repeat itself — a mistake within it requires no further sajdah.

This lesson presents a famous anecdote between Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and the grammarian al-Kasa'i. It illustrates a subtle Hanafi ruling: if you forget while performing the prostration of forgetfulness, you do not need to perform another sajdah. The ruling is derived via qiyas (analogy) from a grammatical maxim — the diminutive is not further diminished.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actors
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (the great Hanafi jurist) asks al-Kasa'i (a grammarian) to derive a fiqh ruling from grammar.
Note the relationship: al-Kasa'i is Muhammad's cousin.
2
Extract the core fiqh question
The question is: 'What do you say about someone who forgets in the prostration of forgetfulness?'
This is a scenario of a mistake within the compensatory act itself.
3
Understand al-Kasa'i's answer
Al-Kasa'i answers: 'No prostration is required upon him.'
Muhammad then asks for the grammatical basis.
4
Analyze the qiyas analogy
Al-Kasa'i compares it to the linguistic principle 'al-musagghar la yusagghar' – a word in the diminutive form cannot be further diminished. Similarly, an act that is already a compensation (sajdah al-sahw) cannot itself be compensated.
The illa (effective cause) is that both are secondary, derivative acts.
5
State the Hanafi ruling
The ruling: If one forgets or makes a mistake while performing sajdah al-sahw, no additional sajdah is required.
This is a well-established principle in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكى أن محمد بن الحسن قال للكسائي ابن خالته: لم لا تشتغل بالفقه؟ فقال: من أحكم علماً فذلك يهديه إلى سائر العلوم. فقال محمد رحمه الله : أنا ألقي عليك شيئاً من مسائل الفقه فتخرج جوابه من النحو فقال هات. قال : فما تقول فيمن سها في سجود السهو فتفكر ساعة فقال : لا سجود عليه . فقال : من أي باب من النحو خرجت هذا الجواب؟ فقال : من باب أن المصغر لا يصغر، فتحير من فطنته .
It is narrated that Muhammad ibn al-Hasan said to al-Kasa'i, his cousin: 'Why do you not engage in fiqh?' He said: 'Whoever masters one science, that guides him to the rest of the sciences.' Muhammad said: 'I will ask you something from fiqh, and you will deduce its answer from grammar.' He said: 'Go ahead.' He said: 'What do you say about someone who forgets in the prostration of forgetfulness?' He thought for a while and said: 'No prostration is required upon him.' He said: 'From which chapter of grammar did you derive this answer?' He said: 'From the chapter that the diminutive is not further diminished.' He was amazed at his intelligence.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This anecdote illustrates a key Hanafi principle: sajdah al-sahw does not repeat itself. Just as in Arabic grammar, a word in the diminutive form (musagghar) cannot be made diminutive again, so too, if one forgets in the sajdah that is already for forgetfulness, no further sajdah is required. This shows the depth of legal reasoning using analogical (qiyas) and linguistic (usul) principles. The story involves Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani testing the grammarian al-Kasa'i, who correctly deduced the fiqh ruling from a grammatical principle.

Key Terms
المصغر لا يصغر (al-musagghar la yusagghar): A linguistic principle that a word already in the diminutive form cannot be further diminished.
سها في سجود السهو (saha fi sujud al-sahw): To forget or make a mistake while performing the prostration of forgetfulness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone forgets (makes a mistake) in the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw)?
A) He must repeat the sajdah al-sahw
B) He must perform an additional sajdah
C) No additional sajdah is required
D) The entire prayer becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that sajdah al-sahw does not repeat itself; a mistake within it requires no additional sajdah, analogized from the linguistic maxim 'al-musagghar la yusagghar'.

Number of Salams after Sajdah al-Sahw: One or Two?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of salams after sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi view on the number of salams after sajdah al-sahw and explain the reasoning for preferring one salam to the right.

Core Idea
For sajdah al-sahw, one salam to the right is sufficient; giving two is unnecessary and may nullify the sajdah.

The default salam in prayer is two salutations, but after sajdah al-sahw, the scholars differed. Should we give two salams, one to the right, or one straight ahead? In this passage, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the various views and concludes that the most correct position is to give a single salam to the right. Let's walk through the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib; the number of salams after it is a procedural detail. Determine what the default salam in prayer is and why it might differ here.
2
List the three main positions
Two salams (default view), one salam straight ahead (Fakhr al-Islam), one salam to the right (al-Mujtaba).
Note that some sources conflate the straight-ahead and right views.
3
Analyze the talil for each
Al-Bazdawi argued for two salams due to the angel on the left. Al-Muhit argued that the first salam is for tahlil, the second for tahiyya; sajdah only needs tahlil, so one salam suffices.
The talil is key to the tarjih.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The author prefers al-Mujtaba because its reasoning aligns with the majority of later scholars and avoids futility.
5
State the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is one salam to the right only.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق المصنف في السلام فانصرف إلى المعهود في الصلاة وهو تسليمتان كما هو في الحديث، وصححه في الظهيرية والهداية وذكر في التجنيس أنه المختار، وعلل علي البزدوي فقال : لم يجن ملك الشمال حتى تترك السلام عليه وعزاه في البدائع إلى عامتهم، واختار فخر الإسلام أنه يسجد بعد التسليمة الأولى ويكون تلقاء وجهه لا ينحرف. وذكر في المحيط أنه الأصوب لأن الأول للتحليل والثاني للتحية وهذا السلام للتحليل لا للتحية فكان ضم الثاني إلى الأول عبثاً واختاره المصنف في الكافي وقال : إن عليه الجمهور وإليه أشار في الأصل وهو الصواب، فقد تعارض النقل عن الجمهور. وهناك قولان آخران: أحدهما أنه يسلم عن يمينه فقط وصححه في المجتبى . ثانيهما لو سلم التسليمتين سقط عنه سجود السهو لأنه بمنزلة الكلام حكاه الشارح عن خواهر زاده فقد اختلف التصحيح فيها. والذي ينبغي الاعتماد عليه تصحيح المجتبي أنه يسلم عن يمينه فقط لأن السلام عن اليمين معهود متعلق بقوله الآتي يتحرى فهو علة مقدمة على المعلول قوله : (وأطلق) المصنف) أي في قوله «يجب بعد السلام والمراد هنا بيان تحقيق المراد بالسلام وكيفيته بعد بيان أن محله بعد السلام لا قبله فقط أو قبله تارة وبعده أخرى قوله : (أحدهما أنه يسلم عن يمينه فقط ظاهره بل صريحه أنه قول ثالث خارج عن القولين السابقين وأن القول الثاني منهما كون التسليمة الواحدة تلقاء وجهه وهذا القول يخالفه بكون التسليمة عن يمينه وفي شرح المنية ما يخالفه فإنه قال : ثم قيل يسلم تسليمة واحدة ويسجد للسهو، وهو قول الجمهور منهم شيخ الإسلام وفخر الإسلام. وقال في الكافي: إنه الصواب وعليه الجمهور وإليه أشار في الأصل أ هـ. إلا أن مختار فخر الإسلام كونها تلقاء وجهه من غير انحراف الخ. ا هـ. فأفاد أن القائلين بأنها تسليمة واحدة قائلون بأنها عن اليمين إلا فخر الإسلام فإنه يقول بأنها تلقاء وجهه، وبه صرح في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج، وكذا في فتح القدير والعناية والمعراج . والحاصل أن ما صححه في المجتبي هو بعينه ما تقدم أنه قول الجمهور وأنه الأصوب والصواب،
The author (of Kanz al-Daqa'iq) used the term 'al-salam' in an absolute sense, meaning the salam that is well-known in prayer, which is two salutations as in the hadith. This was declared sahih in al-Dhahiriyyah and al-Hidayah, and it is mentioned in al-Tajnīs that it is the preferred (mukhtar) view. Al-Bazdawi gave the reason: 'The angel of the left does not record until you give salam to him.' This was attributed to the majority in al-Bada'i'. Fakhral-Islam chose that he performs sajdah after the first taslim, and [he gives salam] facing his front without turning. It is mentioned in al-Muhit that it is the most correct, because the first is for tahlil (making permissible) and the second is for greeting. This salam is for tahlil, not for greeting, so adding the second to the first is futile. The author of al-Kafi chose this and said that the majority are upon it, and it is indicated in the original (al-Asl), and it is correct. Thus the transmission from the majority is conflicting. There are two other views: one, that he gives salam only to his right, and this was declared sahih in al-Mujtaba. The second, that if he gives both salams, his sajdah al-sahw is dropped because it is like speech — narrated by al-Sharh from Khwahar Zadah. The correction has differed among them. What should be relied upon is the correction of al-Mujtaba: that he gives salam only to his right, because the salam to the right is customary. (Then commentary on the text.) The conclusion is that what was declared sahih in al-Mujtaba is exactly what was mentioned earlier as the view of the majority and is the most correct and proper.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage deals with a nuanced issue: after performing sajdah al-sahw, how many salams (taslim) are given? The default salam in prayer is two salutations (to the right and left). For sajdah al-sahw, some Hanafi scholars said we should give two salams, others one. Fakhral-Islam said one salam straight ahead. The majority of the Salaf, as in al-Mujtaba, say one salam to the right. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (the current commentary) concludes that the position of al-Mujtaba is the relied-upon view: one salam to the right only. The reasoning is that the first salam (in prayer) is for tahlil (making what was forbidden permissible), while the second is for greeting (tahiyya), but the salam of sajdah al-sahw is only for tahlil, so giving both is unnecessary. Some scholars even held that giving two salams would cancel the sajdah, as it resembles unnecessary speech.

Key Terms
تسليمتان (taslimatani): Two salutations (to the right and left) that normally end the prayer.
تسليمة واحدة (taslimah wahidah): A single salutation, e.g., to the right or straight ahead.
تلقاء وجهه (tilaqaa wajhihi): Facing the front (qibla direction) without turning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon Hanafi view on the number of salams after sajdah al-sahw?
A) Two salams (right and left)
B) One salam to the right
C) One salam straight ahead
D) No salam is required

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that after sajdah al-sahw, one salam to the right is sufficient; giving two is unnecessary and may invalidate the sajdah.

Ruling on Forgetting the Salam and Number of Salams in Sujud al-Sahw
Ruling on forgetting salam and intra-Hanafi dispute on one vs two salams.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of salams after sujud al-sahw and explain the intra-madhhab dispute with its tarjih.

Core Idea
One salam to the right suffices after sujud al-sahw; the second salam is superfluous.

When a person forgets the salam in prayer, sujud al-sahw becomes wajib. But after performing those prostrations, how many salams should one give? The matn's absolute word 'salam' is interpreted as two salams by some, but a deeper look reveals a rich intra-Hanafi dispute. This lesson unpacks the positions and identifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario triggering the dispute
The dispute arises after performing sujud al-sahw: how many salams should one give to complete the prayer? The matn says 'salam' absolutely.
The dispute is about the second salam after sujud al-sahw.
2
State the default view from the matn and its supporters
The matn's unqualified 'salam' is understood as the customary two salams (as in hadith). This view is considered correct in al-Zahiriyya and al-Hidaya, and attributed to the majority by Ali al-Bazdawi.
This view relies on the general practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) giving two salams.
3
Identify the opposing positions within the Hanafi school
Fakhr al-Islam holds one salam facing the qibla. Others say one salam to the right (al-Mujtaba). A minority say two salams but sujud al-sahw is dropped.
The dispute is not with another madhhab, but among Hanafi masters.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response and rationale for tarjih
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is one salam to the right. The first salam achieves tahlil (making prayer permissible); the second is tahiyya (greeting) and adding it in sujud al-sahw is frivolous (عبث).
This is supported by al-Mujtaba and many later scholars.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling in practice
The practical consequence: a person performing sujud al-sahw should give one salam to the right only. Two salams are not required and the second would be considered irreligious play.
This is the operative fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو بقي لوسها عن السلام ينجبر به وصور في غاية البيان السهو عن السلام بأن قام إلى الخامسة مثلاً ساهياً يلزمه سجود السهو لتأخير السلام. وصوره الأسبيجابي وصاحب التجنيس بما إذا قاعداً على ظن أنه سلم ثم تبين أنه لم يسلم فإنه يسلم ويسجد للسهو ولكون سجود السهو لا يتكرر لو شك في السهو فإنه يتحرى ولا يسجد لهذا السهو. وحكى أن محمد بن الحسن قال للكسائي ابن خالته: لم لا تشتغل بالفقه؟ فقال: من أحكم علماً فذلك يهديه إلى سائر العلوم. فقال محمد رحمه الله : أنا ألقي عليك شيئاً من مسائل الفقه فتخرج جوابه من النحو فقال هات. قال : فما تقول فيمن سها في سجود السهو فتفكر ساعة فقال : لا سجود عليه . فقال : من أي باب من النحو خرجت هذا الجواب؟ فقال : من باب أن المصغر لا يصغر، فتحير من فطنته . وأطلق المصنف في السلام فانصرف إلى المعهود في الصلاة وهو تسليمتان كما هو في الحديث، وصححه في الظهيرية والهداية وذكر في التجنيس أنه المختار، وعلل علي البزدوي فقال : لم يجن ملك الشمال حتى تترك السلام عليه وعزاه في البدائع إلى عامتهم، واختار فخر الإسلام أنه يسجد بعد التسليمة الأولى ويكون تلقاء وجهه لا ينحرف. وذكر في المحيط أنه الأصوب لأن الأول للتحليل والثاني للتحية وهذا السلام للتحليل لا للتحية فكان ضم الثاني إلى الأول عبثاً واختاره المصنف في الكافي وقال : إن عليه الجمهور وإليه أشار في الأصل وهو الصواب، فقد تعارض النقل عن الجمهور. وهناك قولان آخران: أحدهما أنه يسلم عن يمينه فقط وصححه في المجتبى . ثانيهما لو سلم التسليمتين سقط عنه سجود السهو لأنه بمنزلة الكلام حكاه الشارح عن خواهر زاده فقد اختلف التصحيح فيها. والذي ينبغي الاعتماد عليه تصحيح المجتبي أنه يسلم عن يمينه فقط لأن السلام عن اليمين معهود متعلق بقوله الآتي يتحرى فهو علة مقدمة على المعلول قوله : (وأطلق) المصنف) أي في قوله «يجب بعد السلام والمراد هنا بيان تحقيق المراد بالسلام وكيفيته بعد بيان أن محله بعد السلام لا قبله فقط أو قبله تارة وبعده أخرى قوله : (أحدهما أنه يسلم عن يمينه فقط ظاهره بل صريحه أنه قول ثالث خارج عن القولين السابقين وأن القول الثاني منهما كون التسليمة الواحدة تلقاء وجهه وهذا القول يخالفه بكون التسليمة عن يمينه وفي شرح المنية ما يخالفه فإنه قال : ثم قيل يسلم تسليمة واحدة ويسجد للسهو، وهو قول الجمهور منهم شيخ الإسلام وفخر الإسلام. وقال في الكافي: إنه الصواب وعليه الجمهور وإليه أشار في الأصل أ هـ. إلا أن مختار فخر الإسلام كونها تلقاء وجهه من غير انحراف الخ. ا هـ. فأفاد أن القائلين بأنها تسليمة واحدة قائلون بأنها عن اليمين إلا فخر الإسلام فإنه يقول بأنها تلقاء وجهه، وبه صرح في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج، وكذا في فتح القدير والعناية والمعراج . والحاصل أن ما صححه في المجتبي هو بعينه ما تقدم أنه قول الجمهور وأنه الأصوب والصواب، وبه يحصل التحليل فلا حاجة إلى غيره
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. Remaining: If he forgets the salam, it is made up for by it (sujud al-sahw). The picture of forgetting the salam is very clear: if he stands up to the fifth rak'ah forgetfully, sujud al-sahw is obligatory for delaying the salam. Al-Asbijabi and the author of al-Tajnis described it as when he is sitting thinking that he has given salam, then it becomes clear that he did not give salam, then he gives salam and performs sujud al-sahw. Because sujud al-sahw is not repeated, if he doubts about the forgetfulness, he makes an estimation and does not prostrate for this forgetfulness. It is narrated that Muhammad ibn al-Hasan said to al-Kisa'i, his cousin: 'Why do you not engage in fiqh?' He said: 'One who masters a science, that guides him to other sciences.' Muhammad said: 'I will pose to you a fiqh issue and you extract the answer from grammar.' He said: 'Go ahead.' He said: 'What do you say about someone who forgets in the sujud al-sahw itself?' He reflected for an hour then said: 'No sujud upon him.' He said: 'From which chapter of grammar did you derive this answer?' He said: 'From the chapter that the diminutive is not made smaller.' He was amazed at his intelligence. The author (al-Quduri) used the word 'salam' absolutely in the matn, which is understood as what is customary in prayer, i.e., two salams as in the hadith. It was considered correct in al-Zahiriyya and al-Hidaya, and in al-Tajnis it is mentioned as the chosen view. Ali al-Bazdawi gave the reason: 'The angel of the left does not record sins until you give salam upon him.' It is attributed in al-Bada'i to their generality. Fakhr al-Islam chose that he prostrates after the first salam and it is facing his face, not turning. In al-Muhit it is mentioned that it is more correct because the first is for tahlil and the second for tahiyya, and this salam is for tahlil not for tahiyya, so adding the second to the first is frivolous. The author chose that in al-Kafi and said: 'The majority are upon it, and the original text indicates it, and it is the correct view.' The transmission from the majority is conflicting. There are two other opinions: one is that he gives salam only to his right, and it was considered correct in al-Mujtaba. The second is that if he gives two salams, sujud al-sahw is dropped because it is like speech, narrated by the sharh from Khawarazada. The tashih (correction) differed among them. The one that should be relied upon is the tashih of al-Mujtaba: he gives salam only to the right, because the salam to the right is customary, related to what he said earlier 'he makes an estimation', so it is a cause presented before the effect. His words: (And he said) the author means in his statement 'it is obligatory after the salam', and the intent here is to clarify the meaning of salam and its modality after explaining that its place is after the salam, not before only or sometimes before and sometimes after. His words: (One of them is that he gives salam only to the right) its apparent meaning, rather its explicit meaning, is that it is a third opinion outside the two previous opinions, and that the second of them is the single salam facing his face, and this opinion contradicts it by being the salam to the right. In Sharh al-Munya there is something contradicting it, for he said: 'Then it was said: he gives one salam and prostrates for forgetfulness, and it is the opinion of the majority, including Shaykh al-Islam and Fakhr al-Islam.' And in al-Kafi it said: 'It is the correct view, and the majority are upon it, and the original text indicates it.' End quote. Except that the choice of Fakhr al-Islam is that it is facing his face without deviation. So it indicates that those who say it is one salam say it is to the right, except Fakhr al-Islam who says it is facing his face. This is clearly stated in Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Hajj, and similarly in Fath al-Qadir, al-Inaya, and al-Mi'raj. The conclusion is that what al-Mujtaba corrected is precisely what was previously mentioned as the opinion of the majority and that it is the most correct and right, and with it tahlil is achieved, so there is no need for anything else.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. It begins by addressing the ruling of forgetting the salam. If a person forgets to give salam at the end of prayer, he must perform sujud al-sahw to compensate for the delay. The text gives specific scenarios: if one stands up for a fifth rak'ah forgetfully, sujud al-sahw is required because the salam is delayed. Al-Asbijabi and the author of al-Tajnis describe another scenario: if a person sits thinking he has given salam, then realizes he did not, he gives salam and performs sujud al-sahw. Importantly, sujud al-sahw itself is not repeated; if one doubts about the forgetfulness, he makes an estimation and does not prostrate. The passage then includes an anecdote about Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani and the grammarian al-Kisa'i, illustrating that fiqh and Arabic grammar are interconnected. Al-Kisa'i deduced from the principle 'the diminutive is not made smaller' (meaning a secondary issue does not get a secondary ruling) that someone who forgets in sujud al-sahw itself does not have to prostrate again. The main discussion is about the number of salams after sujud al-sahw. The author notes that the matn's 'salam' is understood as the customary two salams based on hadith, and this is preferred in many works. However, there is a dispute among Hanafi scholars. Some say sujud al-sahw is performed after the first salam only, facing the qibla. Others say after the first salam but turning to the right. A third opinion says that if he gives two salams, sujud al-sahw is dropped. The relied-upon view according to al-Mujtaba is to give only one salam to the right, as the salam to the right is sufficient for tahlil (making the prayer permissible). Fakhr al-Islam held that it is facing the qibla. The author concludes that the correct view is the one in al-Mujtaba, and there is no need for a second salam.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): The prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer, such as delaying or omitting a wajib.
التحليل (al-tahlil): The act of making the prayer permissible to end, i.e., the salam that releases one from the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in al-Mujtaba, how many salams should one give after sujud al-sahw?
A) Two salams
B) One salam to the right
C) One salam facing the qibla
D) No salam

Key Takeaway
After sujud al-sahw, one salam to the right is sufficient; the second salam is unnecessary.
