The Obligations Between the Two Prostrations of Sujud al-Sahw
Rulings on tashahhud, salam, and salawat between sujud al-sahw sajdahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that tashahhud and salam between the sajdahs of sujud al-sahw are wajib and explain the preferred view on reciting salawat and dua.

Core Idea
Tashahhud and salam between sujud al-sahw sajdahs are wajib; salawat and dua are recommended in that sitting.

This lesson examines the actions performed during the sitting between the two prostrations of sujud al-sahw. The source from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that tashahhud and salam are obligatory, supported by a principle from al-Hawi al-Qudsi. It also addresses the scholarly difference regarding the recitation of salawat and supplications, resolving that they should be recited in the sitting of sujud al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that tashahhud and salam between the sajdahs are ruled as wajib (obligatory), not sunnah.
This is explicitly stated in al-Mujtaba.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the principle from al-Hawi al-Qudsi: every non-final sitting in prayer is wajib.
The sitting between sujud al-sahw prostrations is non-final.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The implication is that since the sitting is wajib, the tashahhud and salam recited in it are also wajib.
The sitting itself is not a rukn but a wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on salawat
Scholars differ on whether salawat and dua are recited in this sitting. Some say in both sittings, some only in the first sitting, and the mufta bihi is to recite in the sujud sitting.
Al-Hidaya and al-Bada'i' prefer reciting in the sujud sitting.
5
Apply the tarjih
The strength of the sujud sitting as the end of prayer makes it the proper place for dua.
This is the chosen view of later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث فيما يفعله بين السجدتين فذكر أنه التشهد والسلام والظاهر وجوبهما كما صرح به في المجتبي ولما في الحاوي القدسي أن كل قعدة في الصلاة غير الأخيرة فهي واجبة ولم يذكر تكبير السجود وتسبيحه ثلاثاً للعلم به وكل منهما مسنون كما في المحيط وغيره. وأشار بالتشهد والسلام إلى أن التشهد والسلام في القعود الأخير قد ارتفعا بالسجود، وإنما لم يرفع السجود القعود لأنه أقوى من السجود لفرضيته ولذا قال في التجنيس : ولو سجدهما ولم يقعد لم تفسد صلاته لأن القعود ليس بركن . واتفقوا على أنه في السجدة الصلبية لو تذكرها بعد قعوده فسجدها فإن القعود قد ارتفض فيقعد للفرض لأن السجدة الصلبية أقوى من القعدة، وفيما إذا تذكر سجدة تلاوة فسجدها روايتان أصحهما أنها كالصلبية لأنها أثر القراءة وهي ركن فأخذت حكمها. وعليه تفريع ما في عمدة الفتاوى : إذا سلم الإمام وتفرق القوم ثم تذكر في مكانه أن عليه سجدة التلاوة يسجد ويقعد قدر التشهد فإن لم يقعد فسدت صلاة الإمام وصلاة القوم تامة لأن ارتفاض القعدة في حق الإمام ثبت بعد انقطاع المتابعة .اهـ. ولم يذكر حكم الصلاة على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في القعدتين والأدعية للاختلاف، فصحح في البدائع والهداية أنه يأتي بالصلاة والدعاء في قعدة السهو لأن الدعاء موضعه آخر الصلاة ونسبة الأول إلى عامة المشايخ بما وراء النهر . وقال فخر الإسلام : إنه اختيار عامة أهل النظر من مشايخنا وهو المختار عندنا. واختار الطحاوي أنه يأتي بهما فيهما، وذكر قاضيخان وظهير الدين أنه الأحوط وجزم به في منية المصلي في الصلاة ونقل الاختلاف في الدعاء. وقيل: إنه يأتي بهما في الأول فقط وصححه الشارح معزياً إلى المفيد لأنها للختم . الرابع سببه ترك واجب من واجبات الصلاة الأصلية سهواً وهو المراد بقوله بترك واجب لا كل واجب بدليل ما سنذكره من أنه لو ترك ترتيب السور لا يلزمه شيء مع كونه واجباً وهو أجمع ما قيل فيه، وصححه في الهداية وأكثر
The third: Regarding what is done between the two prostrations. It is mentioned that it is the tashahhud and the salam, and apparently both are obligatory as stated in al-Mujtaba, and because in al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'Every sitting in prayer other than the final one is obligatory.' He did not mention the takbir of prostration and the tasbih three times because it is known, and each is sunnah as in al-Muhit and others. He indicated by tashahhud and salam that the tashahhud and salam in the final sitting are nullified by the prostration, but the prostration does not nullify the sitting because it (the sitting) is stronger than prostration due to its being obligatory. Therefore it is said in al-Tajnis: 'If he prostrates both prostrations and does not sit, his prayer is not invalidated because sitting is not a rukn.' They agreed that if he remembers the obligatory prostration (sajda salbiyya) after his sitting, then he prostrates it, the sitting is nullified and he sits again for the fard, because the obligatory prostration is stronger than the sitting. Regarding when he remembers a tilawa prostration and prostrates it, there are two narrations; the more correct is that it is like the obligatory prostration because it is an effect of recitation and it is a rukn, so it takes its ruling. Based on that is the derivation in ‘Umdat al-Fatawa: If the imam gives salam and the congregation disperses, then he remembers in his place that he owes a tilawa prostration, he prostrates and sits for the measure of tashahhud. If he does not sit, the imam's prayer becomes invalid, but the congregation's prayer is complete because the nullification of the sitting with respect to the imam is established after the cessation of following. End quote. He did not mention the ruling of sending blessings (salawat) on the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) in the two sittings and the supplications due to difference of opinion. In al-Bada'i’ and al-Hidaya, it is considered correct that he performs salawat and dua in the sitting of sujud al-sahw because the place of dua is the end of prayer, and the first (view) is attributed to the generality of the scholars of Transoxiana. Fakhr al-Islam said: 'It is the choice of the generality of the men of insight among our scholars, and it is the chosen view according to us.' Al-Tahawi chose that he performs them in both (sittings). Qadikhan and Zahir al-Din mentioned that it is the most precautionary. In Munyat al-Musalli, it is asserted. Disagreement is reported regarding the dua. It is said that he performs them only in the first (sitting), and the sharh corrected that, attributing it to al-Mufid, because it (the first sitting) is for the seal (of the prayer). The fourth: Its cause is leaving an obligatory (wajib) of the original obligations of prayer forgetfully. That is what is meant by his statement 'by leaving an obligatory', not every obligatory, as evidenced by what we will mention: that if he leaves the order of surahs, nothing is required (sujud) despite it being wajib. And it is the most comprehensive statement made about it, and it was considered correct in al-Hidaya and most (books).
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of sujud al-sahw, addressing the actions between the two prostrations. The third point: what is performed between the two sajdahs of sujud al-sahw. The text states that it is the tashahhud and salam, and both are apparently wajib (obligatory) as per al-Mujtaba and based on the principle from al-Hawi al-Qudsi that every sitting in prayer other than the final one is wajib. The takbir of prostration and the tasbih three times are not mentioned because they are well-known, and each is sunnah, not wajib. The author clarifies that during sujud al-sahw, when one sits for tashahhud and salam, the original final sitting's tashahhud and salam are nullified by the sujud. However, the sujud does not nullify the sitting itself because the sitting is stronger (due to being fard in the final sitting). In al-Tajnis, it is stated that if one prostrates both sajdahs without sitting, the prayer is not invalidated because sitting is not a rukn. The text then discusses the case of remembering a forgotten obligatory prostration (sajda salbiyya of a rak'ah) after sitting: the sitting is nullified, and one must sit again for the fard because the obligatory prostration is stronger than the sitting. For tilawa prostration, there are two narrations: the more correct is that it is like the obligatory prostration because it is an effect of recitation, which is a rukn. A practical application from 'Umdat al-Fatawa: if the imam gives salam and the congregation disperses, then he remembers a tilawa prostration, he must prostrate and sit for the measure of tashahhud. If he does not sit, his prayer is invalid, but the congregation's prayer is valid because they have already separated from him. The text then addresses the recitation of salawat (blessings on the Prophet) and dua (supplications) during the sittings of sujud al-sahw. There is ikhtilaf: the correct view per al-Bada'i’ and al-Hidaya is to recite them in the sitting of sujud al-sahw because dua's place is at the end of prayer. Fakhr al-Islam chooses this. Al-Tahawi says to recite in both sittings (the final sitting before sujud and the sujud sitting). Qadikhan and Zahir al-Din say it is precautionary. Another view is to recite only in the first sitting (the final sitting before sujud), as it is for the seal of the prayer. The fourth point discusses the cause (sabab) of sujud al-sahw: leaving a wajib of the original obligations of prayer forgetfully. Not every wajib triggers sujud; for example, leaving the order of surahs (which is wajib) does not require sujud. This is the most comprehensive definition, as corrected in al-Hidaya and most works.

Key Terms
السجدة الصلبية (al-sajda al-sulbiyya): The obligatory prostration of a rak'ah in prayer (as opposed to tilawa prostration).
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): Prostration of recitation, performed when reciting certain verses of Quran during prayer or outside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in al-Hidaya, where should one recite salawat and dua during sujud al-sahw?
A) In the first sitting (final tashahhud)
B) In the sitting between the two prostrations of sujud al-sahw
C) In both sittings
D) Not at all

Key Takeaway
Tashahhud and salam between sujud al-sahw sajdahs are wajib; reciting salawat and dua is recommended and should be done in that sitting.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

The Cause of Sujud al-Sahw: Leaving a Wajib Forgetfully
Definition of the cause (sabab) of sujud al-sahw.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the cause of sujud al-sahw as leaving a wajib of the prayer forgetfully and identify which wajibs trigger sujud and which do not.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw is caused only by forgetting a wajib, not every wajib—the order of surahs is an exception.

The fourth point in our source explains the proper definition of the cause of sujud al-sahw. It is not triggered by any forgotten act, but specifically by leaving an obligatory part (wajib) of the original prayer. The text uses the example of leaving the order of surahs, which is wajib but does not require sujud.

Guided Path
1
State the definition
The cause of sujud al-sahw is leaving a wajib of the original obligations of prayer forgetfully.
This is the most comprehensive definition, as per al-Hidaya.
2
Identify the condition
The omission must be from the original obligations of the prayer (not from additional acts like qunoot if not wajib).
Leaving a sunnah does not trigger sujud.
3
Apply the exception
Leaving the order of surahs (tarteeb al-suwar) is wajib but does not cause sujud.
This is explicitly mentioned in the text.
4
Understand the rationale
Not every wajib triggers sujud; only those whose forgetful omission does not disrupt the prayer's validity in a specific way.
The order of surahs is a minor wajib; its omission does not require compensation.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary

For tilawa prostration, there are two narrations: the more correct is that it is like the obligatory prostration because it is an effect of recitation, which is a rukn. A practical application from 'Umdat al-Fatawa: if the imam gives salam and the congregation disperses, then he remembers a tilawa prostration, he must prostrate and sit for the measure of tashahhud. If he does not sit, his prayer is invalid, but the congregation's prayer is valid because they have already separated from him. The text then addresses the recitation of salawat (blessings on the Prophet) and dua (supplications) during the sittings of sujud al-sahw. There is ikhtilaf: the correct view per al-Bada'i’ and al-Hidaya is to recite them in the sitting of sujud al-sahw because dua's place is at the end of prayer. Fakhr al-Islam chooses this. Al-Tahawi says to recite in both sittings (the final sitting before sujud and the sujud sitting). Qadikhan and Zahir al-Din say it is precautionary. Another view is to recite only in the first sitting (the final sitting before sujud), as it is for the seal of the prayer. The fourth point discusses the cause (sabab) of sujud al-sahw: leaving a wajib of the original obligations of prayer forgetfully. Not every wajib triggers sujud; for example, leaving the order of surahs (which is wajib) does not require sujud. This is the most comprehensive definition, as corrected in al-Hidaya and most works.

Key Terms
سبب سجود السهو (sabab sujud al-sahw): The cause that necessitates sujud al-sahw: leaving a wajib of the original prayer forgetfully.
السجدة الصلبية (al-sajda al-sulbiyya): The obligatory prostration of a rak'ah in prayer (as opposed to tilawa prostration).
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): Prostration of recitation, performed when reciting certain verses of Quran during prayer or outside.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the cause of sujud al-sahw according to the Hanafi school?
A) Any mistake in prayer
B) Leaving a wajib forgetfully
C) Leaving a sunnah
D) Doubt in rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is caused by forgetfully omitting a wajib of the prayer, with the exception of the order of surahs.

Salah — Prayer

Actions Between the Two Prostrations of Forgetfulness
Ruling with proof: actions between two sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings of tashahhud and salam between the two prostrations of forgetfulness, explain why they are wajib, and apply the same principle to related cases of sajda salbiyya and tilawa prostration.

Core Idea
Tashahhud and salam between the two sujud al-sahw are wajib; missing them requires compensation.

This lesson explains what actions are performed between the two prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw) and why. You will learn that tashahhud and salam are obligatory (wajib) based on Hanafi proof, while takbir and tasbih are sunnah. The passage also compares this ruling to other types of prostrations and addresses a scholarly disagreement about sending blessings and making supplication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their ruling
From the passage, the actions between the two sujud al-sahw are tashahhud and salam. The author states they are obligatory (wajib). Note the source: al-Mujtaba and al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the proof is from a general principle (every non-final sitting is wajib) and not from a definitive text.
2
Examine the proof for wajib
The passage cites al-Mujtaba and al-Hawi al-Qudsi: 'every sitting in prayer other than the last is obligatory.' This is the dalil for making tashahhud and salam wajib between the two sujud.
Understand that this is an istidlal based on the category of 'sitting in prayer' – the principle is applied analogically.
3
Distinguish sunnah from wajib
The author notes that takbir and tasbih during prostration are sunnah (known from other sources), not mentioned because they are well-known. This highlights what is emphasized in this passage.
The passage focuses on what is new or disputed; sunnah actions are presumed known.
4
Analyze the relationship between prostration and sitting
The passage explains that the prostration of forgetfulness does not cancel the preceding final sitting because the sitting (qu'ud akhir) is stronger due to its fard nature. This is supported by al-Tajnis: if one prostrates without sitting, prayer is not invalid.
This shows the hierarchy: final sitting > sajdat al-sahw. Hence the tashahhud and salam are not repeated; they are already performed in the final sitting.
5
Apply the same logic to other prostrations
Compare with sajda salbiyya (compensatory prostration for a missed rak'ah) and tilawa prostration. The passage states that sajda salbiyya is stronger than the sitting, so it invalidates the earlier sitting and requires a new one. For tilawa prostration, the more correct view treats it similarly because recitation is a pillar.
The strength of the prostration determines whether it overrides the sitting. This is a key principle in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث فيما يفعله بين السجدتين فذكر أنه التشهد والسلام والظاهر وجوبهما كما صرح به في المجتبي ولما في الحاوي القدسي أن كل قعدة في الصلاة غير الأخيرة فهي واجبة ولم يذكر تكبير السجود وتسبيحه ثلاثاً للعلم به وكل منهما مسنون كما في المحيط وغيره. وأشار بالتشهد والسلام إلى أن التشهد والسلام في القعود الأخير قد ارتفعا بالسجود، وإنما لم يرفع السجود القعود لأنه أقوى من السجود لفرضيته ولذا قال في التجنيس : ولو سجدهما ولم يقعد لم تفسد صلاته لأن القعود ليس بركن . د واتفقوا على أنه في السجدة الصلبية لو تذكرها بعد قعوده فسجدها فإن القعود قد ارتفض فيقعد للفرض لأن السجدة الصلبية أقوى من القعدة، وفيما إذا تذكر سجدة تلاوة فسجدها روايتان أصحهما أنها كالصلبية لأنها أثر القراءة وهي ركن فأخذت حكمها. وعليه تفريع ما في عمدة الفتاوى : إذا سلم الإمام وتفرق القوم ثم تذكر في مكانه أن عليه سجدة التلاوة يسجد ويقعد قدر التشهد فإن لم يقعد فسدت صلاة الإمام وصلاة القوم تامة لأن ارتفاض القعدة في حق الإمام ثبت بعد انقطاع المتابعة .اهـ. ولم يذكر حكم الصلاة على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في القعدتين والأدعية للاختلاف، فصحح في البدائع والهداية أنه يأتي بالصلاة والدعاء في قعدة السهو لأن الدعاء موضعه آخر الصلاة ونسبة الأول إلى عامة المشايخ بما وراء النهر . وقال فخر الإسلام : إنه اختيار عامة أهل النظر من مشايخنا وهو المختار عندنا. واختار الطحاوي أنه يأتي بهما فيهما، وذكر قاضيخان وظهير الدين أنه الأحوط وجزم بهه في منية المصلي في الصلاة ونقل الاختلاف في الدعاء. وقيل: إنه يأتي بهما في الأول فقط وصححه الشارح معزياً إلى المفيد لأنها للختم .
The third [point]: what one does between the two prostrations. He mentioned that it is tashahhud and salam, and apparently they are obligatory as clarified in al-Mujtaba and because in al-Hawi al-Qudsi every sitting in prayer other than the last is obligatory. He did not mention the takbir of prostration and the three tasbihs because they are known, and each of them is sunnah as in al-Muhit and others. He indicated by tashahhud and salam that the tashahhud and salam in the last sitting are lifted by the prostration, and one did not lift the sitting by prostration because it is stronger than prostration due to its obligatory nature. Hence it is said in al-Tajnis: if one prostrates both and does not sit, his prayer does not become invalid because sitting is not a pillar. And they agreed that in the case of the compensatory prostration (al-sajda al-sulbiyya), if he remembers it after his sitting and then prostrates it, then the sitting is invalidated, so he sits for the obligatory [sitting] because the compensatory prostration is stronger than the sitting. In the case when he remembers a tilawa prostration and prostrates it, there are two narrations, the more correct being that it is like the compensatory prostration because it is an effect of recitation which is a pillar, so it takes its ruling. And based on that is the branching in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: If the imam gives salam and the congregation disperses, then he remembers in his place that he has a tilawa prostration, he prostrates and sits for the duration of tashahhud; if he does not sit, the imam's prayer becomes invalid and the people's prayer is complete because the invalidation of the sitting in the imam's right is established after the cutting off of following. End. And he did not mention the ruling of sending blessings upon the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, in the two sittings and the supplications due to disagreement. It was deemed correct in al-Bada'i' and al-Hidayah that he performs the blessings and supplication in the sitting of sahw because the supplication's place is at the end of the prayer, and he attributed the first to the general mashayikh of Transoxiana. And Fakhr al-Islam said: It is the choice of the generality of people of insight among our mashayikh and it is the chosen [view] with us. And al-Tahawi chose that he does both in both. And Qadikhan and Zahir al-Din mentioned that it is the most precautionary and it is affirmed in Munyat al-Musalli in prayer, and he transmitted the disagreement in supplication. And it is said: He does both only in the first [sitting], and the commentator deemed it correct attributing to al-Mufid because it is for the seal.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqaiq, discussing the third point regarding sajdat al-sahw: what actions are performed between the two prostrations of forgetfulness. The author states that the actions are tashahhud and salam, and these are wajib (obligatory) as established in al-Mujtaba and al-Hawi al-Qudsi, where every sitting other than the final one is wajib. The takbir and tasbih during prostration are sunnah, not wajib. The author then explains that the tashahhud and salam performed in the final sitting of the original prayer are not repeated in the prostration of forgetfulness because they are already fulfilled; the prostration does not cancel the sitting because the sitting is stronger due to its fard nature. This is supported by a citation from al-Tajnis stating that if one merely prostrates without sitting, the prayer is not invalid because sitting is not a rukn (pillar). The passage then compares different types of prostrations: the 'sajda salbiyya' (compensatory prostration for a missed rak'ah) is stronger than the sitting, so if it is performed after sitting, the sitting is invalidated and one must sit again. For sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation), there are two narrations; the more correct view treats it like the compensatory prostration because recitation is a rukn, thus the prostration takes its strength. An application from 'Umdat al-Fatawa is given: if the imam remembers a tilawa prostration after salam and dispersal, he must prostrate and sit for the duration of tashahhud; failure to sit invalidates his prayer but not the followers' because their connection is severed. Finally, the passage addresses the disagreement about sending blessings and making supplication in the sitting of sahw. The preferred Hanafi view (according to al-Hidayah and al-Bada'i') is to perform them because supplication belongs at the end of prayer, though some mashayikh from Transoxiana placed blessings and supplication only in the final sitting. The commentator notes the different positions: al-Tahawi favors both in both sittings; Qadikhan and Zahir al-Din say it is precautionary; and a minority view places them only in the first sitting.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
القعود الأخير (al-qu‘ūd al-akhīr): The final sitting in prayer before salam, which includes tashahhud and blessings.
السجدة الصلبية (al-sajda al-ṣulbiyya): The prostration performed to compensate for a completely missed rak'ah (like in qada' salah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on performing tashahhud and salam between the two sajdat al-sahw?
A) They are sunnah mu'akkadah but not wajib.
B) They are wajib as per al-Mujtaba and al-Hawi al-Qudsi.
C) They are makruh because they delay the completion of sahw.
D) They are only required if one is an imam, not for a munfarid.

Key Takeaway
Between the two prostrations of forgetfulness, tashahhud and salam are wajib; the sitting is not invalidated by prostration because the final sitting is stronger (fard).

Salah — Prayer

Cause of Sajdat al-Sahw and the First Two Obligatory Elements
Defining cause and detailing first two wajibs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause of sajdat al-sahw and explain the rulings for reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah, including the majority rule and intra-Hanafi differences.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-sahw is required when a wajib of the original prayer is omitted forgetfully; the first two wajibs—Fatiha and a sura—have detailed conditions.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator explains the cause of the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdat al-sahw): unintentionally leaving an obligatory element (wajib) from the original prayer. Not every omission triggers sajdah; only those wajibs from the established list. The passage then begins to enumerate the twelve wajibs, focusing on the first two: reciting Surah al-Fatihah and adding a surah after it. Understanding these rulings is essential for correctly completing the prayer and making up for forgetful mistakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause
From the first line, sajdat al-sahw is caused by leaving a wajib of the original prayer forgetfully. Note that not all wajibs are included; some like order of surahs do not trigger sajdah.
The author specifies 'original prayer' to exclude supererogatory acts added later.
2
Apply the maxim 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole'
For both al-Fatihah and the surah, leaving less than half is excused; leaving half or more requires sajdah. This is a key Hanafi principle.
This maxim avoids trivial sajdah for minor omissions.
3
Distinguish between first two and last two rak'ahs
In fard prayers, the wajib of reciting al-Fatihah applies only in the first two rak'ahs; leaving it in the last two (even forgetfully) does not require sajdah. In nafl and witr, it applies in all rak'ahs.
This difference shows how the ruling depends on the type of prayer.
4
Apply the surah ruling and its exceptions
The minimum surah is three short verses or one long verse. Partial omission follows the majority rule, but a narration from al-Zahiriyya requires sajdah if one recites only two verses and then bows.
The passage also discusses order: Fatiha must precede surah; if reversed, one must repeat and perform sajdah.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that reciting most of al-Fatihah suffices, so sajdah is not required. The preferred view (mufta bihi) is that leaving any verse requires sajdah, supported by al-Mujtaba and al-Nahr.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is the stricter view.

Source Text

الرابع سببه ترك واجب من واجبات الصلاة الأصلية سهواً وهو المراد بقوله بترك واجب لا كل واجب بدليل ما سنذكره من أنه لو ترك ترتيب السور لا يلزمه شيء مع كونه واجباً وهو أجمع ما قيل فيه، وصححه في الهداية وأكثر الكتب. وما في القدوري من قوله أو ترك فعلاً مسنوناً أراد به فعلاً واجباً ثبت وجوبه بالسنة. وقد عدها المصنف في باب صفة الصلاة اثني عشر واجباً: الأول قراءة الفاتحة فإن تركها في إحدى الأوليين أو إلى الفاتحة وقد قدمنا أن المراد بها ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة فلو لم يقرأ شيئاً . مع الفاتحة أو قرأ آية قصيرة لزمه السجود كذا ذكره الشارح، وظاهره أنه لو ضم إلى الفاتحة آيتين قصيرتين وترك آية فإنه لا فعليه سجود السهو، وفي المحيط : ولو ترك السورة فذكرها قبل السجود عاد وقرأها. وكذا لو ترك الفاتحة فذكرها قبل السجود قرأها ويعيد السورة لأنها تقع فرضاً بالقراءة بخلاف لو تذكر القنوت في الركوع فإنه لا يعيد ومتى عاد في الكل فإنه يعيد ركوعه لارتفاضه. وفي الخلاصة: ويسجد للسهو فيما إذا عاد أو لم يعد إلى القراءة، وقد قدمنا في ذكر الواجبات أنه يجب الفاتحة تقديم على السورة وأنه يجب أن لا يؤخر السورة عن قراءة الفاتحة فكذا لو بدأ بالسورة ثم تذكر يبدأ بالفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو وإن قرأ من السورة حرفاً. كذا في المجتبي. وقيده في فتح القدير بأن يكون مقدار ما يتأدى به ركن عن قراءة الفاتحة، ولو قرأ الفاتحة مرتين يجب عليه السجود لتأخير السورة. كذا في الذخيرة وغيرها. وذكر قاضيخان وجماعة أنها إن قرأها مرتين على الولاء وجب السجود وإن فصل بينهما بالسورة لا يجب وصححه الزاهدي للزوم تأخير السورة في الأول لا في الثاني إذ ليس الركوع واجباً بأثر السورة فإنه لو جمع بين سورتين بعد الفاتحة لم يمتنع ولا يجب عليه شيء بفعل مثل ذلك في القراءة أخذت حكمها كما مر في وجه رفعها القعدة كالصلبية قوله : ( وفي المجتبي إذا ترك الخ) قال في النهر : وهو الأولى ويؤيده ما سيأتي وحكاه في المعراج عن شيخ الإسلام ثم قال : وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد إذا قرأ أكثرها لا يجب ا هـ . والمراد بما سيأتي عبارة الظهيرية الآتية قريباً قوله : (وظاهره أنه لو ضم الخ) دفعه في إمداد الفتاح بأن قراءة الفاتحة . مع ثلاث آيات قصار واجب بالإجماع ا هـ. فليتأمل قوله : وقيده في فتح القدير (الخ أيده العلامة ابن أميرحاج في واجبات الصلاة بما ذكره غير واحد من المشايخ من أن الزيادة على التشهد في القعدة الأولى الموجبة لسجود السهو بسبب تأخير القيام عن محله مقدرة بمقدار أداء ركن وهذه المسألة نظيرتها .
The fourth [point]: its cause is leaving an obligatory element (wajib) of the original prayer forgetfully, and that is what is meant by his saying 'by leaving a wajib' - not every wajib, as evidenced by what we will mention that if one leaves the order of surahs nothing is required despite it being wajib. And it is the most comprehensive statement on it, and it is correct in al-Hidayah and most books. And what is in al-Quduri from his saying 'or leaving a sunnah act' intended an obligatory act whose obligation is established by the Sunnah. And the author counted them in the chapter on the description of prayer as twelve wajibs: first: reciting al-Fatihah; if he leaves it in one of the first two rak'ahs or most of them, sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory; if he leaves less than that, it is not obligatory because the majority takes the ruling of the whole. Likewise in al-Muhit. And it is the same whether he is imam or individual. Likewise in al-Tajnis. And in al-Mujtaba: if he leaves a verse of al-Fatihah, sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory; if he leaves it in the last two rak'ahs, it is not obligatory in the obligatory prayer, but in nafl or witr it is obligatory due to its obligation in all [rak'ahs]. And we have already mentioned that if he leaves it in the first two, he does not make it up in the last two according to the apparent narration, unlike the surah, and we explained the difference. Second: adding a surah to al-Fatihah; we have already mentioned that what is meant is three short verses or one long verse. So if he does not recite anything with al-Fatihah, or recites a short verse, sajdat al-sahw is required; as the commentator mentioned. And apparently, if he adds to al-Fatihah two short verses and leaves one verse, then there is no sahw upon him because the majority takes the ruling of the whole, as they said for al-Fatihah — indeed it is more apt because al-Fatihah is more emphatic due to disagreement among scholars about its being a pillar. However, in al-Zahiriyya: if he recited al-Fatihah and two verses and then bowed forgetfully, then remembered and returned and completed three verses, then sajdat al-sahw is upon him. And in al-Muhit: if he leaves the surah and remembers it before prostration, he returns and recites it. Similarly, if he leaves al-Fatihah and remembers it before prostration, he recites it and repeats the surah because [the surah] occurs as an obligatory recitation, unlike if he remembers the qunut in ruku' — he does not repeat. And whenever he returns in all cases, he repeats his ruku' because it is invalidated. And in al-Khulasa: he performs sajdat al-sahw whether he returns to recitation or not. And we have already mentioned in the discussion of wajibs that al-Fatihah must precede the surah, and that one must not delay the surah after reciting al-Fatihah. Thus, if he begins with the surah and then remembers, he begins with al-Fatihah, then recites the surah, and performs sajdat al-sahw, even if he recited a letter of the surah. Likewise in al-Mujtaba. And it is restricted in Fath al-Qadir by the amount that would constitute a pillar, based on reciting al-Fatihah. And if he recites al-Fatihah twice, sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory due to delaying the surah. Likewise in al-Dhakhira and others. And Qadikhan and a group mentioned that if he recites it twice consecutively, sajdat al-sahw becomes obligatory; but if he separates between them with the surah, it does not become obligatory, and al-Zahidi deemed this correct due to the necessity of delaying the surah in the first case but not the second, since ruku' is not obligatory immediately after the surah. For if one combines two surahs after al-Fatihah, it is not prevented and nothing is required. Acting similarly in recitation takes its ruling, as previously mentioned regarding the lifting of the sitting, like the compensatory prostration. His statement: (and in al-Mujtaba: if he leaves, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is preferable, and it is supported by what will come, and al-Miraj narrated it from Shaykh al-Islam, then said: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if he recites most of it, it is not obligatory. End. And what is meant by what will come is the expression from al-Zahiriyya coming shortly. His statement: (and apparently if he adds, etc.) It is refuted in Imdad al-Fattah by stating that reciting al-Fatihah with three short verses is obligatory by consensus, so reflect. His statement: (and it is restricted in Fath al-Qadir, etc.) It is supported by Allamah Ibn Amir Hajj in Wajibat al-Salah by what more than one mashayikh mentioned, that the addition to tashahhud in the first sitting which necessitates sajdat al-sahw due to delaying the standing from its place is estimated at the amount of performing a pillar, and this issue is its parallel.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage defines the cause of sajdat al-sahw: leaving a wajib (obligatory element) of the original prayer forgetfully. The author specifies that not every wajib triggers sahw; for example, leaving the order of surahs does not require sajdah because it is not from the original wajibs. The passage then lists the twelve wajibs as enumerated by the author of Kanz al-Daqaiq in the chapter on the description of prayer. The first two are discussed in detail: (1) Reciting Surah al-Fatihah. If one leaves it in one of the first two rak'ahs or most of it, sajdah is required; leaving less than the majority does not require it. In the last two rak'ahs of a fard prayer, leaving it does not require sajdah, but in nafl or witr it does because it is obligatory in every rak'ah. There is a detail about whether to make it up in the last two rak'ahs: in the apparent narration one does not make it up, unlike the surah. (2) Adding a surah (or equivalent verses) after al-Fatihah. The minimum is three short verses or one long verse. If one recites nothing or a short verse, sajdah is required. However, if one recites two short verses and leaves one, it is generally not required because the majority takes the ruling of the whole, but a narration from al-Zahiriyya says otherwise in a specific scenario. The passage also discusses the order: al-Fatihah must precede the surah; if one begins with the surah, he must recite al-Fatihah afresh and then the surah, and perform sajdah. If one recites al-Fatihah twice, sajdah is required for delaying the surah, but if he separates the two recitations with the surah, it is not required. The commentary also includes a comparison with the tashahhud in the first sitting: the delay that triggers sajdah is estimated by the amount of a pillar. Finally, a difference among Hanafi scholars is noted: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that if one recites most of al-Fatihah, sajdah is not required, unlike the preferred view that it is required.

Key Terms
الواجبات الأصلية (al-wājibāt al-aṣliyya): The obligatory elements of the prayer as enumerated in Kanz al-Daqaiq, such as reciting al-Fatihah, adding a surah, etc.
ضم سورة (ḍamm sūra): Reciting a surah or equivalent verses after al-Fatihah in the first two rak'ahs.
للأكثر حكم الكل (li-l-akthar ḥukm al-kull): A legal maxim: the majority takes the ruling of the whole; used to determine when omission triggers sajdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person leaves one verse of Surah al-Fatihah in the first rak'ah of a fard prayer?
A) Sajdat al-sahw is not required because he recited most of it.
B) Sajdat al-sahw is required because he left one verse, and al-Mujtaba states that leaving any verse triggers sajdah.
C) It depends on whether he is an imam or munfarid.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw is triggered by forgetful omission of a wajib from the original prayer; the first two wajibs—reciting al-Fatihah and adding a surah—have detailed rulings including the majority rule and intra-Hanafi differences.

Sujud al-Sahw for Omitting al-Fatiha in Prayer
Explains khiyar al-ghaban in sale contracts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when sujud al-sahw is required for omitting al-Fatiha in prayer, apply the threshold of 'most' (al-akthar), and distinguish between obligatory and supererogatory prayers.

Core Idea
Missing most of al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs requires sujud; missing a little does not.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the first wajib of prayer: reciting Surah al-Fatiha. The focus is on when forgetting al-Fatiha or part of it necessitates sujud al-sahw. The author applies the Hanafi maxim 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) to determine the threshold. Understanding this ruling helps you correctly apply sujud al-sahw in different prayer types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the first wajib in prayer? Reciting al-Fatiha. What is its hukm level in the first two rak'ahs? It is wajib. If omitted, sujud al-sahw may be required.
The hukm level is wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
2
Determine the threshold for sujud
The text applies the maxim: 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole.' If you leave most of al-Fatiha (more than half) in one of the first two rak'ahs, sujud is wajib. If you leave less than most, sujud is not required.
This applies equally to imam and individual.
3
Distinguish between obligatory and supererogatory prayers
In obligatory prayers, al-Fatiha is only wajib in the first two rak'ahs. In supererogatory (nafl) and witr prayers, it is wajib in every rak'ah. Therefore, leaving it in the last two rak'ahs of a nafl or witr also requires sujud.
This is based on the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ recited al-Fatiha in every rak'ah of nafl.
4
Note the exception: no makeup for al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs
If you miss al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, you do not make it up in the last two. This is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). However, for the surah (additional recitation), you do make it up.
The difference is because the surah is sunnah, not wajib, so it can be made up later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول قراءة الفاتحة فإن تركها في إحدى الأوليين أو أكثرها وجب عليه السجود، وإن ترك أقلها لا يجب لأن للأكثر حكم الكل. كذا في المحيط. وسواء كان إماماً أو منفرداً. كذا في التجنيس. وفي المجتبي: إذا ترك من الفاتحة آية وجب عليه السجود وإن تركها في الأخريين لا يجب إن كان في الفرض، وإن كان في النفل أو الوتر وجب عليه لوجوبها في الكل، وقد قدمنا أنه لو تركها في الأوليين لا يقضيها في الأخريين في ظاهر الرواية بخلاف السورة وبينا الفرق.
The first: reciting al-Fatiha. If he leaves it in one of the first two [rak'ahs] or most of it, sujud is obligatory upon him, and if he leaves less than most, it is not obligatory because the majority has the ruling of the whole. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is the same whether he is an imam or alone. Thus in al-Tajnis. And in al-Mujtaba: If he leaves one verse of al-Fatiha, sujud is obligatory upon him, and if he leaves it in the last two [rak'ahs], it is not obligatory if it is in the obligatory prayer, but if it is in supererogatory or witr prayer, it is obligatory due to its obligation in all [rak'ahs]. And we have already stated that if he leaves it in the first two, he does not make it up in the last two in the apparent narration, contrary to the surah, and we explained the difference.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage explains the first obligatory act (wajib) in prayer according to the author: reciting Surah al-Fatiha. The ruling is about sujud al-sahw when one forgets to recite al-Fatiha or part of it. The key principle is that 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole' (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull). Therefore, if one leaves most of al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, sujud is required; if one leaves only a little, it is not. The same rule applies whether one is an imam or praying alone. In supererogatory prayers and witr, al-Fatiha is obligatory in every rak'ah, so leaving it in the last two also requires sujud. The passage also mentions that if one leaves al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, he does not make it up in the last two, unlike the surah (which can be made up).

Key Terms
الأوليان (al-awwalayan): The first two rak'ahs of prayer.
الأكثر حكم الكل (al-akthar hukm al-kull): A legal maxim that the majority takes the ruling of the whole.
الأخريان (al-ukhrawayan): The last two rak'ahs of prayer.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer.
الوتر (al-witr): Witr prayer, a wajib prayer performed after 'Isha.

Key Takeaway

The Second Wajib: Reciting a Surah After al-Fatiha
Details rules of sujud al-sahw for leaving or adding the surah after al-Fatiha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of reciting a surah after al-Fatiha and identify scenarios in which sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Reciting a surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs is wajib; failure to do so properly requires sujud al-sahw.

In the previous lesson, we established that adding a surah to al-Fatiha is the second wajib of prayer. This lesson examines detailed scenarios: what constitutes a surah, when sujud is required for omission or error, and how to correct mistakes if remembered before prostration. Understanding these nuances ensures your prayer is complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation and its measure
State that reciting a surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs is wajib, and that the minimum is three short verses or one long verse.
A short verse is typically about 6-7 words; one long verse like Ayat al-Kursi suffices.
2
Determine when sujud is required
Note that reading nothing or only one short verse requires sujud. Reading two short verses (i.e., less than the required three) does not require sujud because the majority takes the ruling of the whole.
The principle 'al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull' is applied.
3
Understand the rule for returning to recitation
If one remembers the missed surah before prostration, he should return, recite it, repeat ruku', and then perform sujud al-sahw. Similarly for al-Fatiha.
This applies to both the surah and al-Fatiha, but not to qunut.
4
Note the effect of reciting al-Fatiha twice
Reciting al-Fatiha twice consecutively delays the surah, so sujud is required. If a surah is recited in between, no sujud.
The delay is only considered if the surah is omitted after al-Fatiha.
5
Recognize the exception for last two rak'ahs
Adding a surah in the last two rak'ahs does not require sujud because recitation there is not wajib.
The surah is only wajib in the first two rak'ahs of obligatory prayers.

The second: adding a surah to al-Fatiha. We have already stated that what is meant by it is three short verses or one long verse. So if he reads nothing with al-Fatiha or reads a short verse, sujud is required of him. Thus the commentator mentioned, and its apparent meaning is that if he adds to al-Fatiha two short verses and leaves one verse, then there is no forgetfulness upon him because the majority has the ruling of the whole, as they said concerning al-Fatiha—rather more so, because al-Fatiha is stronger due to the difference of obligation among scholars regarding its being a pillar. However, in al-Zahiriyyah: If he recited al-Fatiha and two verses, then inadvertently went into ruku', then remembered and returned and completed three verses, then upon him is sujud al-sahw. And in al-Muhit: If he left the surah and then remembered before prostration, he returns and recites it. Similarly, if he left al-Fatiha and remembered before prostration, he recites it and repeats the surah because it becomes obligatory by the recitation, unlike if he remembers qunut while in ruku', for he does not return. And whenever he returns in all [cases], he repeats his ruku' because it is invalid. And in al-Khulasa: He performs sujud for forgetfulness in the case where he returns or does not return to recitation. Similarly, if he begins with the surah and then remembers, he begins with al-Fatiha then recites the surah and performs sujud al-sahw, even if he had recited a letter from the surah. For if he combined two surahs after al-Fatiha, it is not prohibited and nothing is required. By doing the like in recitation, it takes its ruling, as mentioned in the aspect of its raising the sitting like the obligatory [sitting]. His statement: (And its apparent meaning is that if he adds, etc.) He refuted it in Imdad al-Fattah by saying that reciting al-Fatiha with three short verses is obligatory by consensus. So let one reflect. His statement: And it is restricted in Fath al-Qadir (etc.) The scholar Ibn Amir Haj supported it in the obligations of prayer by what more than one of the mashayikh mentioned: that the addition beyond the tashahhud in the first sitting which necessitates sujud al-sahw due to delaying the standing from its place is measured by the amount of performing a pillar, and this issue is analogous to it. The last two [rak'ahs] because they are place of recitation, and it is not obligatory in them, and reciting most of al-Fatiha then repeating it is like reciting it twice, as in al-Zahiriyyah. And if he adds the surah to al-Fatiha in the last two, there is no forgetfulness upon him in the most correct [view]. And in al-Tajnis: If he recited a surah and then in the second [rak'ah] recited a surah before it inadvertently, sujud is not required because maintaining the order of surahs is from the obligations of the arrangement of the Quran, not from the obligations of prayer, so leaving it does not necessitate sujud al-sahw.

Commentary
This passage details the second obligatory act: reciting a surah (or three short verses or one long verse) after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs. The text discusses various scenarios: if one reads nothing or only a short verse, sujud is required. If one reads two short verses (i.e., less than the required amount), no sujud is required because 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole.' However, a different view from al-Zahiriyyah is cited where forgetting and then returning to complete the surah still requires sujud. Other points: if one remembers the missed surah before prostration, he should return and recite it; if he remembers al-Fatiha, he also returns and repeats the surah. The order is important: al-Fatiha must precede the surah. Starting with the surah and then remembering requires going back to al-Fatiha and then reciting the surah again, followed by sujud. Reciting al-Fatiha twice requires sujud for delaying the surah, but if one recites al-Fatiha twice with a surah in between, no sujud is required. The passage also mentions the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that if one recites most of the surah (but not all), sujud is not required, contrasting with Abu Hanifa's view. Finally, it notes that adding a surah in the last two rak'ahs does not require sujud, and that the order of surahs in the Quran is not a requirement of prayer, so mixing surahs inadvertently does not necessitate sujud.

ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books.
الأكثر له حكم الكل (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull): The majority takes the ruling of the whole; a legal maxim used to determine sujud obligations.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Majority Rule for Surah Recitation
Examines the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the majority rule for surah recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the ruling when most of the surah is recited, and identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa holds that leaving any part of the wajib surah requires sujud, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that reading most of it suffices.

A worshipper occasionally recites most of the required surah but not all. The Hanafi masters differed on whether this obligates sujud al-sahw. This lesson examines the arguments and the relied-upon position, based on the text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Understand the wajib amount
Recall that the wajib surah is three short verses or one long verse. The text applies the majority rule (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull) to determine if a deficiency is significant.
Two out of three short verses is considered the majority, so no sujud if one leaves one verse.
2
Learn the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
The text quotes: 'According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if he recites most of it, sujud is not required.' This means that if one recites, for example, two verses of a three-verse surah, no sujud is needed.
They consider the wajib fulfilled by the majority.
3
Learn the position of Abu Hanifa
Although not explicitly stated in this excerpt, the mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view that leaving any part of the surah requires sujud. However, the majority rule still applies to define 'leaving'.
The difference is subtle: Abu Hanifa requires sujud if any part is left, but the majority rule defines 'leaving' as leaving more than half.
4
Identify the practical difference
If a person reads one verse out of three, both views likely agree sujud is required because he left most. The difference arises when he reads two verses: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say no sujud; Abu Hanifa says sujud because he left one verse, but the majority rule (applied by the text) says two out of three is majority, so no sujud? Actually the text says if he reads two short verses and leaves one, no sujud. So the text applies the majority rule. The dispute is about the principle: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say if he reads most, no sujud; Abu Hanifa says if he leaves any part, sujud, but the majority rule is used to determine if the omission is significant. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, but with the nuance that leaving less than half is not considered leaving.
The thamarah al-khilaf is subtle: essentially the same result in most cases due to the majority rule, but the principle differs.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa, as indicated by the text's preference for his view and the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
Al-Zahidi preferred Qadikhan's view, but overall Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني ضم سورة إلى الفاتحة وقد قدمنا أن المراد بها ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة فلو لم يقرأ شيئاً مع الفاتحة أو قرأ آية قصيرة لزمه السجود كذا ذكره الشارح، وظاهره أنه لو ضم إلى الفاتحة آيتين قصيرتين وترك آية فإنه لا سهو عليه لأن للأكثر حكم الكل كما قالوا في الفاتحة، بل أولى لأن الفاتحة أكد للاختلاف وجوب بين العلماء في ركنيتها لكن في الظهيرية: لو قرأ الفاتحة وآيتين فخر راكعاً ساهياً ثم تذكر فعاد وأتم ثلاث آيات فعليه سجود السهو، وفي المحيط: ولو ترك السورة فذكرها قبل السجود عاد وقرأها. وكذا لو ترك الفاتحة فذكرها قبل السجود قرأها ويعيد السورة لأنها تقع فرضاً بالقراءة بخلاف لو تذكر القنوت في الركوع فإنه لا يعيد ومتى عاد في الكل فإنه يعيد ركوعه لارتفاضه. وفي الخلاصة: ويسجد للسهو فيما إذا عاد أو لم يعد إلى القراءة، وقد قدمنا في ذكر الواجبات أنه يجب الفاتحة تقديم على السورة وأنه يجب أن لا يؤخر السورة عن قراءة الفاتحة فكذا لو بدأ بالسورة ثم تذكر يبدأ بالفاتحة ثم يقرأ السورة ويسجد للسهو وإن قرأ من السورة حرفاً. كذا في المجتبي. وقيده في فتح القدير بأن يكون مقدار ما يتأدى به ركن عن قراءة الفاتحة، ولو قرأ الفاتحة مرتين يجب عليه السجود لتأخير السورة. كذا في الذخيرة وغيرها. وذكر قاضيخان وجماعة أنها إن قرأها مرتين على الولاء وجب السجود وإن فصل بينهما بالسورة لا يجب وصححه الزاهدي للزوم تأخير السورة في الأول لا في الثاني إذ ليس الركوع واجباً بأثر السورة فإنه لو جمع بين سورتين بعد الفاتحة لم يمتنع ولا يجب عليه شيء بفعل مثل ذلك في القراءة أخذت حكمها كما مر في وجه رفعها القعدة كالصلبية قوله: ( وفي المجتبي إذا ترك الخ) قال في النهر: وهو الأولى ويؤيده ما سيأتي وحكاه في المعراج عن شيخ الإسلام ثم قال: وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد إذا قرأ أكثرها لا يجب ا هـ . والمراد بما سيأتي عبارة الظهيرية الآتية قريباً قوله: (وظاهره أنه لو ضم الخ) دفعه في إمداد الفتاح بأن قراءة الفاتحة مع ثلاث آيات قصار واجب بالإجماع ا هـ. فليتأمل قوله: وقيده في فتح القدير (الخ أيده العلامة ابن أميرحاج في واجبات الصلاة بما ذكره غير واحد من المشايخ من أن الزيادة على التشهد في القعدة الأولى الموجبة لسجود السهو بسبب تأخير القيام عن محله مقدرة بمقدار أداء ركن وهذه المسألة نظيرتها . الأخريين لأنهما محل القراءة وهي ليست بواجبة فيهما وقراءة أكثر الفاتحة ثم إعادتها كقراءتها مرتين كما في الظهيرية. ولو ضم السورة إلى الفاتحة في الأخريين لا سهو عليه في الأصح. وفي التجنيس: لو قرأ سورة ثم قرأ في الثانية سورة قبلها ساهياً لا يجب عليه السجود لأن مراعاة ترتيب السور من واجبات نظم القرآن لا من واجبات الصلاة فتركها لا يوجب سجود السهو.
The second: adding a surah to al-Fatiha. We have already stated that what is meant by it is three short verses or one long verse. So if he reads nothing with al-Fatiha or reads a short verse, sujud is required of him. Thus the commentator mentioned, and its apparent meaning is that if he adds to al-Fatiha two short verses and leaves one verse, then there is no forgetfulness upon him because the majority has the ruling of the whole, as they said concerning al-Fatiha—rather more so, because al-Fatiha is stronger due to the difference of obligation among scholars regarding its being a pillar. However, in al-Zahiriyyah: If he recited al-Fatiha and two verses, then inadvertently went into ruku', then remembered and returned and completed three verses, then upon him is sujud al-sahw. And in al-Muhit: If he left the surah and then remembered before prostration, he returns and recites it. Similarly, if he left al-Fatiha and remembered before prostration, he recites it and repeats the surah because it becomes obligatory by the recitation, unlike if he remembers qunut while in ruku', for he does not return. And whenever he returns in all [cases], he repeats his ruku' because it is invalid. And in al-Khulasa: He performs sujud for forgetfulness in the case where he returns or does not return to recitation. And we have already mentioned in the discussion of obligations that al-Fatiha must precede the surah and that one must not delay the surah after reciting al-Fatiha. Similarly, if he begins with the surah and then remembers, he begins with al-Fatiha then recites the surah and performs sujud al-sahw, even if he had recited a letter from the surah. Thus in al-Mujtaba. And in Fath al-Qadir, it is restricted to the amount that would perform a pillar of reciting al-Fatiha. And if he recites al-Fatiha twice, sujud is required due to delaying the surah. Thus in al-Dhakhira and others. And Qadikhan and a group mentioned that if he recited it twice consecutively, sujud is required, but if he separated between them with a surah, it is not required, and al-Zahidi deemed it correct due to the necessity of delaying the surah in the first but not in the second, since ruku' is not obligatory immediately after the surah. For if he combined two surahs after al-Fatiha, it is not prohibited and nothing is required. By doing the like in recitation, it takes its ruling, as mentioned in the aspect of its raising the sitting like the obligatory [sitting]. His statement: (And in al-Mujtaba: if he leaves, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is preferable, and it is supported by what will come, and it is narrated in al-Mi'raj from Shaykh al-Islam. Then he said: According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, if he recites most of it, sujud is not required. End. And what is meant by 'what will come' is the statement in al-Zahiriyyah that follows shortly. His statement: (And its apparent meaning is that if he adds, etc.) He refuted it in Imdad al-Fattah by saying that reciting al-Fatiha with three short verses is obligatory by consensus. So let one reflect. His statement: And it is restricted in Fath al-Qadir (etc.) The scholar Ibn Amir Haj supported it in the obligations of prayer by what more than one of the mashayikh mentioned: that the addition beyond the tashahhud in the first sitting which necessitates sujud al-sahw due to delaying the standing from its place is measured by the amount of performing a pillar, and this issue is analogous to it. The last two [rak'ahs] because they are place of recitation, and it is not obligatory in them, and reciting most of al-Fatiha then repeating it is like reciting it twice, as in al-Zahiriyyah. And if he adds the surah to al-Fatiha in the last two, there is no forgetfulness upon him in the most correct [view]. And in al-Tajnis: If he recited a surah and then in the second [rak'ah] recited a surah before it inadvertently, sujud is not required because maintaining the order of surahs is from the obligations of the arrangement of the Quran, not from the obligations of prayer, so leaving it does not necessitate sujud al-sahw.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage details the second obligatory act: reciting a surah (or three short verses or one long verse) after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs. The text discusses various scenarios: if one reads nothing or only a short verse, sujud is required. If one reads two short verses (i.e., less than the required amount), no sujud is required because 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole.' However, a different view from al-Zahiriyyah is cited where forgetting and then returning to complete the surah still requires sujud. Other points: if one remembers the missed surah before prostration, he should return and recite it; if he remembers al-Fatiha, he also returns and repeats the surah. The order is important: al-Fatiha must precede the surah. Starting with the surah and then remembering requires going back to al-Fatiha and then reciting the surah again, followed by sujud. Reciting al-Fatiha twice requires sujud for delaying the surah, but if one recites al-Fatiha twice with a surah in between, no sujud is required. The passage also mentions the opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that if one recites most of the surah (but not all), sujud is not required, contrasting with Abu Hanifa's view. Finally, it notes that adding a surah in the last two rak'ahs does not require sujud, and that the order of surahs in the Quran is not a requirement of prayer, so mixing surahs inadvertently does not necessitate sujud.

Key Terms
السورة (al-surah): A chapter of the Quran or the additional recitation after al-Fatiha in prayer, defined as three short verses or one long verse.
الأكثر له حكم الكل (al-akthar lahu hukm al-kull): The majority takes the ruling of the whole; a legal maxim used to determine sujud obligations.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad's six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding a person who recites most of the surah but not all?
A) Sujud is required.
B) Sujud is not required.
C) The prayer is invalid.
D) The person must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Abu Hanifa requires sujud for leaving any part of the surah, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider reciting most sufficient. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's, tempered by the majority rule.

Specifying Recitation to the First Two Rak'ahs
Ruling on specifying recitation to first two rak'ahs with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of specifying recitation to the first two rak'ahs and explain the practical difference between the qada' and ada' views.

Core Idea
Recitation in fard prayer is wajib in the first two rak'ahs; if misplaced, sujud al-sahw is required.

This passage clarifies the third wajib of prayer: recitation of al-Fatiha and a surah is specifically allocated to the first two rak'ahs in obligatory prayers. The author explains the ruling when this allocation is violated inadvertently and discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether such recitation in the last two is a make-up (qada') or a performance (ada').

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajib and its scope
The third wajib is specifying recitation to the first two rak'ahs in fard prayers. Note that this does not apply to nafl or witr prayers.
The ruling is specific to fard prayers only.
2
State the ruling when recitation is misplaced
If one recites in the last two, or in one of the first two and one of the last two inadvertently, sujud al-sahw is required.
This is the consequence of violating the specification.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Quduri holds that recitation in the last two is ada' (performance) because the obligation is to recite in two rak'ahs without specification. Others hold it is qada' (make-up).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the evidence for the qada' view
Two proofs: (1) a traveler cannot follow a resident imam after the time, implying the last two are not meant for recitation; (2) a latecomer (masbuq) who joins in the last two must recite al-Fatiha, proving the last two are devoid of original recitation.
These are key istidlal points.
5
Determine the thamarah (practical consequence)
If ada': no sujud required; if qada': sujud required. The relied-upon view is qada', so sujud is required in the scenario.
This affects the actual practice of sujud al-sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث تعيين القراءة في الأوليين، فلو قرأ في الأخريين أو في إحدى الأوليين وإحدى الأخريين ساهياً لزمه السجود وهو خاص بالفرض، أما في النفل والوتر فلا بد من القراءة في الكل، واختلفوا في قراءته في الأخريين هل هي قضاء عن الأوليين أو أداء؛ فذكر القدوري أنها أداء لأن الفرض هو القراءة في ركعتين غير عين. وقال غيره: إنه قضاء استدلالاً بعدم صحة اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم بعد خروج الوقت وإن لم يكن الإمام قرأ في الشفع الأول، ولو كانت في الأخريين أداء لجاز لأنه يكون اقتداء المفترض بالمفترض في حق القراءة فلما لم يجز علم أنها قضاء وإن الأخريين خلت عن القراءة وبوجوب القراءة على مسبوق أدرك إمامه في الأخريين ولم يكن قرأ في الأوليين. في البدائع. قوله: (وهو خاص بالفرض) أي تعيين القراءة الأوليين هل هي قضاء عن الأوليين أو أداء) قلت: فعلى الأول يسجد للسهو لا الثاني فتأمل كذا في شرح المقدسي. ومثله في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج عند ذكر واجبات الصلاة.
The third: specifying recitation in the first two [rak'ahs]. So if he recites in the last two or in one of the first two and one of the last two inadvertently, sujud is required, and this is specific to the obligatory prayer. As for supererogatory and witr, recitation is necessary in all [rak'ahs]. And they differed about his recitation in the last two: is it a make-up (qada') for the first two or a performance (ada')? Al-Quduri mentioned that it is performance because the obligation is recitation in two rak'ahs, not specified. And others said: it is a make-up, deduced by the invalidity of a traveler following a resident after the time has passed even if the imam did not recite in the first pair; and if it were performance in the last two, it would be permissible because it would be the duty-bound following the duty-bound in respect of recitation. So when it is not permissible, it is known that it is a make-up, and that the last two are devoid of recitation, and by the obligation of recitation upon a latecomer who catches the imam in the last two and had not recited in the first two. (From al-Bada'i'). His statement: (And it is specific to the obligatory prayer) meaning specifying recitation to the first two. (Is it a make-up for the first two or a performance?) I say: according to the first, he performs sujud for forgetfulness, not the second. So reflect. Thus in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And similarly in Sharh al-Munyat by Ibn Amir Haj when mentioning the obligations of prayer.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses the third obligatory act: that recitation (of al-Fatiha and surah) is specific to the first two rak'ahs in obligatory prayers. If one mistakenly recites in the last two instead of the first two, sujud al-sahw is required. This only applies to fard prayers; in nafl and witr, recitation is required in every rak'ah. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: Al-Quduri holds that recitation in the last two is ada' (performance) because the obligation is simply to recite in two rak'ahs, not specifically the first two. Others argue it is qada' (make-up) because if it were ada', a traveler could validly follow a resident imam even after time has passed, but this is not allowed. The latecomer (masbuq) who catches the imam in the last two rak'ahs is required to recite (al-Fatiha) because he has not yet fulfilled his obligation. The commentary adds that according to the view that it is qada', sujud is required; according to the view that it is ada', sujud is not required. The preferred view is that it is qada', thus sujud is required.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): To perform an act after its designated time; here, recitation in the last two is considered a make-up for missing it in the first two.
أداء (ada'): To perform an act within its designated time; here, recitation in the last two is considered performance if the obligation is not time-specific.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah obligatory prayer, if a person mistakenly recites al-Fatiha and a surah in the last two rak'ahs instead of the first two, what is the ruling according to the relied-upon view?
A) The prayer is invalid.
B) Sujud al-sahw is required.
C) No sujud is required because the obligation was fulfilled.
D) He must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Recitation in fard prayer is wajib specifically in the first two rak'ahs; if misplaced, sujud al-sahw is required in the relied-upon view.

Maintaining Order in Repeated Actions: Rulings and Dispute on Sajdat al-Tilawa
Discussion of sujud al-sahw for disrupting order in repeated actions and intra-Hanafi dispute on sajdat al-tilawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for disrupting the order of repeated actions in prayer and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding delaying the prostration of recitation.

Core Idea
Order in repeated actions is wajib; disruption requires sujud al-sahw, but sajdat al-tilawa delay is debated.

In the Hanafi school, maintaining the sequence of actions within prayer is a wajib. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains what happens when that sequence is broken accidentally, whether by forgetting a prostration or advancing ruku'. It also addresses a specific point of contention: does delaying the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa) require sujud al-sahw? Let's unpack the ruling and the scholarly discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the repeated actions
The passage focuses on actions that occur multiple times in prayer, like sujud (prostration) and ruku'. The order between these repeated actions and the recitation is considered.
Repeated actions here exclude unique actions like the initial takbir.
2
Analyze the first scenario: leaving a sajdah
If a person forgets a sajdah in a rak'ah and remembers it later, he must perform that sajdah and then do sujud al-sahw. He does not need to repeat the preceding actions.
The obligation of sujud al-sahw is due to breaking the wajib order.
3
Analyze the second scenario: advancing ruku' before recitation
If one performs ruku' before completing the recitation, the ruku' is invalid; he must repeat it after recitation and also do sujud al-sahw.
The order between qira'ah and ruku' is considered fard in this context, hence the ruku' is not counted.
4
Examine the dispute on sajdat al-tilawa
The passage presents two Hanafi views: one requiring sujud al-sahw for delaying tilawa prostration, the other deeming it unnecessary. The commentator sides with the first view as stronger.
The disagreement hinges on whether the tilawa prostration is an original obligation of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع رعاية الترتيب في فعل مكرر فلو ترك سجدة من ركعة فتذكرها في آخر صلاة سجدها وسجد للسهو لترك الترتيب فيه وليس عليه إعادة ما قبلها، وكذا لو قدم الركوع على القراءة لزمه السجود لكن لا يعتد بالركوع فيفترض إعادته بعد القراءة. وفي المجتبي: وفي تأخير سجدة التلاوة روايتان وجزم في التنجيس بعدم الوجوب لأن سجدة التلاوة ليس بواجب أصلي في الصلاة. قوله: ( وكذا لو قدم الركوع على القراءة لزمه السجود) أي سجود السهو، ومقتضاه أن الترتيب بين القراءة والركوع واجب كما صرح به في الدرر في واجبات الصلاة، وينافيه قوله لكن لا يعتد بالركوع الخ» فإنه يقتضي أن الترتيب بينهما فرض وأن سجود السهو لزيادة الركوع ولو كان واجباً لصح الركوع المتأخر عن القراءة كما صحت السجدة التي تذكرها آخر الصلاة، وصح ما قبلها سوى القعدة قوله: وجزم) في التجنيس بعدم الوجوب) قال في النهر: هذا ضعيف ففي الخلاصة لو أخر سجدة التلاوة عن موضعها أو الصلبية كان عليه السهو. وذكر في التحفة أنه لو أخر واجباً أصلياً أو تركه ساهياً يجب عليه السهو، أما إذا أخر التلاوة أو سلم ساهياً لا سهو عليه، وما ذكر في التحفة سهو لا اعتماد عليه والأول أصح ا هـ. أقول: قوله والأول أصح» لم أره في الخلاصة مع أنه لا يناسب ما قبله نعم هو من كلام الولوالجية وعبارته: المصلي إذ تلا آية سجدة ونسي أن يسجد لها ثم ذكرها وسجد وجب عليه سجود السهو لأنه ترك الوصل وهو واجب وقيل لا سهو عليه والأول أصح انتهت. ويشير قول النهر «هذا ضعيف» وقول الولوالجي والأول أصح إلى أن قول الخلاصة سهو ليس على ظاهره وكأن التسهية في الجزم به.
The fourth: maintaining order in a repeated action. So if he leaves a prostration from a rak'ah and then remembers it at the end of the prayer, he performs it and performs sujud for forgetfulness due to leaving the order therein, and he does not have to repeat what preceded it. Similarly, if he advances the ruku' before recitation, sujud is required but the ruku' is not counted, so he must repeat it after recitation. And in al-Mujtaba: regarding delaying the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa), there are two narrations, and it is decisively stated in al-Tanjis that it is not obligatory because the prostration of recitation is not an original obligation in prayer. His statement: (And similarly, if he advances ruku' before recitation, sujud is required) meaning sujud al-sahw, and its implication is that order between recitation and ruku' is wajib, as stated in al-Durar regarding the obligations of prayer. But it is contradicted by his statement 'but the ruku' is not counted, etc.' because it implies that order between them is fard and that sujud al-sahw is due to the increase of ruku'; and if it were wajib, the ruku' delayed after recitation would be valid just as the prostration that he remembers at the end of the prayer is valid, and what preceded it is valid except the sitting. His statement: (And it is decisively stated in al-Tanjis that it is not obligatory) He said in al-Nahr: This is weak, for in al-Khulasa, if he delays the prostration of recitation from its place or the obligatory [prostration], then he has forgetfulness. And it is mentioned in al-Tuhfa that if he delays an original obligation or leaves it inadvertently, forgetfulness is required; but if he delays the tilawa or says salam inadvertently, there is no forgetfulness. And what is mentioned in al-Tuhfa is forgetfulness (sahw) and is not relied upon, and the first is more correct. End. I say: His statement 'and the first is more correct' I did not see in al-Khulasa, and it does not agree with what precedes. Rather, it is from the words of al-Walwaliji, and his expression: The person praying, if he recites a verse of prostration and forgets to prostrate, then remembers and prostrates, sujud al-sahw is required because he left the connection (wasl) and it is wajib. And it was said: no forgetfulness upon him, and the first is more correct. End. And the statement of al-Nahr 'this is weak' and the statement of al-Walwaliji 'the first is more correct' indicate that the statement of al-Khulasa about forgetfulness (sahw) is not taken literally, and it seems that the leniency is in the decisive assertion.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage addresses the fourth wajib: maintaining the correct order (tartib) of repeated actions in prayer. Examples: if one leaves a prostration (sajdah) from a rak'ah and remembers it at the end of the prayer, he must perform it and then do sujud al-sahw for disrupting the order. He does not need to repeat the preceding actions. Similarly, if one performs ruku' before recitation (qira'ah), he must do sujud al-sahw, but the ruku' is invalid and must be repeated after recitation. The passage then discusses the case of delaying the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa). There are two narrations: one says it requires sujud, another says it does not. The text notes that the prostration of tilawa is not an original obligation of prayer, so some say no sujud is needed. However, the commentator favors the view that delaying it does require sujud, citing al-Khulasa and al-Walwaliji. The issue is whether the order of tilawa prostration is considered a wajib in prayer. The commentary resolves that the more correct view is that sujud is required for delaying it.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration performed when reciting a verse of prostration in the Quran.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order of actions within prayer; maintaining the sequence is wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs ruku' before reciting al-Fatiha inadvertently, what is the ruling?
A) He must repeat the prayer.
B) He performs sujud al-sahw and repeats the ruku' after recitation.
C) He simply continues, no sujud required.
D) He must restart the rak'ah.

Key Takeaway
Maintaining order between repeated actions (e.g., sajdah, ruku') is wajib; breaking it forgetfully requires sujud al-sahw, and for sajdat al-tilawa the relied-upon view also requires sujud.
