Fourth Cause of Sahw: Order in Repeated Actions and the Dispute on Sajda al-Tilawa
Explains the fourth cause of sahw regarding order in repeated actions like sajdah and rak'ah components

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the order between recitation and ruku' in prayer, identify the fard nature of this order, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether delaying sajda al-tilawah requires sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
Order between recitation and ruku' is fard; violating it invalidates the ruku' and requires sahw. Sajda al-tilawah's delay is disputed: connected duty or not?

We now examine the fourth cause of sajdah al-sahw: maintaining order in repeated actions within the prayer, such as the sajdahs of a rak'ah and the sequence of recitation before ruku'. The passage reveals a critical distinction between fard and wajib order, and it opens a lively intra-Hanafi debate about whether delaying the prostration of recitation (sajda al-tilawah) from its immediate place triggers sajdah al-sahw. This lesson will help you navigate the nuances of order violations and the authoritative positions on sajda al-tilawah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses two scenarios: (1) forgetting a sajdah from a rak'ah and remembering at the end, and (2) performing ruku' before recitation. Note the ruling for each: the first requires performing the missed sajdah and sajdah al-sahw without repeating earlier actions; the second requires repeating the ruku' after recitation and sajdah al-sahw.
The differing consequences show different hukm levels for the violated order.
2
Distinguish between fard and wajib order
The passage implies that the order between recitation and ruku' is fard (rukn) because the misplaced ruku' is invalid and must be repeated. If it were only wajib, the ruku' would be considered valid with sahw. This contrasts with the first scenario where the missed sajdah is a wajib—it is valid when performed later, but sahw is required.
The commentator explicitly states that the text indicates the order is fard, not wajib.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on sajda al-tilawah
The passage reports two positions: (a) al-Tajnīs rules that delaying sajda al-tilawah does not require sahw because it is not an original wajib of prayer; (b) al-Khulasa and al-Walwaliji rule that sahw is required because the immediate connection (wasl) is itself a wajib. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq considers the view of al-Tajnīs weak.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school; later authorities have settled on the second view.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position (al-mu'tamad) is that delaying sajda al-tilawah does require sajdah al-sahw, as supported by al-Khulasa, al-Walwaliji, and the endorsement of al-Nahr (al-Bahr al-Raiq). The tarjih is based on the principle that an omitted wajib connected to the prayer necessitates sahw.
The dispute is resolved in favor of the view requiring sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع رعاية الترتيب في فعل مكرر فلو ترك سجدة من ركعة فتذكرها في آخر صلاة سجدها وسجد للسهو لترك الترتيب فيه وليس عليه إعادة ما قبلها، وكذا لو قدم الركوع على القراءة لزمه السجود لكن لا يعتد بالركوع فيفترض إعادته بعد القراءة. وفي المجتبي: وفي تأخير سجدة التلاوة روايتان وجزم في التنجيس بعدم الوجوب لأن سجدة التلاوة ليس بواجب أصلي في الصلاة. قوله: (وكذا لو قدم الركوع على القراءة لزمه السجود) أي سجود السهو، ومقتضاه أن الترتيب بين القراءة والركوع واجب كما صرح به في الدرر في واجبات الصلاة، وينافيه قوله لكن لا يعتد بالركوع الخ فإنه يقتضي أن الترتيب بينهما فرض وأن سجود السهو لزيادة الركوع ولو كان واجباً لصح الركوع المتأخر عن القراءة كما صحت السجدة التي تذكرها آخر الصلاة، وصح ما قبلها سوى القعدة. قوله: وجزم في التجنيس بعدم الوجوب قال في النهر: هذا ضعيف ففي الخلاصة لو أخر سجدة التلاوة عن موضعها أو الصلبية كان عليه السهو. وذكر في التحفة أنه لو أخر واجباً أصلياً أو تركه ساهياً يجب عليه السهو، أما إذا أخر التلاوة أو سلم ساهياً لا سهو عليه، وما ذكر في التحفة سهو لا اعتماد عليه والأول أصح ا هـ. أقول: قوله والأول أصح لم أره في الخلاصة مع أنه لا يناسب ما قبله نعم هو من كلام الولوالجية وعبارته: المصلي إذ تلا آية سجدة ونسي أن يسجد لها ثم ذكرها وسجد وجب عليه سجود السهو لأنه ترك الوصل وهو واجب وقيل لا سهو عليه والأول أصح انتهت. ويشير قول النهر «هذا ضعيف» وقول الولوالجي والأول أصح إلى أن قول الخلاصة سهو ليس على ظاهره وكأن التسهية في الجزم به
The fourth: observance of order in a repeated action. So if one forgets a prostration from a rak'ah and remembers it at the end of the prayer, he performs it and prostrates for sahw due to the violation of order, and he is not required to repeat what preceded it. Similarly, if one places the bowing before the recitation, sajdah al-sahw is incumbent on him, but the bowing is not valid and he must repeat it after recitation. In al-Mujtaba: concerning delaying sajda al-tilawah, there are two narrations, and in al-Tajnīs he definitively ruled it is not obligatory because sajda al-tilawah is not an original obligatory act in the prayer. His statement: (Similarly, if he places bowing before recitation, sajdah is incumbent) meaning sajdah al-sahw, and its implication is that order between recitation and bowing is wajib, as clarified in al-Durar on the obligatory acts of prayer, but it conflicts with his statement 'but the bowing is not valid' etc., because it indicates that order between them is fard and that sajdah al-sahw is due to the addition of bowing; if it were wajib, the delayed bowing after recitation would be valid just as the prostration remembered at the end of prayer was valid, and what preceded it was valid except the sitting. His statement: (And in al-Tajnīs he definitively ruled it is not obligatory) said in al-Nahr: this is weak; for in al-Khulasa, if one delays sajda al-tilawah from its place or from the prayer, sahw is required of him. And it is mentioned in al-Tuhfa that if one delays an original wajib or leaves it forgetfully, sahw is required; but if he delays the tilawa or says salam forgetfully, no sahw is required. And what is mentioned in al-Tuhfa is negligent (sahw), no reliance, and the first is more correct. I say: his statement 'the first is more correct' I have not seen in al-Khulasa, and it is inconsistent with what precedes; rather it is from the words of al-Walwaliji, and his expression: 'A praying person, when he recites a verse of sajdah and forgets to prostrate for it, then remembers and prostrates, sajdah al-sahw is obligatory upon him because he left the connecting (al-wasl) which is wajib, and it is said no sahw is required, and the first is more correct' — it ends. And the statement of al-Nahr 'this is weak' and the statement of al-Walwaliji 'the first is more correct' indicates that the statement of al-Khulasa is not apparent, and it is as if there is leniency in asserting it.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth cause of sajdah al-sahw: maintaining order in repeated actions within the prayer. If a sajdah is forgotten from a rak'ah and remembered at the end, it is performed and sajdah al-sahw is required for the disruption of order; there is no need to repeat earlier parts. However, if one mistakenly performs ruku' before recitation, sajdah al-sahw is required, but the ruku' itself is invalid and must be repeated after recitation. This indicates that order between recitation and ruku' is fard (integral) rather than just wajib, because if it were wajib, the misplaced ruku' would still be valid with sahw. The passage then discusses delaying sajda al-tilawah: some narrations consider it wajib, others not. The author of al-Tajnīs ruled it is not obligatory because sajda al-tilawah is not an original wajib of the prayer. However, al-Nahr considers that view weak, citing al-Khulasa that delaying it does require sahw. The super-commentary clarifies that the relied-upon position is that delaying sajda al-tilawah does require sajdah al-sahw.

Key Terms
رعاية الترتيب (ri'āyat al-tartīb): Observance of the prescribed order of actions within the prayer, especially between recitation and ruku', and between sajdahs.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwa): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a verse of sajdah in the Quran; its ruling in prayer is disputed among Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling if a person delays sajda al-tilawah during prayer and remembers it after saying salam?
A) No sajdah al-sahw is required because it is not an original wajib of prayer.
B) Sajdah al-sahw is required because leaving the immediate connection is a wajib.
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
D) He must perform the sajda al-tilawah immediately after salam without sahw.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi prayer, violating the fard order between recitation and ruku' requires repetition of the misplaced action and sahw, while delaying sajda al-tilawah, though disputed by al-Tajnīs, is ruled by the majority of later authorities (al-Khulasa, al-Walwaliji) to require sajdah al-sahw.

Tranquility in Ruku' and Sujud: A Wajib Requiring Sajdah al-Sahw
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tranquility as cause of sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tranquility (tuma'ninah) in salah, distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the correct consequence when it is omitted forgetfully.

Core Idea
Tranquility in ruku' and sujud is wajib; omitting it forgetfully requires sajdah al-sahw, not repetition.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author explains the fifth cause of sajdah al-sahw: the proper performance of prayer pillars, specifically tranquility in ruku' and sujud. While all Hanafi scholars agree that tranquility is required in prayer, they differ on its legal status—whether it is wajib or fard. This distinction has practical consequences for the validity of the prayer and the need for sajdah al-sahw when it is omitted forgetfully.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its disputed status
The act under discussion is tranquility (tuma'ninah) in ruku' and sujud, a component of the proper performance of prayer pillars (ta'dīl al-arkān). The passage notes a difference of opinion on whether it is wajib or sunnah, but the school holds it is wajib.
The term 'wajib' here means obligatory but not integral; the prayer remains valid if omitted but compensation is needed.
2
State the intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani consider tranquility wajib, requiring sajdah al-sahw for its forgetful omission. Abu Yusuf considers it fard (integral), making its omission invalidate the prayer entirely.
This ikhtilaf is within the Hanafi school; the opposing position is not from another madhhab.
3
Understand the practical consequence
If tranquility is wajib, forgetting it triggers sajdah al-sahw. If it is fard, the prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the former.
The same act (tuma'ninah) has different implications based on its categorization.
4
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
When a person forgets to pause calmly in ruku' and sujud, according to the operative Hanafi view, they must perform sajdah al-sahw at the end of the prayer. The prayer is valid and does not need repetition.
This applies to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers, as tranquility is a wajib in all prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس تعديل الأركان وهو الطمأنينة في الركوع والسجود، وقد اختلف في وجوب السجود بتركه بناء على أنه واجب أو سنة، والمذهب الوجوب ولزوم السجود بتركه، وصححه في البدائع. ساهياً، القعدة قال في التجنيس: وهذا التفريع على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن تعديل الأركان فرض عند أبي يوسف. السادس القعود الأول وكذا كل قعدة ليست أخيرة سواء كان في الفرض أو في النفل فإنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها ساهياً.
The fifth: proper performance of pillars (ta'dīl al-arkān), which is tranquility in bowing and prostration. They differed concerning the obligation of sajdah due to omitting it, based on whether it is wajib or sunnah. The school (madhhab) is that it is wajib and sajdah is required for omitting it, and he confirmed this in al-Bada'i'. Forgetfully; the sitting. He said in al-Tajnīs: This branching is according to the statement of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because proper performance of pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The sixth: the first sitting, and likewise every sitting that is not the final one, whether in obligatory or supererogatory prayers, then sajdah al-sahw is required for omitting it forgetfully.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage discusses the fifth cause of sajdah al-sahw: tranquility (tuma'ninah) in ruku' and sujud, which is part of the proper performance of the prayer pillars. The Hanafi scholars differed on its legal nature: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider it wajib (obligatory but not integral), while Abu Yusuf considers it fard (integral). The ruling on sajdah al-sahw depends on this: if it is wajib, forgetting it requires sahw; if it is fard, omitting it invalidates the prayer entirely. The author confirms the school position (madhhab) that tranquility is wajib and sahw is required for its omission, as affirmed in al-Bada'i'. The passage then notes that in al-Tajnīs, the discussion is based on the views of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. The next sentence introduces the sixth cause (first sitting).

Key Terms
تعديل الأركان (ta'dīl al-arkān): Proper performance of the pillars of prayer, specifically tranquility (tuma'ninah) in ruku' and sujud.
الطمأنينة (al-tuma'nīna): The state of calm and stillness in ruku' and sujud, remaining motionless for at least the duration of one tasbih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) No action is needed because tranquility is a sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Tranquility in ruku' and sujud is a wajib in the Hanafi school; forgetting it requires sajdah al-sahw, but the prayer remains valid.

The First Sitting: A Wajib Requiring Sajdah al-Sahw if Omitted
Ruling on forgetting the first sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the first sitting and identify when sajdah al-sahw is required for its omission.

Core Idea
The first sitting is a wajib; omitting it forgetfully requires sajdah al-sahw in both fard and nafl.

The first sitting (al-qu'ūd al-awwal) after the second rak'ah is not a rukn but a wajib. Understanding this distinction is crucial for knowing the consequences of forgetting it. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Recognize that the first sitting is a wajib, not a rukn. It is an obligatory component whose omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation.
Wajib is a binding duty that is less than fard; its omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
2
Determine the consequence of omission
If the first sitting is omitted forgetfully (sahw), the prayer remains valid but sajdah al-sahw must be performed to compensate for the missing wajib.
If omitted intentionally, the prayer becomes invalid (since wajib is still binding), but this case is not covered here.
3
Apply to fard and nafl
The same ruling applies to both obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers that have more than two rak'ahs. For example, in a 4-rak'ah fard or a 4-rak'ah sunnah, forgetting the first sitting requires sajdah al-sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس القعود الأول وكذا كل قعدة ليست أخيرة سواء كان في الفرض أو في النفل فإنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها ساهياً.
The sixth: the first sitting, and likewise every sitting that is not the final one, whether in obligatory or supererogatory prayers, then sajdah al-sahw is required for omitting it forgetfully.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This is a concise ruling stating the sixth cause of sajdah al-sahw: omitting the first sitting (tashahhud) in a prayer that has two sittings (e.g., 3 or 4 rak'ah prayers). This applies to any sitting that is not the final one, including the first sitting in a 4-rak'ah prayer or any intermediate sitting in supererogatory prayers. The ruling is the same for both fard and nafl: if forgotten, sajdah al-sahw is required. The first sitting is a wajib according to the Hanafi school, not a fard, so omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ūd al-awwal): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs; it is a wajib, not a rukn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Prayer invalid, must be repeated
B) Valid, sajdah al-sahw is required
C) Valid, no sajdah is needed
D) The prayer becomes two rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
The first sitting is a wajib; its forgetful omission necessitates sajdah al-sahw in all prayers with more than two rak'ahs.

Seventh Cause of Sahw: The Tashahhud – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains the seventh cause of sahw: omitting any part of the tashahhud requires sahw, with a dispute on its re-performance after salam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the tashahhud forgotten after salam and apply the general rule that a missed wajib not performed after remembrance is treated as intentional omission.

Core Idea
Forgetting tashahhud requires sajdah al-sahw, but returning to recite it after salam is valid (Muhammad) or invalid (Abu Yusuf); the fatwa follows Muhammad, but imams may adopt Abu Yusuf.

In this lesson, we examine a specific cause of sajdah al-sahw: omitting the tashahhud. The Hanafi school considers the tashahhud a wajib; forgetting any part of it necessitates sajdah al-sahw. However, within the school, there is an important dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding what happens when one remembers the missed tashahhud after the final salam. This dispute has practical consequences for imams and individuals. Understanding the issue involves distinguishing between the original cause of sahw and the subsequent action of returning to recite a wajib after the prayer has apparently ended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The tashahhud is a wajib; its omission, even a little, requires sajdah al-sahw. This applies to both the first and second tashahhud.
2
State the consensus and the dispute
All agree that omitting tashahhud requires sahw. The dispute arises when one remembers after salam and chooses to return to recite it.
3
Present Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf holds that returning to recite after salam invalidates the previous sitting. If the salam is said before completing the tashahhud, the prayer becomes invalid.
4
Present Muhammad's view
Muhammad holds that the sitting remains intact; returning to recite is not a disruption. The prayer remains valid, and sajdah al-sahw is performed after completing the tashahhud.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is validity of the prayer. Fatwa is on Muhammad's view for individuals, but imams are advised to follow Abu Yusuf to avoid confusion.
Also note the general principle: if one can act but does not, the omission becomes intentional, and no sajdah is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع التشهد فإنه يجب سجود السهو بتركه ولو قليلاً في ظاهر الرواية لأنه ذكر واحد منظوم فترك بعضه كترك كله ولا فرق بين الأولى أو الثانية، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية: لو ترك قراءة التشهد ساهياً في القعدة الأولى أو الثانية وتذكر بعد السلام يلزمه سجود السهو، وعن أبي يوسف لا يلزمه قالوا: إن كان المصلي إماماً يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن لم يكن إماماً يأخذ بقول محمد وفي فتح القدير: ثم قد لا يتحقق ترك التشهد على وجه يوجب السجود إلا في الأول، أما في التشهد الثاني فإنه لو تذكره بعد السلام يقرأ ثم يسلم ثم يسجد فإن تذكره بعد شيء يقطع البناء لم يتصور إيجاب السجود، ومن فروع هذا أنه لو اشتغل بعد السلام والتذكر به فلما قرأ بعضه سلم قبل تمامه فسدت صلاته عند أبي يوسف لأن بعوده إلى قراءة التشهد ارتفض قعوده، فإذا سلم قبل إتمامه فقد سلم قبل قعوده قدر التشهد وعند محمد تجوز صلاته لأن قعوده ما ارتفض أصلاً لأن محل قراءة التشهد القعدة فلا ضرورة إلى رفضها وعليه الفتوى ا.هـ. وظاهره أنه لو تذكره بعد السلام ولم يقرأ لا يسجد للسهو وبتركه لأنه لما تذكره وأمكنه فعله ولم يفعله صار كأنه تركه عمداً فلا يلزمه السجود وإنما يكون مسيئاً، ولو وجب عليه السجود لتحقق وجوبه بتركه. وعلى هذا كلية أن من ترك واجباً سهواً وأمكنه فعله بعد تذكره فلم يفعله لا سجود عليه كمن تركه عمداً وفي الهداية: ثم ذكر التشهد يحتمل القعدة الأولى والثانية
The seventh: the tashahhud. Sajdah al-sahw is required for omitting it, even a little, according to the apparent transmission, because it is a single organized remembrance; leaving part of it is like leaving all of it, and there is no difference between the first or second (sitting). Hence it is said in al-Zahiriyya: If one forgets to recite the tashahhud in the first or second sitting and remembers after salam, sajdah al-sahw is required of him. And from Abu Yusuf, it is not required. They said: If the praying person is an imam, he takes the statement of Abu Yusuf; if not an imam, he takes the statement of Muhammad. In Fath al-Qadir: Then the omission of tashahhud in a way that obligates sajdah may not be actualized except in the first (sitting). As for the second tashahhud, if he remembers it after salam, he recites then says salam then prostrates; but if he remembers after something that cuts off the building (of the prayer), the obligation of sajdah is inconceivable. Among its branches: if he engages after salam and remembrance in it (the tashahhud), and when he recited part of it he said salam before completing it, his prayer is invalid according to Abu Yusuf because his return to reciting tashahhud invalidates his sitting; so if he says salam before completing it, he has said salam before his sitting of the measure of tashahhud. According to Muhammad, his prayer is valid because his sitting was not invalidated at all, since the place of reciting tashahhud is the sitting, so there is no need to invalidate it; and upon this is the fatwa. Externally, it appears that if he remembers after salam and does not recite, he does not prostrate for sahw and by leaving it, because when he remembered and was able to do it but did not, it became as if he left it intentionally, so sajdah is not required; he is only a wrongdoer. And if sajdah were required, it would be established by its omission. Upon this is a general rule: whoever leaves a wajib forgetfully and is able to do it after remembering but does not do it, there is no sajdah upon him, like one who leaves it intentionally. In al-Hidaya: Then mentioning tashahhud may apply to the first and second sitting.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage discusses the seventh cause of sajdah al-sahw: omitting the tashahhud. The tashahhud is a wajib; forgetting any part of it requires sajdah al-sahw because it is a single organized act of remembrance. This applies equally to the first and second tashahhud. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that forgetting the tashahhud does not require sajdah after salam, while Muhammad holds it does. The practice is that imams follow Abu Yusuf (to avoid confusion for the congregation), while non-imams follow Muhammad. A detailed scenario is given: if someone remembers the tashahhud after salam and begins to recite it but then says salam before completing it, Abu Yusuf considers the prayer invalid because the act of returning to the tashahhud effectively nullified the original sitting, so he has not actually performed a valid sitting. Muhammad considers the prayer valid because the tashahhud belongs to the sitting and does not require invalidating the previous sitting. The fatwa is on Muhammad's view. Finally, a general principle is derived: if one forgets a wajib and has the opportunity to perform it but deliberately chooses not to, sajdah al-sahw is not required and he is considered sinful (the omission becomes intentional). This principle is applied to tashahhud.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of the testimony of faith (attahiyyat) during the sitting of prayer; it is a wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Muhammad), what happens if a person who is praying alone forgets the tashahhud in the first sitting, remembers after the final salam, and then immediately recites the tashahhud and performs sajdah al-sahw?
A) The prayer is invalid because the salam had already ended it.
B) The prayer is valid, and the tashahhud and sajdah are completed correctly.
C) Only sajdah al-sahw is required, no need to recite tashahhud.
D) The prayer is valid but he must repeat the tashahhud in a new prayer.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the tashahhud requires sajdah al-sahw; but if one remembers after salam and has the opportunity to recite but chooses not to, no sajdah is needed and the omission is treated as intentional.

Causes 5-6: Adjusting Pillars and the First Sitting
Enumeration of the fifth and sixth causes of sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that forgetting the first sitting or not performing tuma'nina (adjusting pillars) requires sujud al-sahw according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and explain the ikhtilaf with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Forgetting a wajib like the first sitting or posture in prayer triggers sujud al-sahw, but if it is fard, no sujud.

The author continues enumerating the causes of sujud al-sahw. The fifth cause is neglecting to adjust the pillars (tuma'nina) in prayer, and the sixth is forgetting the first sitting. These are considered wajib in the Hanafi school, and forgetting them requires the prostration of forgetfulness. However, note the difference of opinion among the three imams on the status of tuma'nina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each cause, determine whether the act is wajib or fard. The ruling hinges on this: if wajib, sujud is required; if fard, sujud is not required.
2
Locate the basis
The matn states that sujud is required for these causes. The commentary clarifies that Abu Yusuf considers tuma'nina fard, so no sujud is needed in his view.
The fifth cause is based on the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
3
Note the practical implication
For the first sitting, all agree it is wajib, so forgetting it always requires sujud in the Hanafi school.

قال في التجنيس : وهذا التفريع على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن تعديل الأركان فرض عند أبي يوسف السادس القعود الأول وكذا كل قعدة ليست أخيرة سواء كان في الفرض أو في النفل فإنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها ساهياً . السابع التشهد فإنه يجب سجود السهو بتركه ولو قليلاً في ظاهر الرواية لأنه ذكر واحد منظوم فترك بعضه كترك كله ولا فرق بين الأولى أو الثانية، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية : لو ترك قراءة التشهد ساهياً في القعدة الأولى أو - الثانية وتذكر بعد السلام يلزمه سجود السهو، وعن أبي يوسف لا يلزمه قالوا : إن كان المصلي إماماً يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن لم يكن إماماً يأخذ بقول محمد وفي فتح القدير: ثم قد لا يتحقق ترك التشهد على وجه يوجب السجود إلا في الأول، أما في التشهد الثاني فإنه لو تذكره بعد السلام يقرأ ثم يسلم ثم يسجد فإن تذكره بعد شيء يقطع البناء لم يتصور إيجاب السجود، ومن فروع هذا أنه لو اشتغل بعد السلام والتذكر به فلما قرأ بعضه سلم قبل تمامه فسدت صلاته عند أبي يوسف لأن بعوده إلى قراءة التشهد ارتفض قعوده، فإذا سلم قبل إتمامه فقد سلم قبل قعوده قدر التشهد وعند محمد تجوز صلاته لأن قعوده ما ارتفض أصلاً لأن محل قراءة التشهد القعدة فلا ضرورة إلى رفضها وعليه الفتوى ا.هـ. وظاهره أنه لو تذكره بعد السلام ولم يقرأ لا يسجد للسهو وبتركه لأنه لما تذكره وأمكنه فعله ولم يفعله صار كأنه تركه عمداً فلا يلزمه السجود وإنما يكون مسيئاً، ولو وجب عليه السجود لتحقق وجوبه بتركه. وعلى هذا كلية أن من ترك واجباً سهواً وأمكنه فعله بعد تذكره فلم يفعله لا سجود عليه كمن تركه عمداً وفي الهداية : ثم ذكر التشهد يحتمل القعدة الأولى والثانية

والقراءة فيهما وكل ذلك واجب وفيها سجدة هو الصحيح، واعترض عليه بالقعدة الأخيرة فإنها فرض لا واجب. فأجاب في المعراج بأن المراد غيرها إذا لتخصيص شائع بقرينة ذكره لها سابقاً أنها فرض وما أجاب به في غاية البيان من حمل الترك فيها على تأخيرها فاسد لأنه أراد حقيقة الترك في غيرها، فلو أراد التأخير فيها لزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وكذا لو أراد بالواجب حينئذ الفرض فيها والواجب الاصطلاحي في غيرها وهو جمع كذلك. كذا في الغاية . .. ورده في الكافي بأن الممنوع اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظ واحد وهو لم يتعرض للإرادة بل قال : يحتمل هذا وذاك ولا فساد كاحتمال القرء الحيض والطهر كما في المجتبي وغيره. وما في النهاية من أن الأوجه فيه أن يحمل على رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة بأنه تجوز الصلاة بدون القعدة الأخيرة ليس بأوجه لأنها رواية ضعيفة جداً لأنهم نقلوا الإجماع على فرضيتها كما قدمناه، والظاهر أنه سهو وقع من صاحب الهداية. الثامن لفظ السلام ولا يتصور إيجاب السجود بتركه لأنه بعد القعود الأخير إذا لم يأت بمنافٍ فإنه يسلم، وإن أتى بمنافٍ فلا سجود ولهذا قال في التجنيس والسهو عن السلام يوجب سجوداً السهو والسهو عنه أن يطيل القعدة يقع أنه خرج من الصلاة ثم يعلم ذلك فيسلم ويسجد لأنه أخر واجباً أو ركناً على اختلاف الأصلين ا هـ .
عنده
وإنما يتصور إيجابه بتأخيره كما قدمناه وذكرنا في باب صفة الصلاة أن الواجب منه التسليمة الأولى وهي السلام دون عليكم ورحمة الله. وفي البدائع : إنه لم سلم عن يساره أولاً لا سهو عليه لأنه ترك السنة. وفي الظهيرية : وإذا سلم الرجل عن يمينه وسها عن التسليمة الأخرى فما دام في المسجد يأتي بالأخرى وإن استدبر القبلة، وعامة المشايخ على أنه لا يأتي متى استدبر القبلة ا هـ . التاسع قنوت الوتر وقدمنا أنه لا يختص بدعاء وأنه لا يعود إليه لو ركع على الصحيح كما في المجتبي وغيره فحينئذ يتحقق تركه بالركوع وأنه سنة عندهما كالوتر فالوجوب بتركه إنما هو قوله فقط. وفي فتح القدير: ولو قرأ القنوت في الثالثة ونسي قراءة الفاتحة أو السورة أو كليهما فتذكر بعد ما ركع قام وقرأ وأعاد القنوت لأنه والركوع رجع إلى محله قبله ويسجد للسهو بخلاف ما لو نسي سجدة التلاوة ومحلها فتذكرها في الركوع أو السجود أو القعود فإنه ينحط لها ثم يعود إلى ما كان فيه فيعيده استحباباً ا ومما ألحق به تكبيره وجزم الشارح بوجوب السجود بتركها. وذكر في الظهيرية أنه لو ترك تكبيرة القنوت فإنه لا رواية لهذا، وقيل يجب سجود السهو اعتباراً بتكبيرات العيد، وقيل لا يجب ا هـ . وينبغي ترجيح عدم الوجوب لأنه الأصل ولا دليل عليه بخلاف تكبيرات العيد فإن دليل الوجوب المواظبة مع قوله تعالى ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام
هـ.
واجب آخر، وهنا وإن أمكنه العود إلى قراءة الفاتحة يلزمه تأخير الركوع تأمل .
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. The obligation of prostration by leaving [an act] is based on it being wajib or sunnah, and the madhhab is obligation and necessary prostration by leaving it, and it was corrected in al-Bada'i'. 'Forgotfully, the sitting'. He said in al-Tajnis: This branching is on the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because adjusting the pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The sixth: the first sitting, and likewise every sitting that is not the last, whether in fard or nafl, then it necessitates sujud al-sahw by leaving it forgetfully. The seventh: the tashahhud, for sujud al-sahw is necessary by leaving it, even a little in the apparent narration because it is a single organized dhikr, so leaving some is like leaving all, and there is no difference between first or second. Therefore it is said in al-Zahiriyya: If one forgetfully leaves reciting tashahhud in the first or second sitting and remembers after salam, sujud al-sahw is necessary. From Abu Yusuf: it is not necessary. They said: If the praying person is an imam, he takes the saying of Abu Yusuf; if he is not an imam, he takes the saying of Muhammad. In Fath al-Qadir: Then the leaving of tashahhud in a way that necessitates sujud is only realized in the first [sitting]; as for the second tashahhud, if he remembers after salam, he recites then salams then prostrates; if he remembers after something that cuts off the building, the obligation of sujud is not conceivable. Among its branches: if after salam and remembering he occupies himself, and when he recited some of it he salamed before completing it, his prayer is invalid according to Abu Yusuf because by returning to reciting tashahhud his sitting was nullified; so if he salamed before completing it, he salamed before his sitting was of the measure of tashahhud. According to Muhammad, his prayer is valid because his sitting was not nullified at all, because the place of reciting tashahhud is the sitting, so there is no necessity to nullify it, and upon this is the fatwa. End quote. Its apparent meaning: if he remembers after salam and does not recite, he does not prostrate for forgetfulness by leaving it, because when he remembered and could do it but did not, it becomes as if he left it intentionally, so sujud is not necessary and he is only sinful. And if sujud were necessary for him, its obligation would be realized by leaving it. Upon this is a general rule: whoever forgetfully leaves a wajib and can do it after remembering but does not, there is no sujud upon him, like one who leaves it intentionally. In al-Hidayah: Then mentioning tashahhud may refer to the first and second sitting. ... The eighth: the wording of salam, and the obligation of sujud by leaving it is not conceivable because after the last sitting, if he does not do something contradictory, he salams; if he does something contradictory, there is no sujud. Therefore al-Tajnis said: forgetfulness about salam necessitates sujud al-sahw, and forgetfulness about it means that he lengthens the sitting, thinking that he has left the prayer, then learns that [he is still in it], so he salams and prostrates because he delayed an obligatory or pillar according to the two different principles. End quote. Rather, its obligation is conceivable by delaying it as we have stated. We mentioned in the chapter on description of prayer that the wajib of it is the first taslima, which is 'al-salam' not 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah'. In al-Bada'i': if he salamed to his left first, there is no sujud upon him because he left a sunnah. In al-Zahiriyya: if a man salamed to his right and forgot the other taslima, as long as he is in the mosque he performs the other, even if he has turned his back to the qibla. The majority of mashayikh hold that he does not perform it once he has turned his back to the qibla. End quote. The ninth: qunut of witr. We have stated that it is not specific to a du'a, and that he does not return to it if he has bowed according to the correct view as in al-Mujtaba and others. Thus its leaving is realized by bowing, and it is sunnah according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] like the witr itself, so the obligation by leaving it is only his saying [Abu Hanifa's]. In Fath al-Qadir: if he recited qunut in the third rak'a and forgot to recite the Fatiha or sura or both, then remembered after he bowed, he stands and recites and repeats the qunut because the bowing returned to its place before it, and he prostrates for forgetfulness. Unlike if he forgot a prostration of recitation and its place, then remembered in bowing or prostration or sitting: he goes down for it, then returns to what he was doing and repeats it as a recommendable act. End quote. Among what is annexed to it is its takbir. The commentator affirmed the obligation of sujud by leaving it. It is mentioned in al-Zahiriyya: if one leaves the takbir of qunut, there is no narration for this. It is said: sujud al-sahw is necessary by analogy to the takbirs of Eid. It is said: not necessary. End quote. It should be preferred that it is not obligatory because it is the original, and there is no evidence for it, unlike the takbirs of Eid for which the evidence of obligation is continuity with the verse 'and they mention the name of Allah in days'. End quote. Another wajib: here, even if he can return to reciting Fatiha, delaying bowing is necessary. Reflect.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This is an expansion on the causes of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by affirming that the madhhab holds sujud al-sahw as wajib (obligatory) when a wajib element is left forgetfully, contrary to those who consider it sunnah. He then enumerates several causes from the fifth to the ninth.

The fifth cause: تعديل الأركان (adjusting the pillars) — this refers to performing the postures calmly with proper pause (tuma'nina). The author notes that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, leaving it requires sujud, while Abu Yusuf considers it fard (so no sujud needed for leaving a fard by forgetting? Actually, the text says: 'because adjusting the pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf' implying that since it is fard, sujud is not required for forgetting it? But the author is clarifying the basis. The passage is a bit obscure.

The sixth cause: القعود الأول (the first sitting). This includes every sitting that is not the final one, whether in fard or nafl prayers. Forgetting this sitting requires sujud.

The seventh cause: التشهد (the tashahhud). Forgetting any part of the tashahhud, even a small part, requires sujud because it is considered a single organized dhikr. There is an ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf holds that if one remembers after salam, sujud is not required, while Muhammad holds it is required. The author mentions a fatwa: an imam should follow Abu Yusuf's view (to avoid confusion for the congregation), and a non-imam should follow Muhammad's view. Further branches discuss the case where one starts reciting tashahhud after salam and then salams prematurely. The author then states a general rule: if one forgets a wajib, remembers it, and can still perform it without breaking the prayer, but deliberately chooses not to, then no sujud is required because it becomes like an intentional omission. This rule is later critiqued by al-Nahr, who gives the counterexample of forgetting Fatiha and not returning to it even though possible — sujud would be required. The author responds by qualifying 'possible' as possible without causing another wajib to be missed.

The eighth cause: لفظ السلام (the wording of salam). Forgetting the salam itself does not require sujud; rather, sujud is only required if one delays the salam (e.g., remains sitting thinking he has finished). The required salam is the first 'al-salam' not 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah'. If one salams to the left first, it is a sunnah omission, not requiring sujud.

The ninth cause: قنوت الوتر (qunut of witr). Qunut is sunnah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but wajib according to Abu Hanifa. Forgetting qunut and bowing means it is omitted, and sujud is required on Abu Hanifa's view. If one forgets Fatiha and remembers after bowing, he returns to recite and repeats qunut. The takbir of qunut is also discussed: the commentator holds sujud required for leaving it, but there is no explicit narration; the preferred view is that it is not obligatory.

The passage ends with a note about another wajib and the need to delay bowing if one can return to Fatiha without causing another wajib to be missed.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer when a wajib element is omitted or delayed.
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting in a prayer of three or more rak'at, after the second rak'a.
تعديل الأركان (ta'dil al-arkan): Performing the physical postures of prayer with calm and proper pause (tuma'nina).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on forgetting the first sitting in a fard prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) No sujud, prayer is invalid.
B) Sujud al-sahw is required.
C) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
D) Sujud is recommended but not obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the first sitting or not performing tuma'nina (according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is a wajib omission, so sujud al-sahw is required.

The Seventh Cause: Forgetting Tashahhud
Detailed treatment of the seventh cause (tashahhud) with intra-madhhab dispute and branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on sujud for forgotten tashahhud and state the mufta bihi distinction between imam and non-imam.

Core Idea
Forgetting tashahhud triggers sujud, unless you are an imam who remembers after salam — then follow Abu Yusuf's view and omit sujud.

The seventh cause of sujud al-sahw is forgetting the tashahhud. This cause involves a detailed dispute within the Hanafi school between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The author presents both views and the practical fatwa distinction between an imam and a non-imam. Additionally, complex branches arise when one remembers after salam and begins reciting but then salams prematurely.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Tashahhud is wajib; forgetting it in any sitting requires sujud al-sahw according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
The proof is that tashahhud is a single organized dhikr.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that if one remembers after salam, no sujud is needed because it becomes like an intentional omission.
3
Apply the tarjih
For an imam, take Abu Yusuf's view to avoid confusion; for a non-imam, take Muhammad's view.
This is the fatwa as stated in the text.
4
Analyze the branch
If after salam one starts reciting tashahhud then salams prematurely, Abu Yusuf says prayer invalid; Muhammad says valid with sujud.
The fatwa is on Muhammad's view.

ساهياً،
القعدة
قال في التجنيس : وهذا التفريع على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن تعديل الأركان فرض عند أبي يوسف السادس القعود الأول وكذا كل قعدة ليست أخيرة سواء كان في الفرض أو في النفل فإنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها ساهياً . السابع التشهد فإنه يجب سجود السهو بتركه ولو قليلاً في ظاهر الرواية لأنه ذكر واحد منظوم فترك بعضه كترك كله ولا فرق بين الأولى أو الثانية، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية : لو ترك قراءة التشهد ساهياً في القعدة الأولى أو - الثانية وتذكر بعد السلام يلزمه سجود السهو، وعن أبي يوسف لا يلزمه قالوا : إن كان المصلي إماماً يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن لم يكن إماماً يأخذ بقول محمد وفي فتح القدير: ثم قد لا يتحقق ترك التشهد على وجه يوجب السجود إلا في الأول، أما في التشهد الثاني فإنه لو تذكره بعد السلام يقرأ ثم يسلم ثم يسجد فإن تذكره بعد شيء يقطع البناء لم يتصور إيجاب السجود، ومن فروع هذا أنه لو اشتغل بعد السلام والتذكر به فلما قرأ بعضه سلم قبل تمامه فسدت صلاته عند أبي يوسف لأن بعوده إلى قراءة التشهد ارتفض قعوده، فإذا سلم قبل إتمامه فقد سلم قبل قعوده قدر التشهد وعند محمد تجوز صلاته لأن قعوده ما ارتفض أصلاً لأن محل قراءة التشهد القعدة فلا ضرورة إلى رفضها وعليه الفتوى ا.هـ. وظاهره أنه لو تذكره بعد السلام ولم يقرأ لا يسجد للسهو وبتركه لأنه لما تذكره وأمكنه فعله ولم يفعله صار كأنه تركه عمداً فلا يلزمه السجود وإنما يكون مسيئاً، ولو وجب عليه السجود لتحقق وجوبه بتركه. وعلى هذا كلية أن من ترك واجباً سهواً وأمكنه فعله بعد تذكره فلم يفعله لا سجود عليه كمن تركه عمداً وفي الهداية : ثم ذكر التشهد يحتمل القعدة الأولى والثانية
tصير
تأمل قوله : (الخامس تعديل الأركان الخ) أقول : قال في الضياء المعنوي شرح مقدمة الغزنوي : إن في ترك الطمأنينة لا يجب سجود السهو لأنها واجبة للغير لأنها شرعت مكملة لفرض، وهذا دليل السنة فشابهت السنة من هذا الوجه وإن كانت واجبة وبترك السنة لا يجب سجود السهو نص على ذلك في عمدة المصلي ا هـ . تأمل . لكن قدم المؤلف في واجبات الصلاة التصريح بلزوم وجوب السهو بتركها عن القنية والمحيط، وكذا في الرفع من الركوع والسجود قوله : ( يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف) لعل وجهه أنه إذا تذكر بعد السلام يكون قد تفرق بعض الجماعة أو يحصل لهم اشتبتاه فالأسهل الأخذ بقول أبي يوسف بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن إماماً تأمل قوله : (وظاهره أنه لو تذكره الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر وذلك أن تركه إنما يتحقق إذا أتى بما يمنع البناء وفي هذه الحالة يمتنع السجود عن كل واجب ترك لا أن امتناعه لتركه إياه عمداً والكلية ممنوعة ألا ترى أنه لو تذكر في ركوعه أنه ترك الفاتحة فلم يعد مع إمكانه وجب عليه السجود ا . أقول : قد يجاب عن المنع بأن المراد إمكانه على وجه لا يؤدي إلى ترك
والقراءة فيهما وكل ذلك واجب وفيها سجدة هو الصحيح، واعترض عليه بالقعدة الأخيرة فإنها فرض لا واجب. فأجاب في المعراج بأن المراد غيرها إذا لتخصيص شائع بقرينة ذكره لها سابقاً أنها فرض وما أجاب به في غاية البيان من حمل الترك فيها على تأخيرها فاسد لأنه أراد حقيقة الترك في غيرها، فلو أراد التأخير فيها لزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وكذا لو أراد بالواجب حينئذ الفرض فيها والواجب الاصطلاحي في غيرها وهو جمع كذلك. كذا في الغاية . .. ورده في الكافي بأن الممنوع اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظ واحد وهو لم يتعرض للإرادة بل قال : يحتمل هذا وذاك ولا فساد كاحتمال القرء الحيض والطهر كما في المجتبي وغيره. وما في النهاية من أن الأوجه فيه أن يحمل على رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة بأنه تجوز الصلاة بدون القعدة الأخيرة ليس بأوجه لأنها رواية ضعيفة جداً لأنهم نقلوا الإجماع على فرضيتها كما قدمناه، والظاهر أنه سهو وقع من صاحب الهداية. الثامن لفظ السلام ولا يتصور إيجاب السجود بتركه لأنه بعد القعود الأخير إذا لم يأت بمنافٍ فإنه يسلم، وإن أتى بمنافٍ فلا سجود ولهذا قال في التجنيس والسهو عن السلام يوجب سجوداً السهو والسهو عنه أن يطيل القعدة يقع أنه خرج من الصلاة ثم يعلم ذلك فيسلم ويسجد لأنه أخر واجباً أو ركناً على اختلاف الأصلين ا هـ .
عنده
وإنما يتصور إيجابه بتأخيره كما قدمناه وذكرنا في باب صفة الصلاة أن الواجب منه التسليمة الأولى وهي السلام دون عليكم ورحمة الله. وفي البدائع : إنه لم سلم عن يساره أولاً لا سهو عليه لأنه ترك السنة. وفي الظهيرية : وإذا سلم الرجل عن يمينه وسها عن التسليمة الأخرى فما دام في المسجد يأتي بالأخرى وإن استدبر القبلة، وعامة المشايخ على أنه لا يأتي متى استدبر القبلة ا هـ . التاسع قنوت الوتر وقدمنا أنه لا يختص بدعاء وأنه لا يعود إليه لو ركع على الصحيح كما في المجتبي وغيره فحينئذ يتحقق تركه بالركوع وأنه سنة عندهما كالوتر فالوجوب بتركه إنما هو قوله فقط. وفي فتح القدير: ولو قرأ القنوت في الثالثة ونسي قراءة الفاتحة أو السورة أو كليهما فتذكر بعد ما ركع قام وقرأ وأعاد القنوت لأنه والركوع رجع إلى محله قبله ويسجد للسهو بخلاف ما لو نسي سجدة التلاوة ومحلها فتذكرها في الركوع أو السجود أو القعود فإنه ينحط لها ثم يعود إلى ما كان فيه فيعيده استحباباً ا ومما ألحق به تكبيره وجزم الشارح بوجوب السجود بتركها. وذكر في الظهيرية أنه لو ترك تكبيرة القنوت فإنه لا رواية لهذا، وقيل يجب سجود السهو اعتباراً بتكبيرات العيد، وقيل لا يجب ا هـ . وينبغي ترجيح عدم الوجوب لأنه الأصل ولا دليل عليه بخلاف تكبيرات العيد فإن دليل الوجوب المواظبة مع قوله تعالى ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام
هـ.
واجب آخر، وهنا وإن أمكنه العود إلى قراءة الفاتحة يلزمه تأخير الركوع تأمل .
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. The obligation of prostration by leaving [an act] is based on it being wajib or sunnah, and the madhhab is obligation and necessary prostration by leaving it, and it was corrected in al-Bada'i'. 'Forgotfully, the sitting'. He said in al-Tajnis: This branching is on the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because adjusting the pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The sixth: the first sitting, and likewise every sitting that is not the last, whether in fard or nafl, then it necessitates sujud al-sahw by leaving it forgetfully. The seventh: the tashahhud, for sujud al-sahw is necessary by leaving it, even a little in the apparent narration because it is a single organized dhikr, so leaving some is like leaving all, and there is no difference between first or second. Therefore it is said in al-Zahiriyya: If one forgetfully leaves reciting tashahhud in the first or second sitting and remembers after salam, sujud al-sahw is necessary. From Abu Yusuf: it is not necessary. They said: If the praying person is an imam, he takes the saying of Abu Yusuf; if he is not an imam, he takes the saying of Muhammad. In Fath al-Qadir: Then the leaving of tashahhud in a way that necessitates sujud is only realized in the first [sitting]; as for the second tashahhud, if he remembers after salam, he recites then salams then prostrates; if he remembers after something that cuts off the building, the obligation of sujud is not conceivable. Among its branches: if after salam and remembering he occupies himself, and when he recited some of it he salamed before completing it, his prayer is invalid according to Abu Yusuf because by returning to reciting tashahhud his sitting was nullified; so if he salamed before completing it, he salamed before his sitting was of the measure of tashahhud. According to Muhammad, his prayer is valid because his sitting was not nullified at all, because the place of reciting tashahhud is the sitting, so there is no necessity to nullify it, and upon this is the fatwa. End quote. Its apparent meaning: if he remembers after salam and does not recite, he does not prostrate for forgetfulness by leaving it, because when he remembered and could do it but did not, it becomes as if he left it intentionally, so sujud is not necessary and he is only sinful. And if sujud were necessary for him, its obligation would be realized by leaving it. Upon this is a general rule: whoever forgetfully leaves a wajib and can do it after remembering but does not, there is no sujud upon him, like one who leaves it intentionally. In al-Hidayah: Then mentioning tashahhud may refer to the first and second sitting. ... The eighth: the wording of salam, and the obligation of sujud by leaving it is not conceivable because after the last sitting, if he does not do something contradictory, he salams; if he does something contradictory, there is no sujud. Therefore al-Tajnis said: forgetfulness about salam necessitates sujud al-sahw, and forgetfulness about it means that he lengthens the sitting, thinking that he has left the prayer, then learns that [he is still in it], so he salams and prostrates because he delayed an obligatory or pillar according to the two different principles. End quote. Rather, its obligation is conceivable by delaying it as we have stated. We mentioned in the chapter on description of prayer that the wajib of it is the first taslima, which is 'al-salam' not 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah'. In al-Bada'i': if he salamed to his left first, there is no sujud upon him because he left a sunnah. In al-Zahiriyya: if a man salamed to his right and forgot the other taslima, as long as he is in the mosque he performs the other, even if he has turned his back to the qibla. The majority of mashayikh hold that he does not perform it once he has turned his back to the qibla. End quote. The ninth: qunut of witr. We have stated that it is not specific to a du'a, and that he does not return to it if he has bowed according to the correct view as in al-Mujtaba and others. Thus its leaving is realized by bowing, and it is sunnah according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] like the witr itself, so the obligation by leaving it is only his saying [Abu Hanifa's]. In Fath al-Qadir: if he recited qunut in the third rak'a and forgot to recite the Fatiha or sura or both, then remembered after he bowed, he stands and recites and repeats the qunut because the bowing returned to its place before it, and he prostrates for forgetfulness. Unlike if he forgot a prostration of recitation and its place, then remembered in bowing or prostration or sitting: he goes down for it, then returns to what he was doing and repeats it as a recommendable act. End quote. Among what is annexed to it is its takbir. The commentator affirmed the obligation of sujud by leaving it. It is mentioned in al-Zahiriyya: if one leaves the takbir of qunut, there is no narration for this. It is said: sujud al-sahw is necessary by analogy to the takbirs of Eid. It is said: not necessary. End quote. It should be preferred that it is not obligatory because it is the original, and there is no evidence for it, unlike the takbirs of Eid for which the evidence of obligation is continuity with the verse 'and they mention the name of Allah in days'. End quote. Another wajib: here, even if he can return to reciting Fatiha, delaying bowing is necessary. Reflect.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This is an expansion on the causes of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by affirming that the madhhab holds sujud al-sahw as wajib (obligatory) when a wajib element is left forgetfully, contrary to those who consider it sunnah. He then enumerates several causes from the fifth to the ninth.

The fifth cause: تعديل الأركان (adjusting the pillars) — this refers to performing the postures calmly with proper pause (tuma'nina). The author notes that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, leaving it requires sujud, while Abu Yusuf considers it fard (so no sujud needed for leaving a fard by forgetting? Actually, the text says: 'because adjusting the pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf' implying that since it is fard, sujud is not required for forgetting it? But the author is clarifying the basis. The passage is a bit obscure.

The sixth cause: القعود الأول (the first sitting). This includes every sitting that is not the final one, whether in fard or nafl prayers. Forgetting this sitting requires sujud.

The seventh cause: التشهد (the tashahhud). Forgetting any part of the tashahhud, even a small part, requires sujud because it is considered a single organized dhikr. There is an ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf holds that if one remembers after salam, sujud is not required, while Muhammad holds it is required. The author mentions a fatwa: an imam should follow Abu Yusuf's view (to avoid confusion for the congregation), and a non-imam should follow Muhammad's view. Further branches discuss the case where one starts reciting tashahhud after salam and then salams prematurely. The author then states a general rule: if one forgets a wajib, remembers it, and can still perform it without breaking the prayer, but deliberately chooses not to, then no sujud is required because it becomes like an intentional omission. This rule is later critiqued by al-Nahr, who gives the counterexample of forgetting Fatiha and not returning to it even though possible — sujud would be required. The author responds by qualifying 'possible' as possible without causing another wajib to be missed.

The eighth cause: لفظ السلام (the wording of salam). Forgetting the salam itself does not require sujud; rather, sujud is only required if one delays the salam (e.g., remains sitting thinking he has finished). The required salam is the first 'al-salam' not 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah'. If one salams to the left first, it is a sunnah omission, not requiring sujud.

The ninth cause: قنوت الوتر (qunut of witr). Qunut is sunnah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but wajib according to Abu Hanifa. Forgetting qunut and bowing means it is omitted, and sujud is required on Abu Hanifa's view. If one forgets Fatiha and remembers after bowing, he returns to recite and repeats qunut. The takbir of qunut is also discussed: the commentator holds sujud required for leaving it, but there is no explicit narration; the preferred view is that it is not obligatory.

The passage ends with a note about another wajib and the need to delay bowing if one can return to Fatiha without causing another wajib to be missed.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer, consisting of 'At-tahiyyat lillah...'
ذكر واحد منظوم (dhikr wahid manzum): A single organized dhikr; the tashahhud is treated as one unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi fatwa, if an imam forgets the second tashahhud and remembers after salam, what should he do?
A) Perform sujud al-sahw.
B) Not perform sujud.
C) Repeat the prayer.
D) Recite tashahhud after salam and then sujud.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting tashahhud requires sujud, but the imam is excused to avoid confusion; the general rule: if one can perform the missed wajib after remembering but does not, no sujud.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
7 min
Causes 8-9: Salam and Qunut of Witr
Enumeration of the eighth and ninth causes of sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why forgetting the salam itself does not require sujud but delaying it does, and state the ruling on qunut of witr.

Core Idea
Forgetting the salam does not trigger sujud, only its delay; qunut of witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and requires sujud if omitted.

The final two causes in this section cover the salam (greeting of peace) and the qunut of witr. The author clarifies that the salam itself is wajib, but its complete omission is not a cause for sujud because the prayer is still valid? Actually, if one completely omits salam, the prayer is incomplete and must be repeated? The text says forgetting the salam is not conceivable for sujud because if no contradictory act, he eventually salams. Only delaying the salam (thinking prayer ended) requires sujud. For qunut, there is a difference of opinion: Abu Hanifa considers it wajib, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah. Forgetting qunut thus requires sujud according to Abu Hanifa only.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish forgetting salam from delaying it
Forgetting the salam entirely (e.g., after salam thinking it's done but actually not) is not a cause for sujud because the prayer continues. Delaying the salam (sitting too long thinking finished) requires sujud.
The text says: 'وإنما يتصور إيجابه بتأخيره'.
2
Identify the wajib part of salam
The wajib is the first 'al-salam'; 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah' is sunnah. Saluting to the left first is a sunnah omission.
3
Analyze the qunut of witr
Qunut is wajib according to Abu Hanifa, sunnah according to the two companions. Forgetting it and bowing realizes its leaving, requiring sujud on Abu Hanifa's view.
The takbir of qunut is annexed; the preferred view is that it is not obligatory.

باب سجود السهو
وجوب السجود بتركه بناء على أنه واجب أو سنة، والمذهب الوجوب ولزوم السجود بتركه ا، وصححه في البدائع .
ساهياً،
القعدة
قال في التجنيس : وهذا التفريع على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد لأن تعديل الأركان فرض عند أبي يوسف السادس القعود الأول وكذا كل قعدة ليست أخيرة سواء كان في الفرض أو في النفل فإنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها ساهياً . السابع التشهد فإنه يجب سجود السهو بتركه ولو قليلاً في ظاهر الرواية لأنه ذكر واحد منظوم فترك بعضه كترك كله ولا فرق بين الأولى أو الثانية، ولهذا قال في الظهيرية : لو ترك قراءة التشهد ساهياً في القعدة الأولى أو - الثانية وتذكر بعد السلام يلزمه سجود السهو، وعن أبي يوسف لا يلزمه قالوا : إن كان المصلي إماماً يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف، وإن لم يكن إماماً يأخذ بقول محمد وفي فتح القدير: ثم قد لا يتحقق ترك التشهد على وجه يوجب السجود إلا في الأول، أما في التشهد الثاني فإنه لو تذكره بعد السلام يقرأ ثم يسلم ثم يسجد فإن تذكره بعد شيء يقطع البناء لم يتصور إيجاب السجود، ومن فروع هذا أنه لو اشتغل بعد السلام والتذكر به فلما قرأ بعضه سلم قبل تمامه فسدت صلاته عند أبي يوسف لأن بعوده إلى قراءة التشهد ارتفض قعوده، فإذا سلم قبل إتمامه فقد سلم قبل قعوده قدر التشهد وعند محمد تجوز صلاته لأن قعوده ما ارتفض أصلاً لأن محل قراءة التشهد القعدة فلا ضرورة إلى رفضها وعليه الفتوى ا.هـ. وظاهره أنه لو تذكره بعد السلام ولم يقرأ لا يسجد للسهو وبتركه لأنه لما تذكره وأمكنه فعله ولم يفعله صار كأنه تركه عمداً فلا يلزمه السجود وإنما يكون مسيئاً، ولو وجب عليه السجود لتحقق وجوبه بتركه. وعلى هذا كلية أن من ترك واجباً سهواً وأمكنه فعله بعد تذكره فلم يفعله لا سجود عليه كمن تركه عمداً وفي الهداية : ثم ذكر التشهد يحتمل القعدة الأولى والثانية
tصير
تأمل قوله : (الخامس تعديل الأركان الخ) أقول : قال في الضياء المعنوي شرح مقدمة الغزنوي : إن في ترك الطمأنينة لا يجب سجود السهو لأنها واجبة للغير لأنها شرعت مكملة لفرض، وهذا دليل السنة فشابهت السنة من هذا الوجه وإن كانت واجبة وبترك السنة لا يجب سجود السهو نص على ذلك في عمدة المصلي ا هـ . تأمل . لكن قدم المؤلف في واجبات الصلاة التصريح بلزوم وجوب السهو بتركها عن القنية والمحيط، وكذا في الرفع من الركوع والسجود قوله : ( يأخذ بقول أبي يوسف) لعل وجهه أنه إذا تذكر بعد السلام يكون قد تفرق بعض الجماعة أو يحصل لهم اشتبتاه فالأسهل الأخذ بقول أبي يوسف بخلاف ما إذا لم يكن إماماً تأمل قوله : (وظاهره أنه لو تذكره الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر وذلك أن تركه إنما يتحقق إذا أتى بما يمنع البناء وفي هذه الحالة يمتنع السجود عن كل واجب ترك لا أن امتناعه لتركه إياه عمداً والكلية ممنوعة ألا ترى أنه لو تذكر في ركوعه أنه ترك الفاتحة فلم يعد مع إمكانه وجب عليه السجود ا . أقول : قد يجاب عن المنع بأن المراد إمكانه على وجه لا يؤدي إلى ترك
والقراءة فيهما وكل ذلك واجب وفيها سجدة هو الصحيح، واعترض عليه بالقعدة الأخيرة فإنها فرض لا واجب. فأجاب في المعراج بأن المراد غيرها إذا لتخصيص شائع بقرينة ذكره لها سابقاً أنها فرض وما أجاب به في غاية البيان من حمل الترك فيها على تأخيرها فاسد لأنه أراد حقيقة الترك في غيرها، فلو أراد التأخير فيها لزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وكذا لو أراد بالواجب حينئذ الفرض فيها والواجب الاصطلاحي في غيرها وهو جمع كذلك. كذا في الغاية . .. ورده في الكافي بأن الممنوع اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظ واحد وهو لم يتعرض للإرادة بل قال : يحتمل هذا وذاك ولا فساد كاحتمال القرء الحيض والطهر كما في المجتبي وغيره. وما في النهاية من أن الأوجه فيه أن يحمل على رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة بأنه تجوز الصلاة بدون القعدة الأخيرة ليس بأوجه لأنها رواية ضعيفة جداً لأنهم نقلوا الإجماع على فرضيتها كما قدمناه، والظاهر أنه سهو وقع من صاحب الهداية. الثامن لفظ السلام ولا يتصور إيجاب السجود بتركه لأنه بعد القعود الأخير إذا لم يأت بمنافٍ فإنه يسلم، وإن أتى بمنافٍ فلا سجود ولهذا قال في التجنيس والسهو عن السلام يوجب سجوداً السهو والسهو عنه أن يطيل القعدة يقع أنه خرج من الصلاة ثم يعلم ذلك فيسلم ويسجد لأنه أخر واجباً أو ركناً على اختلاف الأصلين ا هـ .
عنده
وإنما يتصور إيجابه بتأخيره كما قدمناه وذكرنا في باب صفة الصلاة أن الواجب منه التسليمة الأولى وهي السلام دون عليكم ورحمة الله. وفي البدائع : إنه لم سلم عن يساره أولاً لا سهو عليه لأنه ترك السنة. وفي الظهيرية : وإذا سلم الرجل عن يمينه وسها عن التسليمة الأخرى فما دام في المسجد يأتي بالأخرى وإن استدبر القبلة، وعامة المشايخ على أنه لا يأتي متى استدبر القبلة ا هـ . التاسع قنوت الوتر وقدمنا أنه لا يختص بدعاء وأنه لا يعود إليه لو ركع على الصحيح كما في المجتبي وغيره فحينئذ يتحقق تركه بالركوع وأنه سنة عندهما كالوتر فالوجوب بتركه إنما هو قوله فقط. وفي فتح القدير: ولو قرأ القنوت في الثالثة ونسي قراءة الفاتحة أو السورة أو كليهما فتذكر بعد ما ركع قام وقرأ وأعاد القنوت لأنه والركوع رجع إلى محله قبله ويسجد للسهو بخلاف ما لو نسي سجدة التلاوة ومحلها فتذكرها في الركوع أو السجود أو القعود فإنه ينحط لها ثم يعود إلى ما كان فيه فيعيده استحباباً ا ومما ألحق به تكبيره وجزم الشارح بوجوب السجود بتركها. وذكر في الظهيرية أنه لو ترك تكبيرة القنوت فإنه لا رواية لهذا، وقيل يجب سجود السهو اعتباراً بتكبيرات العيد، وقيل لا يجب ا هـ . وينبغي ترجيح عدم الوجوب لأنه الأصل ولا دليل عليه بخلاف تكبيرات العيد فإن دليل الوجوب المواظبة مع قوله تعالى ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام
هـ.
واجب آخر، وهنا وإن أمكنه العود إلى قراءة الفاتحة يلزمه تأخير الركوع تأمل .
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. The obligation of prostration by leaving [an act] is based on it being wajib or sunnah, and the madhhab is obligation and necessary prostration by leaving it, and it was corrected in al-Bada'i'. 'Forgotfully, the sitting'. He said in al-Tajnis: This branching is on the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because adjusting the pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf. The sixth: the first sitting, and likewise every sitting that is not the last, whether in fard or nafl, then it necessitates sujud al-sahw by leaving it forgetfully. The seventh: the tashahhud, for sujud al-sahw is necessary by leaving it, even a little in the apparent narration because it is a single organized dhikr, so leaving some is like leaving all, and there is no difference between first or second. Therefore it is said in al-Zahiriyya: If one forgetfully leaves reciting tashahhud in the first or second sitting and remembers after salam, sujud al-sahw is necessary. From Abu Yusuf: it is not necessary. They said: If the praying person is an imam, he takes the saying of Abu Yusuf; if he is not an imam, he takes the saying of Muhammad. In Fath al-Qadir: Then the leaving of tashahhud in a way that necessitates sujud is only realized in the first [sitting]; as for the second tashahhud, if he remembers after salam, he recites then salams then prostrates; if he remembers after something that cuts off the building, the obligation of sujud is not conceivable. Among its branches: if after salam and remembering he occupies himself, and when he recited some of it he salamed before completing it, his prayer is invalid according to Abu Yusuf because by returning to reciting tashahhud his sitting was nullified; so if he salamed before completing it, he salamed before his sitting was of the measure of tashahhud. According to Muhammad, his prayer is valid because his sitting was not nullified at all, because the place of reciting tashahhud is the sitting, so there is no necessity to nullify it, and upon this is the fatwa. End quote. Its apparent meaning: if he remembers after salam and does not recite, he does not prostrate for forgetfulness by leaving it, because when he remembered and could do it but did not, it becomes as if he left it intentionally, so sujud is not necessary and he is only sinful. And if sujud were necessary for him, its obligation would be realized by leaving it. Upon this is a general rule: whoever forgetfully leaves a wajib and can do it after remembering but does not, there is no sujud upon him, like one who leaves it intentionally. In al-Hidayah: Then mentioning tashahhud may refer to the first and second sitting. ... The eighth: the wording of salam, and the obligation of sujud by leaving it is not conceivable because after the last sitting, if he does not do something contradictory, he salams; if he does something contradictory, there is no sujud. Therefore al-Tajnis said: forgetfulness about salam necessitates sujud al-sahw, and forgetfulness about it means that he lengthens the sitting, thinking that he has left the prayer, then learns that [he is still in it], so he salams and prostrates because he delayed an obligatory or pillar according to the two different principles. End quote. Rather, its obligation is conceivable by delaying it as we have stated. We mentioned in the chapter on description of prayer that the wajib of it is the first taslima, which is 'al-salam' not 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah'. In al-Bada'i': if he salamed to his left first, there is no sujud upon him because he left a sunnah. In al-Zahiriyya: if a man salamed to his right and forgot the other taslima, as long as he is in the mosque he performs the other, even if he has turned his back to the qibla. The majority of mashayikh hold that he does not perform it once he has turned his back to the qibla. End quote. The ninth: qunut of witr. We have stated that it is not specific to a du'a, and that he does not return to it if he has bowed according to the correct view as in al-Mujtaba and others. Thus its leaving is realized by bowing, and it is sunnah according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] like the witr itself, so the obligation by leaving it is only his saying [Abu Hanifa's]. In Fath al-Qadir: if he recited qunut in the third rak'a and forgot to recite the Fatiha or sura or both, then remembered after he bowed, he stands and recites and repeats the qunut because the bowing returned to its place before it, and he prostrates for forgetfulness. Unlike if he forgot a prostration of recitation and its place, then remembered in bowing or prostration or sitting: he goes down for it, then returns to what he was doing and repeats it as a recommendable act. End quote. Among what is annexed to it is its takbir. The commentator affirmed the obligation of sujud by leaving it. It is mentioned in al-Zahiriyya: if one leaves the takbir of qunut, there is no narration for this. It is said: sujud al-sahw is necessary by analogy to the takbirs of Eid. It is said: not necessary. End quote. It should be preferred that it is not obligatory because it is the original, and there is no evidence for it, unlike the takbirs of Eid for which the evidence of obligation is continuity with the verse 'and they mention the name of Allah in days'. End quote. Another wajib: here, even if he can return to reciting Fatiha, delaying bowing is necessary. Reflect.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This is an expansion on the causes of sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by affirming that the madhhab holds sujud al-sahw as wajib (obligatory) when a wajib element is left forgetfully, contrary to those who consider it sunnah. He then enumerates several causes from the fifth to the ninth.

The fifth cause: تعديل الأركان (adjusting the pillars) — this refers to performing the postures calmly with proper pause (tuma'nina). The author notes that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, leaving it requires sujud, while Abu Yusuf considers it fard (so no sujud needed for leaving a fard by forgetting? Actually, the text says: 'because adjusting the pillars is fard according to Abu Yusuf' implying that since it is fard, sujud is not required for forgetting it? But the author is clarifying the basis. The passage is a bit obscure.

The sixth cause: القعود الأول (the first sitting). This includes every sitting that is not the final one, whether in fard or nafl prayers. Forgetting this sitting requires sujud.

The seventh cause: التشهد (the tashahhud). Forgetting any part of the tashahhud, even a small part, requires sujud because it is considered a single organized dhikr. There is an ikhtilaf: Abu Yusuf holds that if one remembers after salam, sujud is not required, while Muhammad holds it is required. The author mentions a fatwa: an imam should follow Abu Yusuf's view (to avoid confusion for the congregation), and a non-imam should follow Muhammad's view. Further branches discuss the case where one starts reciting tashahhud after salam and then salams prematurely. The author then states a general rule: if one forgets a wajib, remembers it, and can still perform it without breaking the prayer, but deliberately chooses not to, then no sujud is required because it becomes like an intentional omission. This rule is later critiqued by al-Nahr, who gives the counterexample of forgetting Fatiha and not returning to it even though possible — sujud would be required. The author responds by qualifying 'possible' as possible without causing another wajib to be missed.

The eighth cause: لفظ السلام (the wording of salam). Forgetting the salam itself does not require sujud; rather, sujud is only required if one delays the salam (e.g., remains sitting thinking he has finished). The required salam is the first 'al-salam' not 'alaykum wa rahmat Allah'. If one salams to the left first, it is a sunnah omission, not requiring sujud.

The ninth cause: قنوت الوتر (qunut of witr). Qunut is sunnah according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but wajib according to Abu Hanifa. Forgetting qunut and bowing means it is omitted, and sujud is required on Abu Hanifa's view. If one forgets Fatiha and remembers after bowing, he returns to recite and repeats qunut. The takbir of qunut is also discussed: the commentator holds sujud required for leaving it, but there is no explicit narration; the preferred view is that it is not obligatory.

The passage ends with a note about another wajib and the need to delay bowing if one can return to Fatiha without causing another wajib to be missed.

Key Terms
السلام في الصلاة (al-salam fi al-salah): The greeting of peace that ends the prayer. The wajib part is the first 'al-salam'.
قنوت الوتر (qunut al-witr): A supplication recited in the witr prayer, usually in the last rak'a before bowing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling on qunut of witr?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) Wajib.
C) Fard.
D) Mustahab.

Key Takeaway
Delaying the salam requires sujud; qunut of witr is wajib (Abu Hanifa) so forgetting it requires sujud al-sahw.

The Final Sitting: Fard or Wajib?
Dispute on the fard/wajib status of the final sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why the Hanafi school holds the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) as fard and evaluate the weak narration that suggests otherwise.

Core Idea
The final sitting is fard; its omission invalidates the prayer, and sajdat al-sahw only covers delay.

This passage tackles a critical intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the final sitting is fard (pillar) or merely wajib (obligatory). The base text had linked sajdat al-sahw to omission of wajib acts, but an objection arises because the final sitting is widely accepted as fard. The author clarifies that the ruling of sajdat al-sahw applies to other wajib acts, and he firmly rejects a weak narration that would downgrade the final sitting to mere wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Recognize that the passage concerns the legal status of the final sitting: is it fard or wajib? The objection states it is fard, not wajib.
This distinction matters because omission of fard invalidates the prayer, while omission of wajib requires sajdat al-sahw.
2
Trace the author's response
The author in al-Mi'raj explains that the base text's ruling on sajdat al-sahw applies to other wajib acts, not the final sitting. He dismisses a counter-argument that interprets omission as delay.
He argues that mixing literal and metaphorical meanings is problematic.
3
Examine the weak narration
The text mentions a narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that prayer is valid without the final sitting. The author dismisses it as very weak because it contradicts consensus.
This narration is attributed to al-Hidayah but is not relied upon.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if one omits the final sitting entirely, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. If one delays it (e.g., begins to stand up but returns), sajdat al-sahw is required.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو ١٦٩ والقراءة فيهما وكل ذلك واجب وفيها سجدة هو الصحيح، واعترض عليه بالقعدة الأخيرة فإنها فرض لا واجب. فأجاب في المعراج بأن المراد غيرها إذا لتخصيص شائع بقرينة ذكره لها سابقاً أنها فرض وما أجاب به في غاية البيان من حمل الترك فيها على تأخيرها فاسد لأنه أراد حقيقة الترك في غيرها، فلو أراد التأخير فيها لزم الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وكذا لو أراد بالواجب حينئذ الفرض فيها والواجب الاصطلاحي في غيرها وهو جمع كذلك. كذا في الغاية . .. ورده في الكافي بأن الممنوع اجتماعهما مرادين بلفظ واحد وهو لم يتعرض للإرادة بل قال : يحتمل هذا وذاك ولا فساد كاحتمال القرء الحيض والطهر كما في المجتبي وغيره. وما في النهاية من أن الأوجه فيه أن يحمل على رواية الحسن عن أبي حنيفة بأنه تجوز الصلاة بدون القعدة الأخيرة ليس بأوجه لأنها رواية ضعيفة جداً لأنهم نقلوا الإجماع على فرضيتها كما قدمناه، والظاهر أنه سهو وقع من صاحب الهداية.
The Book of Prayer, Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. [169] Reading in them (the first two rak'ahs) and all that is wajib, and in it (the prostration) is correct. It was objected regarding the final sitting, for it is fard, not wajib. He answered in al-Mi'raj that the intended meaning is other than it, because a common specification is indicated by his previous mention that it is fard. What he answered regarding the manifest clarity of interpreting its omission as delaying it is corrupt, because he intended actual omission in other than it. If he intended delay in it, then the combination of literal and metaphorical would be necessary. Similarly, if he intended by 'wajib' then the fard in it and the technical wajib in other than it, that is also a combination. Thus in al-Ghayah. He refuted it in al-Kafi that the prevented thing is both meanings being intended by one word, and he (the objector) did not address intention but said: It is possible this and that, and there is no corruption, like the possibility of 'qur' meaning menstruation or purity, as in al-Mujtaba and others. What is in al-Nihayah that the proper view is to interpret it according to the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifah that prayer is valid without the final sitting is not proper, because it is a very weak narration, since they transmitted consensus on its being fard as we have presented. And it appears to be a slip from the author of al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage discusses the legal status of the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in prayer and whether omitting it requires sajdat al-sahw. The base text states that reading (qira'ah) in the first two rak'ahs and all other wajib acts require sujood if omitted. An objection is raised: the final sitting is fard, not wajib, so omitting it should invalidate the prayer, not merely require sujood. The author responds by clarifying that the ruling of sujood applies to other wajib acts, not the final sitting. He critiques a counter-argument that interprets omission as delay, noting that this would mix literal and metaphorical meanings. He also refutes a weak narration from al-Hasan that prayer is valid without the final sitting, reaffirming the consensus that it is fard. Thus, the correct Hanafi position is that the final sitting is fard; sujood is required only for delaying it, not for omitting it entirely.

Key Terms
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The final sitting in prayer after the last sajdah, during which the tashahhud is recited.
سجود السهو (sujood al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for errors or forgetfulness in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the final sitting (qa'dah akhirah) according to the majority of the Hanafi school?
A) It is wajib, and omitting it requires sajdat al-sahw.
B) It is fard, and omitting it invalidates the prayer.
C) It is sunnah, and omitting it is permissible.
D) It is makruh, and sajdat al-sahw is recommended.

Key Takeaway
The final sitting is fard; its omission invalidates prayer, and only delay requires sajdat al-sahw.
