When the Taslim Requires Sujood al-Sahw
Ruling on when taslim requires sujood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on when omission or delay of the taslim requires sajdat al-sahw, and distinguish between the first and second salutation.

Core Idea
Forgetting the taslim does not require sujood unless you delay it.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling: the taslim (salutation) at the end of prayer is not a simple matter. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the first taslim (wajib) and the second (sunnah), and sajdat al-sahw is only triggered by delay, not by omission. We will break down the conditions and the scholarly discussion from the text of Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The taslim is the eighth wajib of prayer. The first taslim (to the right) is wajib; the second (to the left) is sunnah. Understand this classification.
The first taslim is 'al-salam' without 'alaykum wa rahmatullah' according to the Hanafi school.
2
Determine when sujood is required
Sajdat al-sahw is not required for omitting the taslim entirely (after final sitting, if no invalidating action, one must still say salam; if invalidating, no sujood). It is only required for delaying the taslim, e.g., prolonging the final sitting.
Delay of a wajib or rukn triggers sujood.
3
Explore the scenario from al-Tajnīs
If a person prolongs the final sitting thinking they have left the prayer, then remembers and says the salam, they must also prostrate because they delayed a wajib or rukn.
The two bases refer to whether the delay was of a wajib (first taslim) or a rukn (final sitting itself).
4
Note the distinction between the two salutations
The first taslim is wajib; the second is sunnah. Forgetting the second does not require sujood. If one says salam to the left first, no sujood because it's merely leaving a sunnah.
From al-Bada'i': saying salam to left first is a sunnah omission, no sujood.
5
Understand the majority opinion on the second taslim
If one forgets the second taslim (to the left) and remembers while still in the mosque, they should perform it even if facing away from qibla. Once they have left the mosque (faced away from qibla), the majority hold they do not return.
From al-Zahiriyyah and the majority of mashāyikh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن لفظ السلام ولا يتصور إيجاب السجود بتركه لأنه بعد القعود الأخير إذا لم يأت بمنافٍ فإنه يسلم، وإن أتى بمنافٍ فلا سجود ولهذا قال في التجنيس والسهو عن السلام يوجب سجوداً السهو والسهو عنه أن يطيل القعدة يقع أنه خرج من الصلاة ثم يعلم ذلك فيسلم ويسجد لأنه أخر واجباً أو ركناً على اختلاف الأصلين ا هـ . عنده وإنما يتصور إيجابه بتأخيره كما قدمناه وذكرنا في باب صفة الصلاة أن الواجب منه التسليمة الأولى وهي السلام دون عليكم ورحمة الله. وفي البدائع : إنه لم سلم عن يساره أولاً لا سهو عليه لأنه ترك السنة. وفي الظهيرية : وإذا سلم الرجل عن يمينه وسها عن التسليمة الأخرى فما دام في المسجد يأتي بالأخرى وإن استدبر القبلة، وعامة المشايخ على أنه لا يأتي متى استدبر القبلة ا هـ .
The eighth is the utterance of the salutation (salam). The obligation of prostration by its omission is not conceivable, because after the final sitting, if he does not do something that invalidates, he will say the salam; if he does something that invalidates, then no sujood. For this reason, it is said in al-Tajnīs: 'Forgetfulness about the salam obliges a prostration of forgetfulness. Forgetfulness about it means that he prolongs the sitting, and it is thought that he has left the prayer, then he knows that, so he says the salam and prostrates, because he delayed a wajib or a rukn according to the difference of the two bases.' In his opinion, it is only conceivable to require it by delay, as we have presented. We mentioned in the chapter on the description of prayer that the obligatory part of it is the first salutation, which is 'al-salam' without 'alaykum' and 'rahmatullah'. In al-Bada'i': If he first says the salam to his left, there is no sujood on him because he left a sunnah. In al-Zahiriyyah: If a man says the salam to his right and forgets the other salutation, then as long as he is in the mosque, he should perform the other, even if he has faced away from the qiblah. The majority of the mashāyikh hold that he should not perform it once he has faced away from the qiblah.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage discusses the taslim (salutation) and when sajdat al-sahw is required. The key point is that the obligation of sujood is not for uttering the taslim itself, but for delaying it. After the final sitting, if one does nothing to invalidate the prayer, the taslim is due. If one does something invalidating, no sujood is needed. The passage distinguishes between the first taslim (which is wajib) and the second (which is sunnah). If one forgets the second taslim and leaves the mosque, the majority hold that he does not return. The ruling hinges on whether the omission is actual (no sujood) or delay (sujood required).

Key Terms
التسليمة الأولى (al-taslimah al-ula): The first salutation (saying 'al-salam') to the right, which is wajib in Hanafi prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does forgetting the taslim (salutation) require sajdat al-sahw?
A) When one omits both salutations entirely.
B) When one delays the taslim after the final sitting.
C) When one says the salam to the left first.
D) When one forgets the second salutation.

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw for the taslim is required only when it is delayed, not when it is omitted entirely.

The Qunut of Witr: Wajib or Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qunut and its takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi internal dispute on the status of qunut in witr and apply the ruling on forgetting its takbir.

Core Idea
The qunut of witr is sunnah according to the Sahibayn and does not require sujood, unlike Abu Hanifa's view.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the status of qunut in witr. It clarifies the practical difference between the two positions and extends the analysis to the takbir of qunut, weighing analogies to Eid takbir against the default principle of no obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Determine what act is being discussed (qunut in witr) and which Hanafi imams differ: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn).
The passage states: 'it is sunnah according to them (the Sahibayn) like witr' and 'the obligation for its omission is only according to his (Abu Hanifa's) view.'
2
State each position and the thamarah al-khilaf
Abu Hanifa holds qunut is wajib, so omitting it requires sajdat al-sahw; the Sahibayn hold it is sunnah, so omission does not require sujood. The practical consequence is whether the worshipper must perform extra prostrations.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf: sujood vs. no sujood.
3
Analyze the sub-issue of forgetting the takbir of qunut
The passage reports conflicting opinions: some analogize to Eid takbir (where sujood is required), others say no sujood due to lack of evidence. The author gives preponderance to no sujood because it is the default (al-asl) and there is no clear evidence.
Contrast with Eid takbir: there is evidence from Quran and consistent practice.
4
Determine the preferred view and its implications
The author's tarjih (preference) for no sujood on the takbir implies a leaning toward the Sahibayn's position on qunut. The mufta bihi view is that qunut is sunnah and its omission does not require sajdat al-sahw.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
التاسع قنوت الوتر وقدمنا أنه لا يختص بدعاء وأنه لا يعود إليه لو ركع على الصحيح كما في المجتبي وغيره فحينئذ يتحقق تركه بالركوع وأنه سنة عندهما كالوتر فالوجوب بتركه إنما هو قوله فقط. وفي فتح القدير: ولو قرأ القنوت في الثالثة ونسي قراءة الفاتحة أو السورة أو كليهما فتذكر بعد ما ركع قام وقرأ وأعاد القنوت لأنه والركوع رجع إلى محله قبله ويسجد للسهو بخلاف ما لو نسي سجدة التلاوة ومحلها فتذكرها في الركوع أو السجود أو القعود فإنه ينحط لها ثم يعود إلى ما كان فيه فيعيده استحباباً ا ومما ألحق به تكبيره وجزم الشارح بوجوب السجود بتركها. وذكر في الظهيرية أنه لو ترك تكبيرة القنوت فإنه لا رواية لهذا، وقيل يجب سجود السهو اعتباراً بتكبيرات العيد، وقيل لا يجب ا هـ . وينبغي ترجيح عدم الوجوب لأنه الأصل ولا دليل عليه بخلاف تكبيرات العيد فإن دليل الوجوب المواظبة مع قوله تعالى ويذكروا اسم الله في أيام هـ. واجب آخر، وهنا وإن أمكنه العود إلى قراءة الفاتحة يلزمه تأخير الركوع تأمل .
The ninth is the qunut of witr. We have already mentioned that it is not specific to a particular supplication, and that one does not return to it if he has bowed, according to the correct view as in al-Mujtaba and others. Thus, its omission is actualized by bowing, and it is sunnah according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) like witr itself, so the obligation (of sujood) for its omission is only according to his (Abu Hanifa's) view. In Fath al-Qadir: If one recited the qunut in the third rak'ah and forgot to recite al-Fatihah or a surah or both, and then remembers after bowing, he should stand and recite and repeat the qunut, because he and the bowing return to their place before it, and he prostrates for forgetfulness. This is unlike the case where one forgets a sajdah of tilawah and its place, and remembers it in bowing, prostration, or sitting; then he descends for it, then returns to what he was in, and repeats it as a recommendation. Included with it is its takbir, and the commentator affirmed the obligation of prostration for its omission. It is mentioned in al-Zahiriyyah that if one leaves the takbir of qunut, there is no narration regarding this. It is said that sajdat al-sahw is required by analogy with the takbir of 'Eid, and it is said that it is not required. It is preferable to give preponderance to no obligation, because that is the default, and there is no evidence for it, unlike the takbir of 'Eid, for the evidence of obligation is the persistent practice along with His statement 'and mention the name of Allah on [specific] days.' Another wajib, and here, even if he could return to reciting al-Fatihah, it would necessitate delaying the bowing. Contemplate.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage deals with the qunut in witr prayer. The author clarifies that qunut is not restricted to a specific dua, and if one bows without reciting it, he does not return because it is considered omitted. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), qunut is sunnah like witr itself, so omitting it does not require sujood. However, Abu Hanifa considers it wajib, so in his view sujood is required. The passage also discusses a scenario where one forgets Fatihah or surah and remembers after bowing: he must return and recite them, then repeat qunut, and perform sujood. This differs from forgetting a sajdah of tilawah. Regarding the takbir of qunut, there is no clear ruling; the preferred view is that no sujood is required because there is no evidence, unlike the takbir of 'Eid which has evidence from the Quran and consistent practice.

Key Terms
قنوت الوتر (qunut al-witr): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer, typically in the last rak'ah before bowing.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
تكبيرة القنوت (takbirat al-qunut): The takbir said before the qunut supplication in witr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the status of qunut in witr?
A) Wajib, and its omission requires sajdat al-sahw.
B) Sunnah, and its omission does not require sajdat al-sahw.
C) Fard, and its omission invalidates the prayer.
D) Makruh, and should be avoided.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi view is that qunut in witr is sunnah, and omitting it does not necessitate sajdat al-sahw.

The Ruling on the Eid Takbirs: Omission and Correction
Ruling on forgetting the extra takbirs in Eid prayer and the required action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on omitting, reducing, increasing, or misplacing the Eid takbirs, and determine the required action for the imam and the latecomer.

Core Idea
The Eid takbirs are wajib; their omission requires sajdat al-sahw, but the imam must return to standing if he forgets them before bowing, while a latecomer recites them in bowing.

The Eid prayer includes extra takbirs that have a specific ruling. This passage from al-Bada'i clarifies what happens if they are not performed correctly, and distinguishes between the imam and a latecomer. Additionally, it addresses the takbir of the second bowing in Eid prayer and the takbirs of Tashriq. By understanding this ruling, you will grasp the fiqh of wajib elements and the concept of 'actual performance' versus 'substitute'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
For any change in the Eid takbirs (omission, reduction, increase, misplacement), sajdat al-sahw is wajib.
2
Distinguish the imam's case
If the imam forgets the takbirs and bows, he returns to standing and recites them because he can still perform them properly.
This is because he is capable of actual performance (haqiqat al-ada).
3
Contrast the latecomer
If a latecomer joins the imam in bowing, he recites the takbirs while bowing because he cannot go back.
The latecomer acts by substitute (shabah) due to inability.
4
Examine the annexation
The takbir of the second bowing in Eid prayer is wajib by annexation; its omission requires sujood, unlike the first bowing's takbir.
5
Note the exception
Forgetting takbirs during the days of Tashriq does not require sujood since they are not prayer obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العاشر تكبيرات العيدين قال في البدائع : إذا تركها أو نقص منها أو زاد عليها أو أتى بها في غير موضعها فإنه يجب عليه السجود، وذكر في كشف الأسرار أن الإمام إذا سها عن التكبيرات حتى ركع فإنه يعود إلى القيام لأنه قادر على حقيقة الأداء فلا يعمل بشبهه بخلاف المسبوق إذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع فإنه يأتي بالتكبيرات في الركوع لأنه عجز عن حقيقته فيعمل بشبهه ا هـ . ومما ألحق بها تكبيرة الركوع الثاني من صلاة العيد فإنه يجب سجود السهو بتركها لأنها واجبة تبعاً لتكبيرات العيد بخلاف تكبيرة الركوع الأول لأنها ليست ملحقة بها. ذكره الشارح وصاحب المجتبى. وفي البدائع : ولو نسي التكبير في أيام التشريق لا سهو عليه لأنه لم يترك واجباً من واجبات الصلاة
The tenth is the takbirs of the two Eids. He said in al-Bada'i: If one leaves them, or reduces them, or increases upon them, or performs them in other than their place, then sajdat al-sahw is obligatory upon him. It is mentioned in Kashf al-Asrar that if the imam forgets the takbirs until he bows, he returns to standing, because he is capable of actual performance, so he does not act by its substitute; unlike the latecomer who catches the imam in bowing, for he performs the takbirs in bowing, because he is incapable of actual performance, so he acts by its substitute. Included with them is the takbir of the second bowing in the Eid prayer, for sajdat al-sahw is obligatory for its omission, because it is wajib by following the Eid takbirs, unlike the takbir of the first bowing, for it is not annexed to them. The commentator and the author of al-Mujtaba mention it. In al-Bada'i: And if one forgets the takbir during the days of Tashriq, there is no sujood on him, because he did not leave any wajib of the prayer's obligations.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage covers the takbirs of the two Eid prayers. The author of al-Bada'i states that omitting, reducing, increasing, or misplacing them requires sajdat al-sahw. For the imam, if he forgets them and bows, he must return to the standing position to recite them because he can still perform them properly. However, a latecomer who joins the imam in bowing should recite the takbirs while bowing because he cannot go back. The takbir of the second bowing (ruku') in Eid prayer is also considered wajib by annexation to the Eid takbirs, so its omission requires sujood, unlike the first bowing's takbir. Forgetting the takbirs during the days of Tashriq (after Eid al-Adha) does not require sujood because they are not considered obligations of the prayer itself.

Key Terms
تكبيرات العيدين (takbirat al-'idayn): The extra takbirs recited in the Eid prayer, usually in the first and second rak'ahs before recitation.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required to compensate for errors in prayer, such as omitting a wajib or performing an extra act inadvertently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam forgets the Eid takbirs and bows, what should he do?
A) Continue the prayer and perform sajdat al-sahw at the end.
B) Return to standing and recite the takbirs, then bow again.
C) Recite the takbirs while in bowing.
D) Repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Eid takbirs are wajib; any deviation requires sajdat al-sahw, but the imam who forgets them must return to standing if he can, while a latecomer recites them in bowing.

Jahr and Ikhfat: Obligations for the Imam Only
Dispute on whether jahr/ikhfat applies to the munfarid and the amount that necessitates sujood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jahr and ikhfat for the imam and munfarid, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum amount that triggers sujood, and apply the ruling to determine when sajdat al-sahw is required.

Core Idea
Jahr and ikhfat are wajib for the imam only; the munfarid is free and no sujood is required for his choice.

This lesson examines the eleventh and twelfth causes of sajdat al-sahw: the imam's failure to recite audibly in audible prayers or quietly in quiet prayers. While the obligation on the imam is clear, the precise amount that constitutes a violation is disputed among the Hanafi masters. Additionally, the status of the individual (munfarid) is distinct: he is not bound by these requirements, and no sujood is needed for his recitation choices.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
The imam must recite audibly in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and quietly in Zuhr and Asr. Violation requires sujood.
This is the eleventh and twelfth cause of sujood al-sahw.
2
Analyze the dispute on amount
Abu Hanifa says one verse; Sahibayn say three. The preferred view is that any amount, even small, triggers sujood.
The text says 'the most correct is the amount that makes prayer valid' – a large amount.
3
Distinguish imam from munfarid
Jahr/ikhfat are characteristics of the congregation; thus they apply only to the imam, not the munfarid.
The munfarid is free to choose his recitation level.
4
Examine the minority narration
Abu Sulayman narrates that if the munfarid thinks he is imam and recites audibly, sujood is required, but the majority rejects this.
The majority view is that no sujood is needed for the munfarid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The imam's sujood is wajib for any violation; the munfarid does not require sujood.
This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحادي عشر والثاني عشر الجهر الإمام فيما يجهر فيه والمخافتة مطلقاً فيما يخافت فيه واختلفت الرواية في المقدار والأصح قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين لأن اليسير من الجهر والإخفاء لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه، وعن الكثير يمكن وما تصح به الصلاة كثير غير أن ذلك عنده آية واحدة، وعندهما ثلاث آيات وهذا في حق الإمام دون المنفرد لأن الجهر والمخافتة من خصائص الجماعة. كذا في الهداية . وذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أن ظاهر الرواية وجوب السجود على الإمام إذا جهر فيما يخافت أو خافت فيما يجهر قل ذلك أو كثر، وكذا في الظهيرية والذخيرة، زاد في الخلاصة وعليه اعتماد شمس الأئمة الحلواني لا على رواية النوادر وفي الظهيرية : وروى أبو سليمان أن المنفرد إذا ظن إنه إمام فجهر كما يجهر الإمام يلزمه سجود السهو ا هـ . وهو مبني على وجوب المخافتة عليه وهو رواية الأصل وهو الصحيح كما في البدائع. وفي العناية: إن قوله : (والمخافتة مطلقاً) أي على الإمام والمنفرد، وهذا بناء على ما يأتي عن البدائع وإلا فالذي في الهداية وغيرها تخصيصه بالإمام وهو المفهوم مما يأتي عن قاضيخان والولوالجي وفي شرح الشيخ إسماعيل عن الكافي وهذا في الإمام، فإن كان منفرداً لا يجب سجود السهو، أما في الجهرية فهو مخير فلا يتمكن النقصان جهر أو خافت وأما في السرية فجهر المنفرد يكون بقدر إسماعه نفسه وهو غير منهي عنه فلذا لا يلزمه سجود السهو ا هـ. وفي شرح الزيلعي ومنح الغفار والشرنبلالية : والمنفرد لا يجب عليه السجود بالجهر والإخفاء لأنهما من خصائص الجماعة وسنذكر مثله عن التتارخانية قوله : ( والأصح قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة صححه أيضاً الزيلعي وابن الهمام قوله: (وفي الظهيرية وروى أبو سليمان (الخ قلت : وفي المعراج قال أبو اليسر : المنفرد مخير بين الجهر والمخافتة قالوا: هذا إذا كان يجهر قليلاً، أما إذا كان يسمع الناس يلزمه السهو لأنه وفي فصل القراءة من الهداية في المنفرد إن شاء جهر وأسمع نفسه ا هـ . ويوافقه ما قدمناه عن الكافي من جهر المنفرد يكون بقدر إسماعه نفسه قوله : (وفي العناية أقول : وكذا في النهاية والكفاية أن منعن عن ذلك اهـ .
The eleventh and twelfth: The imam’s audible recitation (jahr) in what he should recite audibly, and quiet recitation (ikhfat) absolutely in what he should recite quietly. There is difference in the narration regarding the amount; the most correct is the amount that makes the prayer valid in both cases, because a small amount of jahr or ikhfat cannot be avoided, while a large amount can be avoided, and what makes the prayer valid is a large amount. However, according to him (Abu Hanifa), it is one verse; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is three verses. This applies to the imam only, not the individual (munfarid), because jahr and ikhfat are characteristics of the congregation. Thus in al-Hidayah. Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that the apparent narration is the obligation of sujood upon the imam if he recites audibly in a quiet prayer or quietly in an audible prayer, whether little or much. Similarly in al-Zahiriyyah and al-Dhakhirah. In al-Khulasah, it is added that Shams al-A'immah al-Halwani relied on this, not on the rare narration (riwayat al-nawadir). In al-Zahiriyyah: Abu Sulayman narrated that the individual (munfarid), if he thought he was an imam and recited audibly as the imam does, sajdat al-sahw is obligatory upon him. This is based on the obligation of quiet recitation upon him, which is the original narration, and it is the correct view as in al-Bada'i. In al-Inayah: His statement 'and quiet recitation absolutely' means upon the imam and the individual; this is based on what will come from al-Bada'i. Otherwise, what is in al-Hidayah and others is its specification to the imam, and that is understood from what will come from Qadikhan and al-Walwaliji. In the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il from al-Kafi: This is for the imam; if he is an individual, sajdat al-sahw is not obligatory. As for the audible prayer, he is free to choose, so no deficiency occurs whether he recites audibly or quietly. As for the quiet prayer, the individual's audible recitation is to the extent of making himself hear, which is not prohibited, so no sujood is required. In al-Zayla'i's commentary, Manna al-Ghaffar, and al-Shurnublaliyyah: The individual does not have sujood due to jahr or ikhfat because they are characteristics of the congregation. We will mention similar from al-Tatarkhaniyyah. His statement: 'The most correct is the amount that makes prayer valid' was also deemed correct by al-Zayla'i and Ibn al-Humann. His statement: 'In al-Zahiriyyah: Abu Sulayman narrated...' I say: In al-Mi'raj, Abu al-Yusr said: The individual is free to choose between jahr and ikhfat. They said: This is if he recites audibly a little; but if he makes people hear, sujood is required because he is prohibited from that. In the chapter on recitation from al-Hidayah: The individual may recite audibly and make himself hear. This agrees with what we have from al-Kafi that the individual's audible recitation is to the extent of making himself hear. His statement: 'In al-Inayah, I say: Similarly in al-Nihayah and al-Kifayah that he is prohibited from that.'
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage deals with the eleventh and twelfth items that require sajdat al-sahw: the imam's jahr (audible recitation) and ikhfat (quiet recitation). The primary ruling is that the imam must recite audibly in audible prayers and quietly in quiet prayers. Failure to do so, even by a small amount, requires sujood according to the predominant view. There is disagreement on the minimum amount: Abu Hanifa says one verse, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say three verses. These rulings apply specifically to the imam because jahr and ikhfat are functions of the congregation. The passage then discusses the individual (munfarid). The majority hold that the individual is not required to observe jahr or ikhfat in a way that necessitates sujood; he may recite as he wishes as long as he can hear himself. However, if he deliberately recites loudly so that others hear, some narrations require sujood. The preferred view is that no sujood is required for the individual because he is free to choose, and the obligation of jahr/ikhfat is specific to the imam.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Audible recitation in prayers where it is required, such as Fajr, Maghrib, and Isha.
المخافتة (al-ikhfat): Quiet recitation in prayers where it is required, such as Zuhr and Asr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the predominant Hanafi view, does an individual (munfarid) need to perform sajdat al-sahw if he recites audibly in a quiet prayer?
A) Yes, because jahr and ikhfat apply to everyone.
B) No, because jahr and ikhfat are specific to the imam.
C) Yes, if he recites loudly enough for others to hear.
D) No, but only if he recites at least three verses.

Key Takeaway
The imam must observe jahr and ikhfat, and any violation requires sujood; the munfarid is free to choose and no sujood is needed.

Sujud al-Sahw for Eid Takbirs: Omission, Addition, and the Imam-Masbuq Distinction
Rulings on missing, adding, or misplacing Eid takbirs and the imam's return to standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when sujud al-sahw is required for Eid takbirs and explain why the imam returns to standing while the masbuq compensates in ruku'.

Core Idea
Missing, adding, or misplacing Eid takbirs triggers sujud; the imam returns to standing, but the masbuq acts in ruku'.

This passage from Al-Bada'i' and Kashf al-Asrar clarifies the Hanafi position on forgetfulness concerning the extra takbirs in Eid prayer. It establishes a general rule that any alteration of these wajib takbirs necessitates prostration of forgetfulness, and then provides a practical distinction between the imam's ability to correct fully and the latecomer's limited capacity.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify that leaving, reducing, increasing, or misplacing Eid takbirs makes sujud al-sahw wajib. This is because these takbirs are wajib elements in the prayer.
2
Analyze the imam's situation
If the imam forgets and remembers after ruku', he must return to standing to perform the takbirs because he can still execute the actual act. He does not act upon its likeness.
3
Analyze the masbuq's situation
The latecomer who catches the imam in ruku' must perform the takbirs while bowing because he cannot return to the proper place. He acts upon the likeness.
4
Distinguish attached takbirs
The takbir of the second ruku' in Eid is attached to the Eid takbirs; forgetting it requires sujud. The first ruku' takbir is not attached, so forgetting it does not require sujud.
5
Apply the rule to Tashriq
Forgetting takbirs during the Days of Tashriq does not require sujud because those takbirs are not wajib in the prayer itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو معلومات [الحج : ۲۸] العاشر تكبيرات العيدين قال في البدائع : إذا تركها أو نقص منها أو زاد عليها أو أتى بها في غير موضعها فإنه يجب عليه السجود، وذكر في كشف الأسرار أن الإمام إذا سها عن التكبيرات حتى ركع فإنه يعود إلى القيام لأنه قادر على حقيقة الأداء فلا يعمل بشبهه بخلاف المسبوق إذا أدرك الإمام في الركوع فإنه يأتي بالتكبيرات في الركوع لأنه عجز عن حقيقته فيعمل بشبهه ا هـ . ومما ألحق بها تكبيرة الركوع الثاني من صلاة العيد فإنه يجب سجود السهو بتركها لأنها واجبة تبعاً لتكبيرات العيد بخلاف تكبيرة الركوع الأول لأنها ليست ملحقة بها. ذكره الشارح وصاحب المجتبى. وفي البدائع : ولو نسي التكبير في أيام التشريق لا سهو عليه لأنه لم يترك واجباً من واجبات الصلاة
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration for Forgetfulness. Information [Al-Hajj:28]. Tenth: The takbirs of the two Eids. Al-Bada'i' said: If one leaves them, or reduces them, or increases them, or performs them in their wrong place, then prostration is obligatory upon him. And it is mentioned in Kashf al-Asrar that if the imam forgets the takbirs until he has bowed, then he returns to standing because he is able to perform the actual act, so he does not act upon its likeness, contrary to the masbuq (latecomer) if he catches the imam in bowing: he performs the takbirs in bowing because he is unable to perform the actual act, so he acts upon its likeness. And among the things attached to them is the takbir of the second bowing in the Eid prayer; forgetting it requires prostration of forgetfulness because it is obligatory as following the Eid takbirs, contrary to the takbir of the first bowing because it is not attached to them. Mentioned by the commentator and the author of al-Mujtaba. And in al-Bada'i': If one forgets the takbir during the Days of Tashriq, there is no prostration upon him because he did not omit an obligatory element from the obligatory elements of the prayer.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage presents rulings from the Hanafi school regarding the extra takbirs in Eid prayer (takbirat al-'idain). The general rule: any alteration—omission, addition, misplacement—of these takbirs necessitates the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) because these takbirs are wajib. A further detail from Kashf al-Asrar distinguishes between the imam and a latecomer (masbuq). If the imam forgets and only remembers after bowing (ruku'), he must return to standing to perform the takbirs in their proper place because he is still capable, whereas the latecomer who joins in ruku' performs them while bowing as he cannot return. The takbir of the second ruku' in Eid prayer is attached to these takbirs, so forgetting it requires sujud, but the first ruku' takbir is not attached. Finally, forgetting the takbirs during the Days of Tashriq does not require sujud because those takbirs are not wajib in the prayer itself.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, specifically when a wajib element is omitted, added, or misplaced.
تكبيرات العيدين (takbīrāt al-ʿīdayn): The extra takbirs in the Eid prayer, additional to the normal takbirs of the prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the imam forgets the Eid takbirs and only remembers after going into ruku', what must he do?
A) He continues his prayer and does not return.
B) He returns to standing to perform the takbirs.
C) He performs sujud al-sahw without returning.
D) He completes the prayer and repeats it.

Key Takeaway
Any alteration of the Eid takbirs (leaving, reducing, increasing, misplacing) requires sujud al-sahw; the imam returns to standing if able, while the masbuq performs them in ruku'.

Jahr and Ikhfā' in Prayer and Sujud al-Sahw: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on jahr/ikhfā' and sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on jahr and ikhfā' for the imam and munfarid, and apply the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum quantity triggering sujud al-sahw.

Core Idea
For the imam, jahr/ikhfā' are wajib; for the munfarid, they are not required.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into the detailed rulings of loud and quiet recitation in prayer, focusing on the imam's obligation and the forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw) that results from violation. It also examines the intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum quantity that triggers sujud, and clarifies that these rulings are specific to the imam, not the individual praying alone. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of recitation and sujud al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Rulings
Define jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfā' (quiet recitation) and state in which prayers each is prescribed for the imam.
Fajr, Maghrib, 'Isha, Jumu'ah, Eid require jahr; Dhuhr and 'Asr require ikhfā'.
2
Determine Who Is Obligated
Note that these are characteristics of the congregation (khasa'is al-jama'ah) and thus only the imam is obligated, not the munfarid.
3
Locate the Dispute on Quantity
Identify the disagreement: Abu Hanifa says one verse triggers sujud, Sahibayn say three verses. Also note the view that any amount triggers sujud.
4
Apply the Tarjih
The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is that sujud is required for any forgetful change, regardless of quantity.
This is the position preferred by the author and fatwa authorities.
5
Evaluate the Munfarid's Position
According to zahir al-riwaya, no sujud is required for the munfarid. However, there is a conflicting narration from Abu Sulayman requiring sujud if he mistakenly acts as an imam.
The predominant view is that the munfarid is not bound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحادي عشر والثاني عشر الجهر الإمام فيما يجهر فيه والمخافتة مطلقاً فيما يخافت فيه واختلفت الرواية في المقدار والأصح قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين لأن اليسير من الجهر والإخفاء لا يمكن الاحتراز عنه، وعن الكثير يمكن وما تصح به الصلاة كثير غير أن ذلك عنده آية واحدة، وعندهما ثلاث آيات وهذا في حق الإمام دون المنفرد لأن الجهر والمخافتة من خصائص الجماعة. كذا في الهداية . وذكر قاضيخان في فتاواه أن ظاهر الرواية وجوب السجود على الإمام إذا جهر فيما يخافت أو خافت فيما يجهر قل ذلك أو كثر، وكذا في الظهيرية والذخيرة، زاد في الخلاصة وعليه اعتماد شمس الأئمة الحلواني لا على رواية النوادر وفي الظهيرية : وروى أبو سليمان أن المنفرد إذا ظن إنه إمام فجهر كما يجهر الإمام يلزمه سجود السهو ا هـ . وهو مبني على وجوب المخافتة عليه وهو رواية الأصل وهو الصحيح كما في البدائع. وفي العناية: إن قوله : (والمخافتة مطلقاً) أي على الإمام والمنفرد، وهذا بناء على ما يأتي عن البدائع وإلا فالذي في الهداية وغيرها تخصيصه بالإمام وهو المفهوم مما يأتي عن قاضيخان والولوالجي وفي شرح الشيخ إسماعيل عن الكافي وهذا في الإمام، فإن كان منفرداً لا يجب سجود السهو، أما في الجهرية فهو مخير فلا يتمكن النقصان جهر أو خافت وأما في السرية فجهر المنفرد يكون بقدر إسماعه نفسه وهو غير منهي عنه فلذا لا يلزمه سجود السهو ا هـ. وفي شرح الزيلعي ومنح الغفار والشرنبلالية : والمنفرد لا يجب عليه السجود بالجهر والإخفاء لأنهما من خصائص الجماعة وسنذكر مثله عن التتارخانية قوله : ( والأصح قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة صححه أيضاً الزيلعي وابن الهمام قوله: (وفي الظهيرية وروى أبو سليمان (الخ قلت : وفي المعراج قال أبو اليسر : المنفرد مخير بين الجهر والمخافتة قالوا: هذا إذا كان يجهر قليلاً، أما إذا كان يسمع الناس يلزمه السهو لأنه وفي فصل القراءة من الهداية في المنفرد إن شاء جهر وأسمع نفسه ا هـ . ويوافقه ما قدمناه عن الكافي من جهر المنفرد يكون بقدر إسماعه نفسه قوله : (وفي العناية أقول : وكذا في النهاية والكفاية أن ظاهر الرواية أن الإخفاء ليس بواجب عليه وذكر الولوالجي أنه إذا جهر فيما يخافت فيه يجب سجدة السهو قل أو كثر ، وإذا خافت فيما يجهر به لا يجب ما لم يكن قدر ما يتعلق به وجوب الصلاة على الاختلاف الذي مر وهذا أصح اهـ. فقد اختلف الترجيح على ثلاثة أقوال، وينبغي عدم العدول عن ظاهر الرواية الذي نقله الثقات من أصحاب الفتاوي كما لا يخفى . وذكر في الخلاصة أنه لو رجلاً أو رجلين لا يكون جهراً والجهر أن يسمع الكل ا هـ . وصرحوا بأنه إذا جهر سهواً بشيء من الأدعية والأثنية ولو تشهداً فإنه لا يجب عليه السجود. قال العلامة الحلبي : ولا يعرى القول بذلك في التشهد من تأمل ا هـ . وقد اقتصر سمع من من المخافتة ومعراج الدراية. وقال في الهداية بعد ما تقدم وهذا في الإمام دون المنفرد لأن الجهر والمخافتة من خصائص الجماعة. قال الشراح : إن ما ذكره جواب ظاهر الرواية، وأما جواب رواية النوادر فإنه يجب عليه سجدة السهو وفي التتارخانية عن المحيط : وأما المنفرد فلا سهو عليه إذا خافت فيما يجهر لأن الجهر غير واجب عليه. وكذلك إذا جهر فيما يخافت لأنه لم يترك واجباً لأن المخافتة إنما وجبت لنفي المغالطة وإنما يحتاج إلى هذا في صلاة تؤدى على سبيل الشهرة والمنفرد يؤدي على سبيل الخفية . وفي الذخيرة : المنفرد إذا جهر فيما يخافت أن عليه السهو، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا سهو عليه وقد مر ذلك شيء من في صفة الصلاة فراجعه وفي شرح المنية : وميل الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام إلى أن المخافتة واجبة على المنفرد في موضعها فيجب بتركها السهو وهو الاحتياط ا هـ . وإليه جنح المؤلف وأخوه قوله: (وذكر الولوالجي (الخ) عزا هذا التفصيل في المعراج إلى النوادر وقال : ووجه الفرق أن حكم الجهر فيما يخافت أغلظ المخافتة فيما يجهر لأن الصلاة التي يجهر فيها لها حظ ا هـ. وفيه بحث للمحقق ابن الهمام ذكره المؤلف في باب صفة الصلاة فراجعه قوله : (فقد اختلف الترجيح) أي في مقدار ما يجب به السجود على ثلاثة أقوال الأول ما في الهداية من تقديره بما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين الثاني ما في الخانية وغيرها من عدم التقدير بشيء فيهما. الثالث ما في الولوالجية من عدم التقدير فيما إذا جهر فيما يخافت والتقدير في عكسه قوله : ( وينبغي عدم العدول عن ظاهر الرواية) أي القول الثاني قال في النهر وأقول : بل الذي ينبغي أن يعول عليه ما في البدائع للمواظبة على أن ما في الأصل هو ظاهر الرواية ا هـ . قال الشيخ إسماعيل : ويؤيده زيادة قوله «وهو الصحيح لكن عبر في الحجة فيه بظاهر رواية الأصل فليتأمل ا هـ . وأنت خبير بأن كلام المؤلف في بيان المقدار كما هو صريح قوله أولاً واختلفت الرواية في المقدار» وقوله ثانياً «فقد اختلف الترجيح على ثلاثة أقوال ؛ فقوله «وبنبغي الخ» ترجيح هو ظاهر الرواية في هذه المسألة والذي . في البدائع مسألة أخرى وهي وجوب المخافته على المنفرد، والقول الذي رجحه المؤلف أعني ما في الخانية وإن كان يفهم منه ما يخالف ما في البدائع موافقاً في العناية لكن لم يقصد المؤلف ترجيحه هذه الجهة أيضاً بل ترجيح ما هو بصدده من مسألة المقدار بدليل قوله في باب صفة الصلاة بعد نقله ما في العناية وفيه تأمل والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب، وكذا صرح بذلك في غير هذا
Eleventh and Twelfth: The imam recites loudly where loud recitation is prescribed, and quietly where quiet recitation is prescribed. The narrations differ concerning the quantity. The most sound is that it is the amount that makes the prayer valid in both cases, because a small amount of loudness or quietness cannot be avoided, while a large amount can be avoided. What makes the prayer valid is a large amount, except that in his view (Abu Hanifa) it is one verse, and in their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is three verses. This applies to the imam, not the individual (munfarid), because loud and quiet recitation are characteristics of the congregation. Thus in al-Hidayah. Qadikhan mentioned in his Fatawa that according to zahir al-riwaya, sujud is obligatory upon the imam if he recites loudly where he should be quiet, or quietly where he should be loud, whether little or much. Similarly in al-Zahiriyya and al-Dhakhira. In al-Khulasa, it is added: and upon it is the reliance of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, not on the narration of al-Nawadir. And in al-Zahiriyya: Abu Sulayman narrated that if the individual thinks he is an imam and recites loudly as the imam does, sujud al-sahw is obligatory upon him. This is based on the obligation of quiet recitation upon him, and that is the original narration, and it is correct as in al-Bada'i'. And in al-'Inayah: his saying: (and quiet recitation absolutely) means upon the imam and the individual, and this is based on what comes from al-Bada'i'; otherwise, that which is in al-Hidayah and others specifies it for the imam... (continued at length).
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi discussion on the rulings of jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfā' (quiet recitation) in prayer, and whether forgetting to observe them requires sujud al-sahw. The core ruling from al-Hidayah is that the imam must recite loudly in loud prayers and quietly in quiet prayers; if he forgets, sujud is required. The amount that triggers sujud is disputed: according to Abu Hanifa, it is one verse; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, three verses. The relied-upon view (al-asahh) is the amount that makes the prayer valid. Importantly, this ruling is for the imam only; the individual (munfarid) is not bound by jahr/ikhfā' because these are characteristics of congregation. The passage then presents multiple narrations and opinions: Qadikhan reports that zahir al-riwaya obligates sujud for the imam regardless of the amount. Others restrict it. For the munfarid, the predominant view is that no sujud is required, though there is a narration from Abu Sulayman requiring it if he mistakenly acts as an imam. The author of al-Hidayah and later commentators clarify that the obligation of ikhfā' on the munfarid is not established in zahir al-riwaya. At the end, the author discusses the tarjih (preference) among three opinions and advises not to deviate from zahir al-riwaya, which is the second opinion (no fixed measure). The passage emphasizes that jahr/ikhfā' are specifically for the imam, and the munfarid has more flexibility.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation, specifically audible to others, as prescribed in Fajr, Maghrib, 'Isha', Jumu'ah, and Eid prayers for the imam.
المخافتة (al-mukhāfatah): Quiet recitation, where the reciter can hear himself but is not loud enough for others, prescribed in Dhuhr and 'Asr prayers.
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known transmitted ruling from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, considered the authoritative position of the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion (zahir al-riwaya), what is the ruling on a munfarid (individual praying alone) who recites loudly in a quiet prayer?
A) He must perform sujud al-sahw regardless of the amount.
B) He is not required to perform sujud al-sahw.
C) He must repeat the prayer.
D) He should perform sujud only if he recites three verses or more.

Key Takeaway
The imam must observe jahr/ikhfā' in their prescribed places; any forgetful change requires sujud al-sahw, while the munfarid is not obligated in this regard.

intermediate
10 min
Jahr and Ikhfa' for Imam and Munfarid: Intra-Hanafi Analysis
Explaining the rulings on jahr and ikhfa' and the necessity of sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jahr and ikhfa' for the imam and munfarid, distinguish between zahir al-riwayah and nawadir positions, and explain the tarjih mechanism.

Core Idea
Jahr and ikhfa' are characteristics of congregation; the munfarid is not bound by them in zahir al-riwayah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deepens the discussion on loud and quiet recitation in prayer. It distinguishes between the imam and the individual praying alone (munfarid), revealing an intra-Hanafi debate on whether ikhfa' is wajib for the munfarid. We will trace the proofs, the different narrations, and the author's tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Pinpoint the precise act: reciting aloud (jahr) or quietly (ikhfa') in the wrong place during prayer. Determine whether this triggers sujud al-sahw. The ruling differs for imam and munfarid.
The text distinguishes between imam and munfarid from the outset.
2
Locate the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The proof is qiyasi: jahr and ikhfa' are characteristics of congregational prayer (khasa'is al-jama'ah). Hence, the munfarid is not obligated by them. The absence of obligation means no sujud al-sahw for leaving them.
wajh al-dalalah: 'li-anna al-jahr wa al-mukhafata min khasa'is al-jama'ah' — a reasoning from the nature of congregational worship.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Contrast the zahir al-riwayah position (no obligation for munfarid) with the nawadir narration that holds ikhfa' wajib on the munfarid. Note the authority weight: zahir al-riwayah is primary.
The text mentions al-Walwaliji, al-Hidaya, and later scholars like Ibn al-Humam who consider ikhfa' wajib as a precaution.
4
Evaluate the tarjih
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (Ibn Nujaym) recommends not deviating from the zahir al-riwayah. However, he also notes Ibn al-Humam's view as a cautious option (ihtiyat). Understand the hierarchy: zahir al-riwayah > nawadir.
The passage ends by discussing the three opinions on the amount that necessitates sujud – but the core tarjih is to stay with zahir al-riwayah.
5
Apply to a practical scenario
Given a scenario: a munfarid inadvertently recites aloud in a quiet prayer. According to zahir al-riwayah, no sujud al-sahw is required. According to nawadir and Ibn al-Humam, sujud is required. The mufta bihi is the zahir al-riwayah position.
This shows the practical consequence (thamarah) of the ikhtilaf.

كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو
ظاهر الرواية أن الإخفاء ليس بواجب عليه وذكر الولوالجي أنه إذا جهر فيما يخافت فيه يجب سجدة السهو قل أو كثر ، وإذا خافت فيما يجهر به لا يجب ما لم يكن قدر ما يتعلق به وجوب الصلاة على الاختلاف الذي مر وهذا أصح اهـ. فقد اختلف الترجيح على ثلاثة أقوال، وينبغي عدم العدول عن ظاهر الرواية الذي نقله الثقات من أصحاب الفتاوي كما لا يخفى . وذكر في الخلاصة أنه لو رجلاً أو رجلين لا يكون جهراً والجهر أن يسمع الكل ا هـ . وصرحوا بأنه إذا جهر سهواً بشيء من الأدعية والأثنية ولو تشهداً فإنه لا يجب عليه السجود. قال العلامة الحلبي : ولا يعرى القول بذلك في التشهد من تأمل ا هـ . وقد اقتصر سمع من من المخافتة ومعراج الدراية. وقال في الهداية بعد ما تقدم وهذا في الإمام دون المنفرد لأن الجهر والمخافتة من خصائص الجماعة. قال الشراح : إن ما ذكره جواب ظاهر الرواية، وأما جواب رواية النوادر فإنه يجب عليه سجدة السهو وفي التتارخانية عن المحيط : وأما المنفرد فلا سهو عليه إذا خافت فيما يجهر لأن الجهر غير واجب عليه. وكذلك إذا جهر فيما يخافت لأنه لم يترك واجباً لأن المخافتة إنما وجبت لنفي المغالطة وإنما يحتاج إلى هذا في صلاة تؤدى على سبيل الشهرة والمنفرد يؤدي على سبيل الخفية . وفي الذخيرة : المنفرد إذا جهر فيما يخافت أن عليه السهو، وفي ظاهر الرواية لا سهو عليه وقد مر ذلك شيء من في صفة الصلاة فراجعه وفي شرح المنية : وميل الشيخ كمال الدين بن الهمام إلى أن المخافتة واجبة على المنفرد في موضعها فيجب بتركها السهو وهو الاحتياط ا هـ . وإليه جنح المؤلف وأخوه قوله: (وذكر الولوالجي (الخ) عزا هذا التفصيل في المعراج إلى النوادر وقال : ووجه الفرق أن حكم الجهر فيما يخافت أغلظ المخافتة فيما يجهر لأن الصلاة التي يجهر فيها لها حظ ا هـ. وفيه بحث للمحقق ابن الهمام ذكره المؤلف في باب صفة الصلاة فراجعه قوله : (فقد اختلف الترجيح) أي في مقدار ما يجب به السجود على ثلاثة أقوال الأول ما في الهداية من تقديره بما تجوز به الصلاة في الفصلين الثاني ما في الخانية وغيرها من عدم ا التقدير بشيء فيهما. الثالث ما في الولوالجية من عدم التقدير فيما إذا جهر فيما يخافت والتقدير في عكسه قوله : ( وينبغي عدم العدول عن ظاهر الرواية) أي القول الثاني قال في النهر وأقول : بل الذي ينبغي أن يعول عليه ما في البدائع للمواظبة على أن ما في الأصل هو ظاهر الرواية ا هـ . قال الشيخ إسماعيل : ويؤيده زيادة قوله «وهو الصحيح لكن عبر في الحجة فيه بظاهر رواية الأصل فليتأمل ا هـ . وأنت خبير بأن كلام المؤلف في بيان المقدار كما هو صريح قوله أولاً واختلفت الرواية في المقدار» وقوله ثانياً «فقد اختلف الترجيح على ثلاثة أقوال ؛ فقوله «وبنبغي الخ» ترجيح هو ظاهر الرواية في هذه المسألة والذي . في البدائع مسألة أخرى وهي وجوب المخافته على المنفرد، والقول الذي رجحه المؤلف أعني ما في الخانية وإن كان يفهم منه ما يخالف ما في البدائع موافقاً في العناية لكن لم يقصد المؤلف ترجيحه هذه الجهة أيضاً بل ترجيح ما هو بصدده من مسألة المقدار بدليل قوله في باب صفة الصلاة بعد نقله ما في العناية وفيه تأمل والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب، وكذا صرح بذلك في غير هذا
من
The Book of Prayer, Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. In zahir al-riwayah, ikhfa' is not wajib upon him. Al-Walwaliji mentioned that if he recites loudly where it is quiet, sujud al-sahw is required, little or much; and if he recites quietly where it is loud, it is not required unless it is an amount that affects the validity of the prayer, according to the difference mentioned, and this is more correct. So the tarjih has differed into three opinions, and it is appropriate not to deviate from zahir al-riwayah which the reliable fatwa scholars have transmitted, as is not hidden. And in al-Khulasa it is mentioned that if it is for one or two men, it is not loud; loudness is that all hear. And they explicitly stated that if one inadvertently recites loudly any of the supplications or praises, even if tashahhud, sujud is not required upon him. Al-Halabi said: The statement about tashahhud is not free from reflection. And he confined himself to ... from ... of quietness and Mi'raj al-Diraya. And al-Hidaya said after the above: This applies to the imam, not the munfarid, because loudness and quietness are characteristics of congregation. The commentators said: What he mentioned is the answer of zahir al-riwayah; as for the answer of the nawadir narration, sujud al-sahw is required upon him. And in al-Tatarkhaniyya from al-Muhit: As for the munfarid, he does not need sujud if he recites quietly where loud because loudness is not wajib upon him. Similarly, if he recites loudly where quiet, because he did not leave a wajib, since quietness is only required to negate disturbance, and this is needed in a prayer performed publicly, while the munfarid performs secretly. And in al-Dhakhira: The munfarid, if he recites loudly where quiet, sujud is upon him; in zahir al-riwayah, no sujud is upon him. And that was mentioned in the chapter on the description of prayer, so refer to it. In Sharh al-Muniyya: Shaykh Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam inclined to the view that quietness is wajib upon the munfarid in its place, so leaving it requires sujud, and this is precaution. And the author and his brother inclined to it. His statement: (And al-Walwaliji mentioned) He attributed this detail in al-Mi'raj to the nawadir and said: The difference is that the ruling of loudness in a quiet place is more severe than quietness in a loud place because the prayer in which loudness occurs has a share. There is a discussion by Ibn al-Humam, mentioned by the author in the chapter on the description of prayer, so refer to it. His statement: (So the tarjih has differed) i.e., regarding the amount that necessitates sujud, there are three opinions: first, what is in al-Hidaya of estimating it by what suffices for the prayer in both cases; second, what is in al-Khaniyya and others of not estimating anything in both; third, what is in al-Walwalijiyya of not estimating when loud in quiet, but estimating in the opposite. His statement: (And it is appropriate not to deviate from zahir al-riwayah) meaning the second opinion. He said in al-Nahr: I say, rather what should be relied upon is what is in al-Bada'i' for diligence, that what is in the original is zahir al-riwayah. Shaykh Isma'il said: It is supported by his additional statement 'and it is correct, but he expressed it in al-Hujja as zahir al-riwayah of the original, so reflect.' You are aware that the author's speech is about explaining the amount, as is clear from his first statement 'the narration differed regarding the amount' and his second 'so the tarjih has differed into three opinions'; his statement 'and it is appropriate' is a tarjih of what is zahir al-riwayah in this issue. And what is in al-Bada'i' is another issue, namely the obligation of quietness on the munfarid, and the opinion that the author favored, i.e., what is in al-Khaniyya, although it may seem to contradict what is in al-Bada'i', agreeing with al-'Inaya, but the author did not intend to favor it in this respect; rather he favored what is concerning the issue of the amount, as evidenced by his statement in the chapter on the description of prayer after quoting from al-'Inaya, 'there is reflection in it, and the apparent from the madhhab is obligation', and he explicitly stated that in other than this from
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discussing the rulings on jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa' (quiet recitation) in prayer, particularly in relation to sujud al-sahw. The text is an expansion probe, explaining different narrations and opinions within the Hanafi school. The opening states that in zahir al-riwayah (the established transmitted view), ikhfa' is not wajib upon the imam. However, al-Walwaliji reports a detail: if the imam recites loudly where it should be quiet, sujud al-sahw is required regardless of the amount; if he recites quietly where loud, sujud is not required unless the silence affects the validity of the prayer. The tarjih has differed into three opinions. The author recommends not deviating from zahir al-riwayah, supported by reliable fatwa scholars. The passage also defines jahr as making all hear. A separate ruling states that inadvertently reciting loud in supplications, praises, or tashahhud does not require sujud. A key point is the distinction between imam and munfarid: al-Hidayah states that these rulings are for the imam only, as jahr and ikhfa' are characteristics of congregational prayer. The commentators explain that this is the answer of zahir al-riwayah, while the nawadir narration requires sujud for the munfarid as well. Later, comparisons are made between different opinions: some say the munfarid does not need sujud at all, others require it. The author inclines to the view of Ibn al-Humam that ikhfa' is wajib on the munfarid, so leaving it requires sujud. The passage then clarifies the three opinions on the amount that necessitates sujud: 1) estimation by what suffices for prayer (al-Hidaya), 2) no estimation (al-Khaniyya), 3) estimation only in one direction (al-Walwalijiyya). The author's tarjih is to follow the second opinion, though al-Bada'i' presents a different issue about the obligation of quietness on the munfarid.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted opinion from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare or less common narrations from the Hanafi imams, not part of the six core books.
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer that may necessitate sujud al-sahw.
خصائص الجماعة (khasa'is al-jama'ah): Characteristics specific to congregational prayer, such as jahr and ikhfa'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text from al-Hidayah cited in this passage, to whom does the ruling about jahr and ikhfa' apply?
A) Both imam and munfarid
B) Only the imam
C) Only the munfarid
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, jahr and ikhfa' are obligations upon the imam in congregational prayer; for the munfarid, they are not wajib in the primary transmitted opinion.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Delaying a Fard or Wajib Necessitates Sujud al-Sahw: Principles and Examples
Rules for ta'khir of fard/wajib and sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that delaying a fard or wajib requires sujud al-sahw, and apply it to scenarios such as reciting in ruku', repeating Fatiha, and sending blessings during prayer.

Core Idea
Delaying a fard or wajib in prayer necessitates sujud al-sahw, even if the delay comes from a virtuous act.

The lesson expands on the obligations (wajibat) of prayer by introducing a critical principle: you must not delay or alter a fard or wajib. Doing so requires compensatory sujud (sujud al-sahw). The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents several concrete examples from the Hanafi tradition, including a key dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding sending blessings on the Prophet in the first sitting. Understanding this principle helps you analyze when sujud al-sahw is needed and why the Hanafi school sometimes differs internally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Principle
The passage states that one of the wajibat of prayer is not to delay or change the fard or wajib. Delaying a fard triggers sujud for the delay itself; delaying a wajib triggers sujud for leaving the wajib (not delay). Grasp this foundational distinction.
Fard: pillar (rukn) → delay invalidates? No, but sujud compensates. Wajib: non-pillar obligation → leaving it also requires sujud.
2
Examine Examples of Delaying a Fard
The author lists: two ruku' (delays first sujud and standing), three sajdahs (delays standing), sitting in place of standing or vice versa. For each, identify which fard is delayed and why sujud is wajib.
The phrase 'المفروض' distinguishes fard sitting (jalsah) from wajib sitting (like tashahhud).
3
Analyze the Dispute on Reciting Quran in Ruku'/Sujud
Al-Bada'i' says no sujud because it is praise; the author prefers the view that sujud is required (delaying a rukn/wajib). Trace the reasoning: the act of reciting an ayah itself is not the problem, but the delay it causes.
The author uses 'والظاهر الأول' to indicate his tarjih.
4
Explore the Dispute on Sending Blessings in the First Sitting
Abu Hanifa says sujud is required because the blessing delays standing (a fard). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue no sujud because there is no deficiency in blessing. Understand the illa (cause) according to each.
The dream narrative supports Abu Hanifa's position that the delay is the cause, not the blessing itself.
5
Understand the Author's Tarjih and Practical Consequence
The author sides with Abu Hanifa on blessings and with the first view on recitation. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) follows this tarjih. The practical difference: in following Abu Hanifa, sujud is required; following the Sahibayn, it is not.
The dispute shows that even within the Hanafi school, there can be legitimate ikhtilaf.

المصنف على هذه الواجبات في باب صفة الصلاة وبقي واجب آخر وهو عدم تأخير الفرض والواجب وعدم تغييرهما وعليه تفرع مسائل منها : لو ركع ركوعين أو سجد ثلاثاً في ركعة لزمه السجود لتأخير الفرض وهو السجود في الأول والقيام في الثاني، وكذا لو قعد في محل القيام أو قام في محل القعود المفروض وإنما قيدنا بالمفروض لأنه لو قام في محل الواجب فقد لزمه السجود لترك الواجب لا لتأخيره، وكذا لو قرأ آية في الركوع أو السجود أو القومة فعليه السهو كما في الظهيرية وغيرها وعلله في المحيط بتأخير ركن أو واجب عليه، وكذا لو قرأها في القعود إن بدأ بالقراءة وإن بدأ بالتشهد ثم قرأها فلا سهو عليه كما في المحيط . وفي البدائع : لو قرأ القرآن في ركوعه أو في سجوده لا سهو عليه لأنه ثناء وهذه الأركان مواضع الثناء ا هـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه فالظاهر الأول. ومنها لو كرر الفاتحة في الأوليين فعليه السهو لتأخير السورة ومنها لو تشهد في قيامه بعد الفاتحة لزمه السجود وقبلها لا على الأصح لتأخير الواجب في الأول وهو السورة، وفي الثاني محل الثناء وهو منه . . وفي الظهيرية : لو تشهد في القيام إن كان في الركعة الأولى لا يلزمه شيء، وإن كان في الثانية اختلف المشايخ فيه والصحيح أنه لا يجب ا هـ . فقد اختلف التصحيح والظاهر الأول المنقول في التبيين وغيره ومنها لو كرر التشهد في القعدة الأولى فعليه السهو ولتأخير القيام وكذا لو صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيها لتأخيره. واختلفوا في قدره والأصح وجوبه باللهم صل على محمد وإن لم يقل وعلى آله . وذكر في البدائع أنه يجب عليه السجود عنده، وعندهما لا يجب لأنه لو وجب لوجب لجبر النقصان ولا يعقل نقصان في الصلاة على رسول الله ، وأبو حنيفة رحمه الله يقول : لا يجب عليه بالصلاة على النبي له بل بتأخير الفرض وهو القيام إلا أن التأخير حصل بالصلاة فيجب عليه من حيث إنها تأخير لا من حيث إنها صلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقد حكي في المناقب أن أبا حنيفة رأى النبي الله في المنام فقال له: كيف أوجبت على من صلى علي سجود السهو فأجابه بكونه صلى عليك ساهياً فاستحسنه منه . ولو كرر التشهد المحل وبدليل قوله والمخافتة مطلقاً فيما يخافت فيه أي سواء كان إماماً أو لا كما بيناه، فعلم أنه ليس مراده ترجيح القول بعدم وجوب الإخفاء على المنفرد بل ترجيح القول بأن الجهر والإخفاء غير مقدرين بمقدار ما تجوز به الصلاة خلافاً لما في الهداية من التقدير فيهما، ولما في الولوالجية من التقدير في الثاني فقط على أنه حيث كان يفهم مما في الخانية تخصيص وجوب المخافتة في ظاهر الرواية بالإمام دون المنفرد وصرح بهذا المفهوم في العناية وغيرها، فلا يعارضه تصريح البدائع بأن وجوب المخافتة على المنفرد رواية الأصل لأنه وإن كان ما في الأصل ظاهر الرواية لا يلزم منه أن يكون ما في غيره غير ظاهر الرواية بل الشأن ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر وذلك بقول البدائع وهو الصحيح لا بقوله وهو رواية الأصل كما قال صاحب النهر فتدبر قوله : (كذا في البدائع) قال
اه.
The author (المصنف) on these obligations in the chapter on the description of prayer: one more obligation remains, which is not to delay the fard or wajib and not to change them. From this branch issues arise, including: if one performs two ruku' or three sajdahs in one rak'ah, sujud is necessary due to delaying the fard, which is sujud in the first and standing in the second. Similarly, if one sits in place of standing or stands in place of the prescribed sitting. We only restricted to the prescribed because if he stands in place of the wajib, sujud is necessary due to leaving the wajib, not due to delaying it. Similarly, if one recites an ayah in ruku', sujud, or qawmah, sujud is upon him, as in al-Dhahiriyya and others, and al-Muhit explains it as delaying a rukn or wajib. Similarly, if he recites it in sitting, if he begins with recitation, but if he begins with tashahhud then recites, no sujud is upon him, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Bada'i': if one recites Quran in his ruku' or sujud, no sujud is upon him because it is praise, and these are places of praise. The apparent is the first. Among them: if one repeats al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs, sujud is upon him due to delaying the surah. Among them: if one recites tashahhud while standing after al-Fatiha, sujud is necessary; before al-Fatiha, it is not, according to the correct view, due to delaying the wajib in the first (the surah), and in the second it is a place of praise. And in al-Dhahiriyya: if one recites tashahhud while standing, if in the first rak'ah, nothing is required; if in the second, the mashayikh differed, and the correct is that it is not required. So the correction differed, and the apparent is the first, transmitted in al-Tabyin and others. Among them: if one repeats tashahhud in the first sitting, sujud is upon him due to delaying the standing. Similarly, if one sends blessings upon the Prophet therein, due to delaying it. They differed regarding its amount, and the correct is that it is required by saying 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad' even if he does not say 'wa ala alihi'. And it is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that sujud is necessary according to him (Abu Hanifa), while according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is not necessary, because if it were necessary, it would be to compensate a deficiency, and there is no deficiency in sending blessings upon the Messenger of Allah. Abu Hanifa says: It is not necessary due to the blessing itself, but due to delaying the fard, which is the standing, except that the delay occurred by the blessing, so it is necessary from the perspective of delay, not from the perspective of blessing. And it is narrated in al-Manaqib that Abu Hanifa saw the Prophet in a dream and asked: How did you make sujud al-sahw obligatory upon one who blessed you? He replied: Because he blessed you forgetfully, and he (Abu Hanifa) approved of it. And if he repeats tashahhud ... and by the evidence of his statement and quietness absolutely in what is quiet, i.e., whether imam or not, as we explained, so it is known that he did not intend to favor the opinion of no obligation of ikhfa' upon the munfarid, but rather to favor the opinion that loudness and quietness are not estimated by the amount that suffices for the prayer, contrary to what is in al-Hidaya of estimation in both, and what is in al-Walwalijiyya of estimation in the second only, on the basis that since it is understood from al-Khaniyya that the obligation of quietness in zahir al-riwayah is specifically for the imam, not the munfarid, and this was explicitly stated in al-'Inaya and others, it does not contradict the statement of al-Bada'i' that obligation of quietness upon the munfarid is the narration of the original, because even if what is in the original is zahir al-riwayah, it does not imply that what is in others is not zahir al-riwayah; rather the matter is to prefer one over the other. That is by the statement of al-Bada'i' that 'it is correct', not by his statement 'it is a narration of the original', as the author of al-Nahr said. So reflect on his statement: (Likewise in al-Bada'i') he said: end.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues the discussion on sujud al-sahw, focusing on the principle that delaying a fard or wajib (or changing them) necessitates sujud. The author lists several examples: performing two ruku' or three sajdahs in one rak'ah delays the fard (sujud in the first case, standing in the second). Sitting in a standing place or standing in a sitting place also causes sujud, with the nuance that standing in a wajib place (not fard) triggers sujud for leaving the wajib, not delay. Reciting an ayah in ruku', sujud, or qawmah requires sujud because it delays a rukn or wajib; however, if reciting after starting tashahhud in sitting, no sujud is needed. Al-Bada'i' presents an opposing view: reciting Quran in ruku' or sujud does not require sujud as it is praise, and these are places of praise. The author prefers the first view (sujud required). Other examples: repeating al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs delays the surah, so sujud; reciting tashahhud while standing after al-Fatiha requires sujud, before it does not; differing views on tashahhud in the first vs. second rak'ah. A significant dispute concerns sending blessings upon the Prophet in the first sitting: Abu Hanifa says sujud is required because it delays the standing, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree because there is no deficiency in blessing. A dream narrative supports Abu Hanifa's view. The passage concludes by returning to the earlier issue of ikhfa' on munfarid, clarifying that the author's preference is not to negate obligation on munfarid, but to reject estimation of amount in jahr/ikhfa'.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): A fundamental obligatory element of prayer; omission invalidates the prayer.
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligatory element that is not fard; omission requires compensation but does not invalidate prayer.
تأخير (ta'khir): Delaying a fard or wajib from its proper place, which necessitates sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on sending blessings upon the Prophet in the first sitting?
A) It always requires sujud.
B) Abu Hanifa says it requires sujud due to delay of standing.
C) The Sahibayn say it requires sujud.
D) No sujud is required at all.

Key Takeaway
Delaying a fard or wajib in prayer necessitates sujud al-sahw, a principle that applies even to virtuous acts that cause delay.

The Wajib of Not Delaying or Changing Fard/Wajib in Prayer
Principle and branches of sujud al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where sujud al-sahw is required for delaying a fard versus leaving a wajib, and apply the principle to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw compensates for delaying a fard or changing sequence; standing in a wajib place requires sujud for leaving the wajib.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq adds a key wajib: not delaying or changing the fard and wajib in prayer. It then illustrates branches: extra rukus, extra sajdas, sitting in standing (qiyam) and standing in sitting (qu'ud). Understanding whether the disruption touches a fard or a wajib is essential to know why sujud is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the additional wajib
Read the opening: there is a wajib to avoid delaying or changing the fard and wajib. This is the basis for the branches.
2
Categorize the examples
Two rukus or three sajdas in one rak'ah delay the fard (sajdah or qiyam). Sitting in qiyam or standing in qu'ud that is fard changes the sequence. Standing in a wajib place (first sitting) leaves the wajib.
3
Apply the talil (reason)
For extra movements, sujud is for delaying the fard. For wrong posture in a fard place, sujud is for changing the fard. For standing in a wajib place, sujud is for leaving the wajib, not delay.
4
Distinguish fard vs wajib in the branches
The passage explicitly restricts 'standing in place of sitting' to when that sitting is fard. If the sitting is wajib (first sitting), then standing earns sujud for leaving the wajib.
This distinction prevents confusion: not all posture errors are for delay.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب سجود السهو المصنف على هذه الواجبات في باب صفة الصلاة وبقي واجب آخر وهو عدم تأخير الفرض والواجب وعدم تغييرهما وعليه تفرع مسائل منها : لو ركع ركوعين أو سجد ثلاثاً في ركعة لزمه السجود لتأخير الفرض وهو السجود في الأول والقيام في الثاني، وكذا لو قعد في محل القيام أو قام في محل القعود المفروض وإنما قيدنا بالمفروض لأنه لو قام في محل الواجب فقد لزمه السجود لترك الواجب لا لتأخيره
The book of prayer, chapter of sujud al-sahw. The author based on these wajibat in the chapter on the description of prayer, and there remains another wajib: not delaying the fard and wajib and not changing them. From it branch issues, including: if he performs two rukus or three sajdas in one rak'ah, sujud becomes necessary for delaying the fard, which is sajdah in the first and qiyam in the second. Similarly, if he sits in the place of standing or stands in the place of sitting that is fard. And we restricted it to the fard because if he stands in the place of wajib, then sujud becomes necessary due to leaving the wajib, not due to delaying it.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw. The commentator adds a new wajib: not delaying or changing the fard and wajib. The first branch: performing two rukus or three sajdas in one rak'ah delays the fard (sajdah in first case, qiyam in second), so sujud al-sahw is required. Similarly, sitting in a place of standing or standing in a place of sitting that is fard requires sujud. If the place is wajib (like the first sitting), then standing there leaves the wajib, not delays it, so sujud is still required but for a different reason.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): A legal obligation of a level below fard, proven by a zanni dalil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person stands up in the first sitting (which is wajib) without performing tashahhud, why is sujud al-sahw required?
A) For delaying the qiyam
B) For delaying the tashahhud
C) For leaving the wajib
D) For changing the fard

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-sahw is wajib to compensate for either delaying a fard, changing a fard posture, or leaving a wajib, with the distinction based on whether the place is fard or wajib.

Reciting Quran in Ruku, Sujud, or Qa'dah: Sujud al-Sahw Required?
Ruling on sujud al-sahw for reciting in non-recitation postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting a verse in ruku, sujud, or qa'dah and explain the reason for sujud al-sahw, including the exception in qa'dah.

Core Idea
Reciting Quran in ruku/sujud/qawmah obligates sujud al-sahw due to delaying a rukn or wajib.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses an important nuance in prayer: when does recitation of Quran in non-recitation postures necessitate sujud al-sahw? The author examines two Hanafi views, provides the reasoning (talil), and gives preference. Understanding this ruling helps avoid common errors in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being ruled? Reciting a verse of Quran in ruku, sujud, or qawmah. The majority view (al-Muhit) says sujud al-sahw is wajib. Identify the ruling: wajib to perform sujud al-sahw.
Also applicable to qa'dah if recitation precedes tashahhud.
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The obligatory sujud al-sahw is due to delaying a rukn or wajib. Reciting a verse in a posture not designated for recitation causes a delay in the performance of that posture's elements. This delay is the cause (illah).
The talil is based on the principle that any unnecessary delay in prayer elements requires correction.
3
Note the exception in qa'dah
If the recitation occurs after beginning tashahhud, no sujud is required because the obligatory tashahhud was performed first—the recitation does not delay any wajib.
The order matters: tashahhud first, then recitation is permissible without penalty.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Bada'i' holds that reciting Quran in ruku or sujud does not require sujud al-sahw because it is considered praise (thana), and these postures are places of praise. This view is rejected by the author because the primary purpose is not praise but recitation.
The disagreement is within the Hanafi school itself, not with other madhhabs.
5
Arrive at the mufta bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the first view (sujud required) as the apparent (al-zahir) position. This is the relied-upon ruling for fatwa.
The principle of 'delay of a rukn or wajib' overrides the characterization as praise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا لو قرأ آية في الركوع أو السجود أو القومة فعليه السهو كما في الظهيرية وغيرها وعلله في المحيط بتأخير ركن أو واجب عليه، وكذا لو قرأها في القعود إن بدأ بالقراءة وإن بدأ بالتشهد ثم قرأها فلا سهو عليه كما في المحيط . وفي البدائع : لو قرأ القرآن في ركوعه أو في سجوده لا سهو عليه لأنه ثناء وهذه الأركان مواضع الثناء ا هـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه فالظاهر الأول
Similarly, if he recites a verse in ruku, or sujud, or qawmah, then sujud al-sahw is upon him, as in al-Zahiriyyah and others. And it is reasoned in al-Muhit by delaying a rukn or a wajib. Similarly, if he recites it in qa'dah: if he begins with recitation, then he must do sujud; if he begins with tashahhud then recites it, then no sujud is upon him, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Bada'i': if he recites the Quran in his ruku or in his sujud, there is no sujud upon him because it is praise, and these pillars are places of praise. (End quote). And it is not hidden what is in it, so the apparent is the first.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage discusses reciting Quran in non-recitation parts of prayer. The majority view (al-Muhit) requires sujud for delaying a rukn or wajib, except in qa'dah if tashahhud is recited first. Al-Bada'i' disagrees for ruku/sujud, considering it praise. The author prefers the first view due to the principle of delay.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): Praise; in this context, reciting Quran in ruku/sujud is considered an act of praise, not tilawah (recitation with the intent of worship as Quran).
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness; sujud al-sahw are two prostrations performed to correct errors in prayer.
ركوع (ruku): Bowing in prayer.
سجود (sujud): Prostration in prayer.
قومة (qawmah): Standing after ruku (i'tidal).
قعود (qu'ud): Sitting in prayer (for tashahhud).
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting posture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the ruling if a person recites a verse of Quran in ruku?
A) No sujud al-sahw is needed because it is praise.
B) Sujud al-sahw is required because it delays a rukn or wajib.
C) The prayer becomes invalid.
D) It is recommended to repeat the rakat.

Key Takeaway
Reciting Quran in ruku, sujud, or qawmah obligates sujud al-sahw because it delays a rukn or wajib; the exception is in qa'dah if tashahhud is recited first.
