Leaving Sunnah Acts in Prayer: No Sujud al-Sahw Required, and the Debate Over Tasmiyah
States the principle that omitting a sunnah does not require sujud al-sahw, and highlights the controversy over tasmiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sunnah, wajib, and fard in terms of omission consequences in prayer, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over whether tasmiyah is wajib.

Core Idea
Sujud al-sahw only compensates wajib omissions; sunnah omissions need no sujud, and tasmiyah is sunnah in the relied-upon Hanafi position.

In Hanafi fiqh, not every mistake in prayer triggers sujud al-sahw. The ruling depends on whether the omitted act is fard, wajib, or sunnah. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that leaving a sunnah does not require sujud, but then notes an internal Hanafi dispute: some later scholars argued that tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillah') is wajib, contrary to the established madhhab. Let's dissect the rule and the dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Ruling
Sujud al-sahw is wajib only when a wajib act is omitted or delayed. For sunnah omissions, no sujud is required. This is the foundational principle.
Sunnah acts are recommended; missing them does not break the prayer.
2
List the Sunnah Acts Mentioned
The passage enumerates several sunnah acts: thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, takbirs in ruku' and sujud, tasbihs, raising hands, Eid takbirs, amin, sami'a, hamd. Omission of any of these does not require sujud.
This list is not exhaustive; other sunnah acts exist.
3
Identify the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Tasmiyah
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., the commentator, al-Qunyah, Ibn Wahban) held that tasmiyah is wajib in every rak'ah, requiring sujud if omitted. The author of the commentary notes this contradicts the apparent madhhab.
This dispute is internal to the Hanafi school, involving later jurists.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that tasmiyah is sunnah, as found in the primary Hanafi texts (mutun, shuruh, fatawa). Hence, omitting tasmiyah does not require sujud al-sahw.
The minority view is considered weak and not operative for fatwa.
5
Contrast with Leaving a Fard
The passage concludes by noting that if a fard act is omitted, the prayer is invalidated entirely and cannot be fixed by sujud. Sujud al-sahw only helps for wajib omission or delay.
Fard omissions require repeating the prayer from the start.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الواجب لأنه لا يجب بترك سنة كالثناء والتعوذ والتسمية وتكبيرات الركوع والسجود وتسبيحاتها ورفع اليدين في تكبيرة الافتتاح وتكبيرات العيدين والتأمين والتسميع والتحميد. كذا في المحيط والخلاصة. وجزم الشارح بوجوب السجود بترك التسمية مصدراً به ثم قال : وقيل لا يجب. وكذا في المجتبي، وصرح في القنية بأن الصحيح وجوب التسمية في كل ركعة، وتبعه العلامة ابن وهبان في منظومته وكله مخالف لظاهر المذهب المذكور في المتون والشروح والفتاوي من أنها سنة لا واجب فلا يجب بتركها شيء. ولو ترك فرضاً فإنه لا ينجبر بالسجود بل تبطل الصلاة أصلاً.
The wajib (sujud) because it is not required by leaving a sunnah, such as thana', ta'awwudh, tasmiyah, takbirs of ruku' and sujud, their tasbihs, raising hands in takbirat al-ihram, takbirs of the two Eids, amin, sami'a, and hamd. Thus in al-Muhit and al-Khulasa. And the commentator asserted the obligation of sujud for leaving tasmiyah, stating it explicitly, then said: 'And it is said: Not obligatory.' Similarly in al-Mujtaba, and it was stated explicitly in al-Qunyah that the correct view is the obligation of tasmiyah in every rak'ah, and 'Allamah Ibn Wahban followed him in his versification. All of this contradicts the apparent madhhab mentioned in the matn, commentaries, and fatwas that it is sunnah, not wajib, so nothing is required for leaving it. And if one leaves a fard, it cannot be compensated by sujud; rather the prayer is invalidated entirely.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author begins by explaining what triggers sujud al-sahw: it is wajib (obligatory) for leaving a wajib, not for leaving a sunnah. He then lists several sunnah acts whose omission does not require sujud: thana' (opening supplication), ta'awwudh (seeking refuge), tasmiyah (basmalah), takbirs during ruku' and sujud, tasbihs in ruku' and sujud, raising hands in takbirat al-ihram, takbirs of Eid prayers, saying amin, sami'a (Allah hears), and hamd (praise). These are all sunnah acts. The passage then highlights a dispute: some Hanafi scholars, including the commentator (al-Sharh), hold that tasmiyah is wajib and leaving it requires sujud. However, the author asserts that this contradicts the apparent madhhab (zahir al-madhhab) found in the authoritative texts (mutun, shuruh, and fatawa), which state that tasmiyah is sunnah only. The relied-upon position is that no sujud is required for leaving it. Finally, the passage notes a contrasting ruling: if one leaves a fard (obligatory act), sujud al-sahw cannot compensate; the prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer, required when a wajib is omitted or delayed.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah' before recitation in prayer.
السنة (al-sunnah): Recommended acts in prayer; omission does not invalidate or require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following acts, if omitted in prayer, requires sujud al-sahw according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Reciting thana' (opening supplication)
B) Reciting tasmiyah (basmalah)
C) Reciting the Fatihah
D) Reciting tashahhud in the first sitting

Key Takeaway
Leaving a sunnah act in prayer does not require sujud al-sahw; tasmiyah is a sunnah, not a wajib, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Ruling on Leaving a Fard or Wajib in Prayer and Qada' of Missed Acts
Expansion of ruling on omission compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fard and wajib omissions in prayer and determine the correct compensation (qada' or sujud al-sahw) for each missed act, including the order of making up prostrations and the exception for ruku'.

Core Idea
In prayer, a forgotten fard invalidates; a forgotten wajib can be compensated by qada' or sujud al-sahw, but some acts (like ruku') cannot be made up.

The Hanafi school meticulously categorises acts in prayer. This passage from al-Bada'i' clarifies the crucial difference between leaving a fard and leaving a wajib, and provides detailed scenarios for when and how a missed act can be 'made up' (qada') within the same prayer. Understanding these rules ensures that your knowledge goes beyond 'sujud al-sahw' to precise juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Read the opening line: 'If one leaves a fard, it cannot be compensated by sujud; the prayer is invalidated. If one leaves a wajib, it does not invalidate but is deficient.' Note that this is the foundational rule.
Fard omission = batil; wajib omission = sahih but makruh, requiring compensation.
2
Apply the rule to physical acts (af'al)
Examine the four scenarios: missed prostration(s), missed ruku', missed both. The text explains when qada' is possible and when it is not. For prostration, qada' is possible at the end of the rak'ah; for ruku', it is not because it cannot be inserted later.
Qada' is only possible if the act can be performed in its proper sequence later.
3
Determine the order of qada' for multiple missed prostrations
If two prostrations are missed, make them up in the order they were missed—first the first then the second. The same order applies when a tilawah prostration and an obligatory prostration are missed from different rak'ahs.
Qada' follows the original sequence (ada').
4
Handle verbal omissions (adhkar)
If recitation is missed in the first two rak'ahs, it can be made up in the last two. For tashahhud, if missed in the last sitting and the person stands, they should return if they have not yet prostrated.
The rule differs for the first sitting (details later).
5
Synthesize the general principle
Summarise: omissions that are fard (like ruku') cannot be compensated; omissions that are wajib (like prostration) can be compensated if the act can be performed in its proper place later. If compensation is not possible, the prayer may be invalid or require repeating.
This principle guides the imam in rectifying mistakes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك فرضاً فإنه لا ينجبر بالسجود بل تبطل الصلاة أصلاً. وفي البدائع : وأما بيان أنَّ المتروك ساهياً هل يقضي أو لا فنقول : إنه يقضي إن أمكنه التدارك بالقضاء، سواء كان من الأفعال أو الأذكار . وإن لم يمكن فإن كان المتروك فرضاً فسدت، وإن كان واجباً لا تفسد ولكنه ينقص ويدخل في حد الكراهة ، فإذا ترك سجدة صلبية من ركعة قضاها في آخرها إذا تذكر ولا تلزمه إعادة ما بعدها، وإذا كانا سجدتين قضاهما ويبدأ بالأولى ثم بالثانية لأن القضاء على حسب الأداء، ولو كانت إحداهما سجدة تلاوة وتركها من الأولى والأخرى صلبية تركها من الثانية يراعى الترتيب أيضاً فيبدأ بالتلاوية عند عامة العلماء. ولو كان المتروك ركوعاً فلا يتصور فيه القضاء، وكذا إذا ترك سجدتين من ركعة لأنه لا يعتد بالسجود قبل الركوع لعدم مصادفته محله، فلو قرأ وسجد ولم يركع ثم قام فقرأ وركع وسجد فهذا قد صلى ركعة ولا يكون هذا الركوع قضاء عن الأول، وكذا لو قرأ وركع ولم يسجد ثم رفع رأسه فقرأ ولم يركع ثم سجد فهذا قد صلى ركعة ولا يكون هذا السجود قضاء عن الأول، وكذا إذا قرأ وركع ثم رفع رأسه وقرأ وركع وسجد وإنما صلى ركعة، والصحيح أن المعتبر الركوع الأول لكونه صادف محله فوقع الثاني مكرراً. وكذا إذا قرأ ولم يركع وسجد ثم قام فقرأ وركع ولم يسجد ثم قام فقرأ ولم يركع وسجد فإنما صلى ركعة، وأما الأذكار فإذا ترك القراءة في الأوليين قضاها في الأخريين، وقد تقدم حكم ترك الفاتحة أو السورة في الأوليين. وإذا ترك التشهد في القعدة الأخيرة ثم قام فتذكر عاد وتشهد إذا لم يقيد بالسجدة بخلافه في الأولى كما سيأتي مفصلاً.
And if one leaves a fard, it cannot be compensated by sujud; rather the prayer is invalidated entirely. And in al-Bada'i': As for the statement that the thing left forgetfully, whether it is made up (qada') or not, we say: He makes it up if he can catch up by qada', whether it is of actions or words. And if not possible, then if the left thing is a fard, the prayer is invalid; if it is a wajib, it does not invalidate but it is deficient and enters into the realm of dislike (karahah). So if he leaves one obligatory prostration (sajda salbiyya) of a rak'ah, he makes it up at its end if he remembers, and he is not required to repeat what came after it. If they are two prostrations, he makes them up, beginning with the first then the second because qada' is according to performance (ada'). Even if one of them is a tilawah prostration left from the first (rak'ah) and the other is an obligatory prostration left from the second, order is also observed; he begins with the tilawah prostration according to general scholars. And if the left thing is ruku', it is inconceivable to make it up; likewise if he leaves two prostrations of a rak'ah because prostration before ruku' is not valid as it does not occur in its place. So if he recites and prostrates without bowing, then stands and recites, bows and prostrates, he has prayed one rak'ah, and this bowing does not serve as qada' for the first. Similarly, if he recites and bows without prostrating, then raises his head, recites without bowing, then prostrates, he has prayed one rak'ah, and this prostration is not qada' for the first. Similarly, if he recites and bows, then raises his head and recites and bows and prostrates, he has only prayed one rak'ah; the correct view is that the first bowing is considered because it occurred in its place, so the second is redundant. Similarly, if he recites without bowing and prostrates, then stands and recites and bows without prostrating, then stands and recites without bowing and prostrates, he has only prayed one rak'ah. As for words, if he leaves recitation in the first two rak'ahs, he makes it up in the last two; the ruling on leaving al-Fatihah or a surah in the first two has preceded. And if he leaves tashahhud in the last sitting and then stands, he remembers and returns and recites tashahhud if he has not yet prostrated; contrary to the first sitting, as will come in detail.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage from al-Bada'i' provides detailed rules for what happens when an act is omitted in prayer forgetfully. It first distinguishes between fard and wajib: leaving a fard invalidates the prayer entirely; leaving a wajib does not invalidate but makes the prayer deficient and disliked, and requires compensation through sujud al-sahw or qada' (making up) where possible. For physical actions (af'al), qada' is only possible if the omitted action can be performed in its proper place later within the prayer. For example, if one omits a prostration in a rak'ah, it can be made up at the end of that rak'ah, and what came after it is not invalidated. If two prostrations are omitted, they are made up in order, beginning with the first. If a tilawah prostration is missed in the first rak'ah and an obligatory prostration in the second, order is observed and the tilawah prostration is made up first. However, if ruku' is omitted, it cannot be made up because prostration before ruku' is invalid, and any subsequent actions do not count as qada'. The passage gives several scenarios to illustrate that a rak'ah is considered valid only if its ruku' occurs first; otherwise, the entire sequence is counted as one rak'ah with the first valid ruku'. For verbal acts (adhkar), if recitation is omitted in the first two rak'ahs, it can be made up in the last two. The ruling on omitting al-Fatihah or a surah has been discussed previously. For tashahhud in the last sitting, if one stands and then remembers before prostrating, he should return and recite tashahhud; this is different from the first sitting.

Key Terms
الفرض (al-fard): An obligatory act in prayer; omission invalidates the prayer and cannot be compensated by sujud al-sahw.
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligatory act in prayer established by zanni evidence; omission does not invalidate but requires sujud al-sahw or qada'.
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a missed act in prayer after its time, e.g., performing a missed prostration later in the same prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgetfully omits one prostration in a rak'ah, what should he do?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
B) He makes up the prostration at the end of that rak'ah and does not need to repeat what followed
C) He must repeat the entire rak'ah
D) He performs sujud al-sahw only

Key Takeaway
The distinction between fard and wajib omissions in prayer determines whether the prayer is invalid or can be compensated; ruku' is a fard that cannot be made up, while prostrations are wajib that can be made up in order.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Multiple Omissions and the Latecomer's Sujud al-Sahw
Ruling and proof for non-repetition of sujud and latecomer case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that multiple wajib omissions require only one sujud al-sahw and explain why the latecomer's qada' is legally a separate prayer requiring a second sujud if he forgets.

Core Idea
Multiple wajib omissions in one prayer require only one sujud al-sahw; the latecomer's qada' is legally a separate prayer.

This lesson unpacks two connected rulings about sujud al-sahw. First, if a person forgetfully omits more than one wajib act in the same prayer, he does not need multiple sujud — one sujud suffices. Second, a latecomer (masbuq) who follows the imam in sujud al-sahw may later err while completing his missed rak'ahs, requiring another sujud. At first glance this seems like repetition, but the Hanafi jurists explain that the latecomer's qada' is legally considered a separate prayer. We will examine the proofs and the intra-madhhab discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
The text states the fifth ruling: leaving multiple wajib acts (e.g., first tashahhud, takbir, etc.) does not multiply the obligation of sujud al-sahw. Only one sujud (two prostrations) is required.
This is the mufta bihi position despite some contrary views.
2
Understand the Proof (Qiyas)
The reasoning is that sujud al-sahw is delayed from its cause (the forgetfulness). Since the law does not allow delaying rulings from their causes, multiple sujud would imply multiple delays, which is invalid. So the cause is one, and the remedy is one.
This is a qiyas jaliy based on the nature of legal causes.
3
Handle the Latecomer (Masbuq) Scenario
A latecomer follows the imam in sujud al-sahw. Later, while making up missed rak'ahs (qada'), if he forgets, he prostrates again. This seems to contradict the non-repetition rule, but the answer is that the latecomer's qada' is legally a separate prayer (hukman), even though the tahrimah is one.
The analogy of a resident following a traveler imam is used to illustrate.
4
Analyze the Intra-Madhhab Ikhtilaf
Al-Bada'i' and al-Dhakhirah may imply that repetition is possible, but the majority of Hanafi works (like Bahr al-Raiq itself) prefer the non-repetition view. The author explicitly states this is a tarjih.
The difference is methodological: the cause is one, so the effect is one.
5
Apply the Principle to a Complex Case
The passage includes a long example from 'Umdat al-Fatawa where tashahhud occurs ten times in one prayer scenario, but the principle is that each sujud addresses a specific deficiency. Earlier sujud do not cover later omissions.
This reinforces that repetition is only apparent, not real.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس أنه لا يتكرر الوجوب بترك أكثر من واجب حتى لو ترك جميع واجبات الصلاة وذكر عبارته ثم قال : وهذا ترجيح لخلاف ما في البدائع والذخيرة قوله: (وكله مخالف لظاهر المذهب) قال العلامة المقدسي قال شيخنا شيخ الإسلام السمديسي في شرح المختار: ليست بواجبة فقد حكى المحققون من الحنفية كالإمام أبي بكر الرازي والإمام أبي بكر الكاشاني وغيرها الخلاف بين أئمتنا في السنية لا في الوجوب . قال بعض المحققين والقول بوجوب البسملة ليس له أصل في الرواية وما نسب إلى أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى من أن الخلاف في الوجوب فهو من طغيان اليراع ومن نسب إليه القول بالوجوب فليس بمشهور الاختيار قوله : (الخامس أنه لا يتكرر) أي من الأحكام التي بينها المصنف كما أشار إليه المؤلف بقوله في صدر القولة بيان لأحكام.

ساهياً فإنه لا يلزمه أكثر من سجدتين لأنه تأخر عن زمان العلة وهو وقت وقوع السهو مع أن الأحكام الشرعية لا تؤخر عن عللها، فعلم أنه لا يتكرر إذ الشرع لم يرد به، وسيأتي أن المسبوق يتابع إمامه في سجود السهو، ثم إذا قام إلى القضاء وسها فإنه يسجد ثانياً فقد تكرر سجود السهو وأجاب عنه في البدائع بأن التكرار في صلاة واحدة غير مشروع وهما صلاتان حكماً وإن كانت التحريمة واحدة لأن المسبوق فيما يقضي كالمنفرد، ونظيره المقيم إذا اقتدى بالمسافر فسها الإمام يتابعه المقيم في السهو وإن كان المقيم ربما يسهو في إتمام صلاته، وعلى تقدير السهو يسجد في أصح الروايتين لكن لما كان منفرداً في ذلك كان صلاتين حكماً ا هـ. وعلله في المحيط بأن السجدة المتقدمة لا ترفع النقصان المتأخر، فأما السجدة المتأخرة فإنها ترفع النقصان المتقدم، ولا يشكل عليه ما في عمدة الفتاوي للصدر الشهيد وخزانة الفقه لأبي الليث من أن التشهد يقع في صلاة واحدة عشر مرات وصورته : رجل أدرك الإمام في التشهد الأول من المغرب وتشهد معه ثم يتشهد معه في الثانية وكان على الإمام سهو فتشهد في الثالثة ثم ذكر الإمام أن عليه سجدة التلاوة فإنه يسجد معه ويتشهد معه الرابعة ثم يسجد للسهو ويتشهد معه الخامسة فإذا سلم الإمام فإنه يقوم إلى قضاء ما سبق به فيصلي ركعة ويتشهد السادسة، فإذا صلى ركعة أخرى يتشهد السابعة وكان قد سها فيما يقضي فيسجد ويتشهد الثامنة، ثم تذكر أنه قرأ آية السجدة في قضائه فإنه يسجد ويتشهد ثم يسجد للسهو ويتشهد للعاشرة ا هـ. مع أنه قد تكرر السجود للسهو في صلاة واحدة حقيقة وحكماً وهي صلاة الإمام والمسبوق بسبب السجدة الخامسة فيهما، وأما التشهد الرابع فلكونه بسبب سجود التلاوة ارتفع تشهد القعدة لا أن لسجود التلاوة تشهداً لأن سجود التلاوة رفع ما كان قبله من التشهد والقعود وسجود السهو فكأنه لم يسجد للسهو، فلذا يسجد آخراً كما لو سجد للسهو ثم نوى الإقامة حتى صار فرضه أربعاً فإنه يعيد سجود السهو. وفي الظهيرية : إذا سها الإمام ثم سها خليفته سجد الثاني سجدتين وكفاه .
Fifth: That the obligation (of sujud) does not recur by leaving more than one wajib, even if he leaves all the wajibat of the prayer. He mentioned his expression then said: 'And this is a preference contrary to what is in al-Bada'i' and al-Dhakhirah.' His saying: 'And all of it is contrary to the apparent madhhab.' Al-'Allamah al-Maqdisi said: Our shaykh, Shaykh al-Islam al-Samdisi, said in Sharh al-Mukhtar: 'They are not wajib.' The investigators among the Hanafis like Imam Abu Bakr al-Razi and Imam Abu Bakr al-Kashani and others have reported the ikhtilaf among our imams as being about sunniyyah, not wujub. Some investigators said: 'The statement that the basmalah is wajib has no basis in narration; what is attributed to Abu Hanifah that the ikhtilaf is about wujub is from the excess of the pen, and whoever attributes to him the statement of wujub is not of well-known choice.' His saying: 'Fifth: That it does not recur' i.e., among the rulings that the author clarified, as the author indicated by his saying at the beginning of the statement: 'An exposition of rulings.'

[PAGE_175]
... forgetfully, he is not obligated more than two prostrations because it is delayed from the time of the cause, which is the moment the forgetfulness occurred, even though Islamic rulings are not delayed from their causes. So it is understood that it does not recur, since the law did not come with it. And it will come that the latecomer follows his imam in sujud al-sahw. Then when he stands to make up (qada') and forgets, he prostrates a second time, thus sujud al-sahw has recurred. And al-Bada'i' answered this by saying repetition in one prayer is not legislated, but they are two prayers legally even though the tahrimah is one, because the latecomer in what he makes up is like a person praying alone. Its analogy is the resident who follows a traveler; if the imam forgets, the resident follows him in forgetfulness, even though the resident might forget in completing his prayer, and on the assumption of forgetfulness, he prostrates in the soundest of the two narrations. But because he is alone in that, it is two prayers legally. End quote. And al-Muhit explains it by saying the earlier prostration does not remove the later deficiency, while the later prostration removes the earlier deficiency. And it is not problematic what is in 'Umdat al-Fatawa by al-Sadr al-Shahid and Khizanat al-Fiqh by Abu al-Layth that tashahhud occurs in one prayer ten times. Its description: A man catches the imam in the first tashahhud of Maghrib and recites tashahhud with him, then recites tashahhud with him in the second, and the imam had forgetfulness so he recites tashahhud in the third, then the imam remembers that he has a tilawah prostration, so he prostrates with him and recites tashahhud a fourth time, then prostrates for sahf and recites tashahhud a fifth time. When the imam says salam, he stands to make up what he missed, prays one rak'ah and recites tashahhud a sixth time. Then when he prays another rak'ah, he recites tashahhud a seventh time, and he had forgetfulness in his qada' so he prostrates and recites tashahhud an eighth time. Then he remembers that he recited a verse of sajdah in his qada', so he prostrates and recites tashahhud (ninth), then prostrates for sahf and recites tashahhud a tenth time. End quote. Even though sujud al-sahw has recurred in one prayer both actually and legally, namely the prayer of the imam and the latecomer due to the fifth sitting? in both. As for the fourth tashahhud, because it was due to tilawah prostration, the tashahhud of the sitting is raised, not that tilawah prostration has a tashahhud, because tilawah prostration raised what came before it of tashahhud and sitting and sujud al-sahw, so it is as if he did not prostrate for sahw, therefore he prostrates later, just as if he prostrated for sahw and then intended to complete (iqamah) so his fard became four, he repeats sujud al-sahw. And in al-Zahiriyyah: If the imam forgets and then his substitute forgets, the second prostrates two prostrations and it suffices him.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage deals with two main issues. First, the fifth ruling: when multiple wajib acts are omitted in one prayer, only one sujud al-sahw (two prostrations) is required, not multiple. This is because the cause (forgetfulness) is one, and the remedy (sujud) is not repeated. This is the preferred view, contrary to what is stated in al-Bada'i' and al-Dhakhirah, which may imply repetition. The author then notes a related dispute about basmalah, confirming it is sunnah, not wajib, based on the majority of Hanafi investigators. Second, the passage discusses the case of a latecomer (masbuq) who follows the imam in sujud al-sahw. If the latecomer later stands to complete his missed rak'ahs and forgets, he may need to prostrate again. This seems to be a repetition of sujud in one prayer, but the answer is that the latecomer's prayer is considered two prayers legally (hukman) because in his qada' he is like a solitary worshipper. The analogy of a resident following a traveler imam is given. Al-Muhit provides a rationale: the first sujud does not remove later deficiencies; only the later sujud removes earlier ones. A long example from 'Umdat al-Fatawa illustrates multiple tashahhuds in one prayer scenario, clarifying that various sujud and tashahhuds occur due to different causes, each addressed separately, and the principle remains that the earlier sujud does not cover later omissions. Finally, al-Zahiriyyah states that if the imam forgets and his substitute also forgets, the substitute prostrates once.

Key Terms
المسبوق (al-masbuq): One who joins the congregation after the imam has started, missing one or more rak'ahs.
التكرار (al-takrar): Repetition of sujud al-sahw within what is legally considered one prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgetfully omits both the first tashahhud (wajib) and a takbir (wajib) in the same prayer, how many sujud al-sahw are required?
A) Four prostrations (two sujud for each omission)
B) Two prostrations (one sujud al-sahw)
C) One prostration
D) None, because the prayer is invalid

Key Takeaway
Multiple wajib omissions in one prayer require only one sujud al-sahw; the latecomer's qada' is legally a separate prayer so a later sujud is not a repetition in the same prayer.
